# 2026 California Gubernatorial Donor Intelligence Report

**Reporting date:** 2026-04-29 (Wednesday) — five weeks before the June 2, 2026 primary
**Compiled for:** Public political-donor intelligence database
**Sourcing tier definitions:**
- **Tier 1** = primary-source government filings (Cal-Access, FEC, IRS 990s, court records, FPPC enforcement docket). Cited inline without flag.
- **Tier 2** = secondary outlets (CalMatters, LAT, SFC, Politico, OpenSecrets, Ballotpedia, FollowTheMoney, TransparencyUSA, TheBallotBook, campaign press releases). Tagged inline as `[Tier 2 — needs primary verification]`.

---

## Important caveat on Cal-Access access

As of the compile date, **Cal-Access (https://cal-access.sos.ca.gov/) is robots-blocked from automated retrieval**, and the **Cal-Access NextGen replacement is partially deployed**. This affected every dossier in this report. Where direct Form 460 / 461 / 496 / 497 retrieval failed, this report relied on:
- Cal-Access aggregators (TheBallotBook, TransparencyUSA, cagovtracker)
- FPPC enforcement portal where it returned data
- Direct campaign press releases (always Tier 2)
- News reporting that quoted specific filings

**Per-candidate Cal-Access reliability** is documented in each dossier's `## DATA GAPS` subsection and consolidated in [data_gaps.md](data/data_gaps.md). In short: **direct itemized Schedule A donor pulls failed for every candidate**. Committee IDs, top-line totals, and many max-donor names were retrievable via aggregators. Granular date-stamped Schedule A line items, treasurer names on some committees, and most Form 496 (24-hour IE) data were not retrievable without manual paid-portal or in-person Sacramento retrieval.

---

## Active field as of 2026-04-29

**Democrats (active, on June 2 primary ballot):**
- Xavier Becerra — former US HHS Secretary, former CA AG
- Matt Mahan — Mayor of San Jose
- Katie Porter — former US Rep CA-47
- Tom Steyer — billionaire, former 2020 presidential candidate
- Tony Thurmond — Superintendent of Public Instruction
- Antonio Villaraigosa — former LA Mayor

**Republicans (active, on June 2 primary ballot):**
- Chad Bianco — Riverside County Sheriff
- Steve Hilton — political commentator, Trump-endorsed

**Suspended (still on ballot, included for protest-vote and donor-network tracing):**
- Eric Swalwell — suspended April 12, 2026; resigned House April 14, 2026

**Withdrawn before filing or running for other office (NOT dossiered):**
- Toni Atkins (withdrew Sept 2025; endorsed Steyer)
- Eleni Kounalakis (running for State Treasurer)
- Stephen Cloobeck (withdrew; initially endorsed Swalwell)
- Betty Yee (withdrew; remained on ballot; endorsed Steyer)
- Brian Dahle (did not file)
- Fiona Ma (running for Lt Governor)

Source: [CalMatters field summary](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/03/california-governor-candidates/); [Wikipedia 2026 CA gubernatorial election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_California_gubernatorial_election); [CBS California debate roster, Apr 28 2026](https://www.cbsnews.com/losangeles/live-updates/california-governor-primary-debate-2026/).

---

## Reading order

Each candidate gets one section. Dossiers are presented in alphabetical order by last name. The cross-cutting analysis follows. Data files (CSVs) are referenced in their own section at the end.

**Dossier sections per candidate** (Tier-1 candidates Porter, Becerra, Villaraigosa, Steyer, Hilton get full depth; Tier-2 candidates Thurmond, Mahan, Bianco get full depth on sections 1-7, 9-10, 12 and abbreviated on 8 and 11):
1. Campaign Committees
2. Top-Line Fundraising
3. Top Individual Donors
4. Top Institutional Donors
5. Independent Expenditures (for/against)
6. Donor Overlaps + Contradictions
7. Network + Relationships
8. Policy-for-Money Patterns
9. Dark Money + Shell Entities
10. Enforcement + Legal Exposure
11. Prior-Office Donor History
12. Story Angles

Swalwell receives a 1,500-word brief covering the suspended-campaign state.

---

## Headline finding

This is the most fragmented California gubernatorial primary in modern history. Eight major candidates split a Democratic field that has no clear front-runner, while Republicans Hilton (Trump-endorsed) and Bianco fight over a base that may well advance two GOP candidates to the November runoff. The donor signal in this report:

1. **Steyer self-funds at unprecedented scale** (~$144M raised, ~$132M spent — almost entirely his own money), drawing an equally unprecedented $21M+ in opposition IE money led by **PG&E ($9.975M)** — the real campaign-finance story of the cycle is utility-driven anti-Steyer spending, not Steyer's spending.
2. **Mahan's machine pre-positioned its dark-money vehicle 19 months before launch** (Back to Basics California 501(c)(4), incorporated March 2024), and is now the subject of an active FPPC coordination complaint.
3. **Tribal gaming, Laborers' Council, PORAC, and AltaMed cut max checks across the field** — they are the cycle's true "both-sides players."
4. **Cross-party billionaire hedging is documented**: Sergey Brin, Chris Larsen (Ripple), and Uber gave to candidates in both parties.
5. **Thurmond's union base abandoned him** — CTA, the union that powered his 2018 and 2022 wins, endorsed Steyer instead. He has $356K cash on hand and is burning 3x receipts.
6. **Bianco faces an active CA DOJ civil-rights investigation** of the Riverside County jail (19 deaths in 2022, $13M+ wrongful-death settlements) while running for governor on a "law and order" platform.
7. **Hilton's wife Rachel Whetstone** is Netflix Chief Communications Officer ($6.7M salary at last public reporting), creating a conflict-of-interest exposure for a CA governor's relationship with content/streaming regulation, AB-5 successor legislation, and CA Public Utilities Commission decisions affecting Hollywood broadband.
8. **Becerra received the first Chevron USA max contribution to a California gubernatorial candidate since Jerry Brown in 2014** — ending a decade of explicit oil-money distance from the Democratic gubernatorial line.

### Prior California State Committees (Cal-Access)
- **AG 2018 Re-Elect Committee**: Becerra raised $7,834,078 in the 2018 AG race per [OpenSecrets CA state data](https://www.opensecrets.org/members-of-congress/xavier-becerra/state-data?cycle=CAREER). Committee accessible via Cal-Access Power Search.
- **AG 2014 (Appointed)**: Appointed by Brown in Jan 2017; did not contest a 2014 election (Kamala Harris held the seat through 2016). Becerra's first AG election was 2018.
- **Leadership PAC**: "Leadership for Today & Tomorrow" — active during Becerra's House tenure, per [OpenSecrets 2016 profile](https://www.opensecrets.org/members-of-congress/xavier-becerra/industries?cycle=2016).
- **Dormant Account at Issue**: A dormant California campaign account (separate from the 2026 committee) was the vehicle for the $225,000 McCluskie-Williamson-Campbell theft scheme (see Section 10).

| Debt | Not disclosed in available filings | — |

**Burn rate flag**: CalMatters reported Becerra's campaign spent four times what it raised in the January–April 18 period — an unsustainable pre-surge pace. The $507K COH at April 18 is the lowest of any major Democratic candidate other than Thurmond. [Tier 2 — CalMatters]

**Post-Swalwell surge**: Campaign reported a 1,659% jump in online engagement and ~$400K in new donations in the days after Swalwell's exit. If verified against Cal-Access F497 filings, this represents a material change in trajectory. [Tier 2 — Scope Weekly]

### Industry Breakdown (Institutional Donors)
- **Organized Labor (Laborers' union family)**: At least $132,900+ across 3-4 Laborers PACs, with the CA State Council of Laborers alone at $54,700. The Laborers are Becerra's primary union endorser (see Section 7).
- **Tribal Gaming**: Pechanga ($44,600) + Agua Caliente ($41,900) = $86,500. Strong tribal presence consistent with his Latino-coalition-building; tribes have significant pending state regulatory relationships.
- **Healthcare**: AltaMed Health Services Corp ($39,200) — notably, AltaMed is both a top donor to Becerra AND simultaneously the single largest funder ($4.7M) of the "Protect Patients" ballot committee opposing SEIU-UHW's Proposition targeting FQHCs. This creates a complex policy-for-money dynamic (see Section 8).
- **Oil & Gas**: **Chevron USA Inc ($39,200)** — Chevron's first contribution to a California gubernatorial candidate since Jerry Brown in 2014, per [Rob Pyers/Twitter, June 25, 2025](https://x.com/rpyers/status/1937909986430198056). Progressive critics have amplified this contribution publicly ([Instagram/estherforcongress, Apr 27, 2026](https://www.instagram.com/reel/DXo_AuKDCCb/)).
- **Undisclosed entity**: "California's Best" — entity type and beneficial owners not confirmed in available data. Needs FPPC/Cal-Access F460 review.

### LLC Beneficial Owner Disclosure
- **South Cord Management LLC**: Listed as a recent contributor (Apr 27, 2026 per Ballot Book) but dollar amount and beneficial ownership not confirmed in available aggregated sources. Cal-Access F460 review required.
- **"California's Best"**: Entity identity unconfirmed. Could be a PAC, an LLC, or a committee. Requires primary-source verification.

## 5. INDEPENDENT EXPENDITURES FOR/AGAINST

### IE Support (For Becerra)
No confirmed large IE committee specifically supporting Becerra found in available sources as of April 29, 2026. The Laborers' union (CA State Council of Laborers) has endorsed Becerra and contributed directly, but no separate 496-filing IE committee identified in research.

**Note**: The [cagovtracker.com Becerra page](https://cagovtracker.com/candidates/xavier-becerra) references "outside spending by IE committees targeting this candidate" but no dollar amounts were populated in available view. This requires direct Cal-Access Form 496 lookup.

### IE Activity Against Other Candidates (Context)
The dominant IE play in the 2026 governor race is *against Steyer*, not directly touching Becerra:
- **"Californians for Resilient and Affordable Energy, No on Steyer for Governor 2026"**: Raised $10M+ from PG&E ($8M on Apr 10 + $1.975M on Apr 20) and IBEW Local 1245 ($75,000). Per [Energy and Policy Institute, Apr 29, 2026](https://energyandpolicy.org/becerra-150k-from-ca-utilities/).
- **Anti-Steyer committee funded by CA Realtors, construction, IBEW, and PG&E**: $14M+ spent on ads attacking Steyer's prior investments. Per [CalMatters, Apr 24, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-race-financials/).
- **Matt Mahan IE support**: ~$25M raised by two IE committees backed by Silicon Valley tech executives.

**Implication for Becerra**: No healthcare-industry IE play confirmed for Becerra. The PG&E/IBEW anti-Steyer spending indirectly benefits all non-Steyer candidates, including Becerra.

---

## 6. DONOR OVERLAPS + CONTRADICTIONS

### Cross-Candidate Giving
- **AltaMed Health Services Corp ($39,200 to Becerra)**: Also gave $39,200 to Eric Swalwell (per Transparency USA contributor page). AltaMed simultaneously donated $4.7M to the "Protect Patients" ballot committee opposing a SEIU-UHW measure targeting FQHCs. AltaMed's interests align with opposing healthcare worker unionization efforts — tension with Becerra's pro-labor platform.
- **Pechanga Band / Agua Caliente**: Both tribes actively lobby for gaming compacts and environmental exemptions. Governor has authority over tribal compact negotiations under state law. Direct financial conflict with future gubernatorial regulatory decisions.
- **Chevron USA ($39,200)**: Becerra's 2026 platform calls for clean energy and challenging utility monopoly pricing. Chevron's contribution creates optics conflict with his stated anti-corporate positioning and his opposition to a billionaire tax supported by progressive unions.

### Platform Contradiction: Chevron Donation
Progressive activists (led by Amar Shergill, former CA Democratic Party progressive caucus chair) are publicly highlighting the Chevron donation, per [Politico, Apr 27, 2026](https://www.politico.com/news/2026/04/27/xavier-becerra-progressive-backlash-00891871). Becerra's platform calls for lower utility bills and clean energy investment, yet Chevron's contribution — its first to a California gubernatorial candidate in over a decade — signals unusual corporate interest in his candidacy.

### Pending State Business Conflicts
- **CommonSpirit Health / Wife Carolina Reyes**: Dr. Reyes has served on CommonSpirit's Board of Trustees since September 2022. CommonSpirit is California's largest Catholic hospital system and faces federal sanctions from CMS at two Sacramento-area hospitals. Any gubernatorial administration's Medi-Cal contracting decisions, hospital licensing, and AG/regulatory actions directly affect CommonSpirit. California Government Code would require recusal from related decisions. Becerra has not addressed this publicly. ([California Globe, Apr 24, 2026](https://californiaglobe.com/fr/unforeseen-complications-can-becerras-family-connections-hurt-his-candidacy/)) [Tier 2 — needs legal review]

---

## 7. NETWORK + RELATIONSHIPS

### Labor
- **California State Council of Laborers**: Sole major labor endorsement to date; $54,700 contributed. The Labor Federation endorsed four candidates but *not* Becerra in March 2026. Per [KQED, Jan 16, 2026](https://www.kqed.org/news/12069984/who-will-labor-support-in-the-race-for-california-governor/) and [Politico CA Playbook, Mar 17, 2026](https://www.politico.com/newsletters/california-playbook/2026/03/17/you-get-an-endorsement-you-get-an-endorsement-00831121).
- **Missing Labor Endorsements**: California Labor Federation (AFL-CIO umbrella), SEIU, CNA, CTA — all withheld or gave to other candidates. This is a significant gap for a candidate claiming a pro-worker record.

### Latino Political Network
- **LCCC PAC** (Bi-Partisan Coalition of Municipal/County Latino Appointed and Elected Leaders): $39,200 contributor — represents a key Latino elected-officials network.
- Congressional Hispanic Caucus: Becerra served as CHC chair 1997-1999; his campaign relies on CHC-adjacent networks, though formal CHC endorsements for governor are not a standard vehicle.

### Former Staff Turned Lobbyists / Current Legal Issues
- **Sean McCluskie** (former chief of staff, 20 years): Pleaded guilty Oct/Nov 2025 to conspiracy to commit wire and bank fraud; stole $225,000 from Becerra's dormant campaign account. Agreed to repay $225,000. Maximum sentence 5 years. Per [PBS NewsHour, Nov 12, 2025](https://www.pbs.org/newshour/politics/former-newsom-aide-indicted-for-alleged-theft-of-campaign-funds-from-ex-health-secretary).
- **Alexis Podesta** (lobbyist): Unindicted co-conspirator in the McCluskie scheme. Podesta began billing Becerra's dormant campaign account in January 2023 for "consulting services" at Williamson's direction. Podesta remains active in Sacramento lobbying (still on SCIF board as of Dec 2025). Per [InsuranceNewsNet, Dec 3, 2025](https://insurancenewsnet.com/oarticle/unindicted-co-conspirator-stays-silent-after-fbi-arrests-but-still-on-scif-board).
- **Dana Williamson** (former Newsom chief of staff): Indicted on 23 counts including bank fraud, wire fraud, obstruction of justice, tax fraud; faces up to 20 years. Per [NBC News, Nov 12, 2025](https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/newsom-ex-chief-staff-accused-steal-campaign-funds-former-health-sec-rcna243569).
- **Greg Campbell** (Sacramento lobbyist): Co-conspirator, reached plea deal.

### Family Connections
- **Dr. Carolina Reyes** (wife): Harvard-trained maternal-fetal medicine specialist. Board of Trustees, CommonSpirit Health (since Sept 2022). Former board member, California Health Care Foundation (joined 2017, received $30,000 in 2018 FY per IRS filing). Former trustee, Catholic Health Association. **No evidence of family members on Becerra campaign payroll.** Per [Washington Free Beacon, Mar 11, 2021](https://freebeacon.com/biden-administration/becerras-wife-sat-on-board-of-non-profit-that-pushed-his-nomination/) and [Sacramento Bee, May 2023](https://www.sacbee.com/news/local/health-and-medicine/article274827976.html). [Tier 2 for Free Beacon]

---

## 8. POLICY-FOR-MONEY ANALYSIS

### HHS Secretary Actions (2021–2025) → Current Donors

**Medicare Drug Price Negotiations (IRA)**
- Becerra led HHS negotiations under the Inflation Reduction Act, securing discounts of 38–79% on 10 high-cost drugs (Eliquis, Jardiance, Xarelto, Januvia). These are effective in 2026 and save Medicare ~$6B/year. Per [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xavier_Becerra) and [NPR, Aug 2026](https://www.npr.org/2024/08/15/nx-s1-5075918/hhs-team-negotiated-with-drug-companies-to-save-on-medicare-drug-prices).
- **Pharma donor linkage in 2026 campaign**: No major pharmaceutical PAC contributions identified in the 2026 governor committee to date. The absence is notable — pharma was heavily present in his congressional career ($392,018 career total per [OpenSecrets career profile](https://www.opensecrets.org/members-of-congress/xavier-becerra/industries?cid=N00006117&cycle=CAREER)).

**ACA Defense and Medicaid Expansion**
- Becerra championed ACA expansion and secured Medicaid CHIP postpartum coverage expansion. Healthcare industry (hospitals, HMOs, insurers) that benefited is now represented in 2026 donors.
- **AltaMed ($39,200)**: Federally Qualified Health Center that benefited materially from Medicaid expansion. Also a major opponent of SEIU-UHW's Prop targeting FQHCs. Becerra's silence on the FQHC ballot measure is notable given AltaMed's dual role.
- **Leonard Schaeffer ($39,200)**: WellPoint/Anthem founder; health insurance expansion under ACA produced windfall for managed care companies.

**Unaccompanied Migrant Children / HHS ORR**
- NYT investigation found HHS released ~85,000 children it couldn't subsequently locate; career staff flagged concerns. Becerra pressed staff to accelerate placements. At a 2022 staff meeting, he compared the system to a "Henry Ford assembly line." Per [LA Times, Apr 27, 2026](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-04-27/becerras-surge-california-governor-race-draws-attention-to-candidacy-long-government-record).
- No donor linkage identified.

### California AG Actions (2017–2021) → Current Donors

**Sutter Health Antitrust — $575 Million Settlement (2019)**
- Becerra's AG office filed a major antitrust suit against Sutter Health. Settlement: $575M. Per [California Globe, Apr 24, 2026](https://californiaglobe.com/fr/unforeseen-complications-can-becerras-family-connections-hurt-his-candidacy/).
- **Conflict**: Becerra's wife, Dr. Carolina Reyes, was simultaneously employed as Regional Medical Director at Dignity Health (Sutter's competitor), which subsequently merged to form CommonSpirit Health in 2019. The AG sued Sutter while his wife worked in the competing system. No evidence of coordination, but the structural conflict is unaddressed.

**Opioid Settlements**
- McKinsey settlement (2021): $573M nationally; California received $59.6M. Per [CBS SF / CA AG press release, Feb 4, 2021](https://oag.ca.gov/news/press-releases/attorney-general-becerra-announces-573-million-nationwide-settlement-mckinsey).
- Additional pharma settlements: Royal/Seton Pharmaceuticals ($10.4M nationwide, 2021); Purdue Pharma investigation.
- **No direct donor linkage**: McKinsey, Purdue, and opioid-adjacent companies are not among identified 2026 governor donors.

**PG&E**
- Becerra received $28,500 from PG&E during his congressional career (1993–2017), per [Energy and Policy Institute, Apr 29, 2026](https://energyandpolicy.org/becerra-150k-from-ca-utilities/).
- **Zero PG&E contribution in 2026 governor race** — PG&E is instead spending $10M+ in IE against Steyer, per EPI.

**Utility Career History vs. 2026 Pattern**
| Source | PG&E | SoCal Edison | Sempra | Other Utilities | Utility Labor | Total |
|--------|------|-------------|--------|-----------------|---------------|-------|
| Congressional career | $28,500 | $62,700 | $62,000 | $38,000 | $0 | $191,200 |
| AG races | $0 | $7,800 | $7,800 | $0 | $42,600 | $58,200 |
| **2026 Governor** | **$0** | **$0** | **$0** | **$0** | **$0** | **$0** |
Source: [Energy and Policy Institute](https://energyandpolicy.org/becerra-150k-from-ca-utilities/)

The complete absence of utility money in 2026 — despite $249,400 in historical utility contributions — is a noteworthy discontinuity, possibly reflecting utility strategic neutrality given their IE spend against Steyer.

### House Votes — Health Industry (Congressional Record)
- Co-sponsored and voted for the ACA (2010); served on Ways and Means Committee with jurisdiction over Medicare/Medicaid.
- Health sector was his #2 career industry donor ($2,417,003 career via PACs, per [OpenSecrets career](https://www.opensecrets.org/members-of-congress/xavier-becerra/industries?cid=N00006117&cycle=CAREER)). Finance sector topped it at $2,625,961.
- 2016 cycle top industries: Health Professionals (#1, $143,649), Real Estate (#2, $133,325), Hospitals/Nursing Homes (#5, $95,805), Pharma (#11, $49,000). Per [OpenSecrets 2016 cycle](https://www.opensecrets.org/members-of-congress/xavier-becerra/industries?cycle=2016).
- Voted for Dodd-Frank (2010) while receiving $2.6M career from Finance, Insurance & Real Estate sector.

---

## 9. DARK MONEY + SHELL ENTITIES

### Undisclosed/Unclear Entities in 2026 Donor File
- **"California's Best"** ($39,200): Entity listed in Transparency USA contributor data. Type (LLC, PAC, 501(c)4) not confirmed. Beneficial owners unknown in available sources. Requires direct Cal-Access F460 review to identify principal officer and entity type.
- **South Cord Management LLC**: Appeared in Ballot Book as a late contributor (Apr 27, 2026). Amount not confirmed; beneficial owner unknown. No public corporate disclosure found in research. Requires CA Secretary of State entity registration lookup.
- **"BAK Festivals"**: Entertainment/events company; late contribution Apr 27, 2026. No amount confirmed. Beneficial owner unknown.

### 501(c)(4) Activity
No confirmed 501(c)(4) dark money operation supporting Becerra identified in research. When Becerra was CA AG, he publicly announced intent to pursue politically active nonprofits "abusing" their nonprofit status (2017), per [Inside Political Law, May 5, 2017](https://www.insidepoliticallaw.com/2017/05/05/california-ag-becerra-hints-crackdown-nonprofit-political-activity/).

### Straw Donor/Conduit Matter — Campaign Theft Scheme
The McCluskie theft scheme (see Sections 7 and 10) involved what amounted to a conduit arrangement: Williamson invoiced the dormant campaign account via her political consulting firm; funds were then transferred to McCluskie's spouse for fictitious work product; Alexis Podesta later billed the account directly for "consulting services." This is not a traditional straw donor arrangement — it was internal embezzlement — but it involved falsified records in campaign finance filings. Per [FPPC CalMatters, Mar 23, 2026](https://calmatters.org/newsletter/newsom-former-chief-of-staff-investigated/).

### FPPC Investigation
The FPPC is separately investigating Dana Williamson for her role in the Activision Blizzard lawsuit settlement (while she was Newsom's chief of staff) and connected financial conduct. The FPPC investigation intersects with the McCluskie scheme insofar as Williamson controlled Becerra's dormant campaign account. Per [CalMatters, Mar 23, 2026](https://calmatters.org/newsletter/newsom-former-chief-of-staff-investigated/).

---

## 10. ENFORCEMENT + LEGAL

### Federal — McCluskie Campaign Theft (U.S. Attorney, Eastern District of CA)
| Person | Status | Charges |
|--------|--------|---------|
| Sean McCluskie (former Becerra chief of staff) | **Pleaded guilty** — 1 count conspiracy to commit wire and bank fraud | Obligated to repay $225,000 to Becerra's campaign; max 5 years |
| Dana Williamson (former Newsom chief of staff) | **Indicted** — 23 counts; not guilty plea | Bank fraud, wire fraud, tax fraud, obstruction; max 20 years |
| Greg Campbell (Sacramento lobbyist) | **Plea deal reached** | — |
| Alexis Podesta (lobbyist) | **Unindicted co-conspirator** | Still active; SCIF board member |
Sources: [PBS NewsHour, Nov 12, 2025](https://www.pbs.org/newshour/politics/former-newsom-aide-indicted-for-alleged-theft-of-campaign-funds-from-ex-health-secretary); [InsuranceNewsNet, Dec 3, 2025](https://insurancenewsnet.com/oarticle/unindicted-co-conspirator-stays-silent-after-fbi-arrests-but-still-on-scif-board); [Sacramento Bee, Apr 8, 2026](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/capitol-alert/article315342965.html)

**Becerra not charged or implicated**. He describes it as a "gut punch" and says it occurred "outside of my vision." He cooperated with the FBI and federal prosecutors (investigation began under Biden DOJ). [LA Times, Apr 27, 2026](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-04-27/becerras-surge-california-governor-race-draws-attention-to-candidacy-long-government-record)

### 2024 Pre-Campaign Finance Activity (Potential Hatch Act Issue)
In 2024, while still HHS Secretary, Becerra was reported to be paying $10,000/month from a dormant state campaign account for "account maintenance" — political experts called this "a very high cost." This occurred while he was reportedly exploring a governor's run, raising Hatch Act concerns. Per [Wikipedia/Politico reference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xavier_Becerra). No formal OSC or FPPC enforcement action confirmed on this specific matter.

### Hatch Act Violations (Confirmed)
1. **OSC Finding, April 18, 2023**: Becerra violated the Hatch Act by endorsing Sen. Alex Padilla's reelection while speaking in his official HHS Secretary capacity at the Congressional Hispanic Caucus Institute Annual Awards Gala (Sept 15, 2022). OSC transmitted report to President Biden. Becerra acknowledged the violation as "unintentional." No termination or disciplinary action; a formal reprimand on the record. Per [U.S. Office of Special Counsel, Apr 18, 2023](https://www.osc.gov/news/2023-04-18/osc-issues-report-to-the-president-finding-hhs-secretary-xavier-becerra-violated-the-hatch-act/).

2. **FACT Complaint, October 28, 2024**: Ethics watchdog FACT filed complaint alleging Becerra violated the Hatch Act by sending a political email ("sales pitch for Kamala Harris") using HHS government data servers to ~67.5 million Medicare recipients. Per [FACT, Oct 28, 2024](https://www.factdc.org/post/ethics-watchdog-files-hatch-act-complaint-against-hhssecretary-xavier-becerra). No confirmed OSC finding as of research date.

### FPPC Actions Against Becerra Directly
No FPPC enforcement actions against Becerra personally identified in available research. The FPPC enforcement database ([fppc.ca.gov/enforcement.html](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/enforcement.html)) was not directly retrievable in research; direct review recommended.

### FEC — No Current Active Matters
FEC records show H2CA30143 with minimal activity (wind-down receipts/disbursements). No open FEC enforcement matters identified.

| Realtors | CA Association of Realtors maxed in 2018 AG → not visible in 2026 governor donors yet |

---

## 12. CONTEXT + STORY ANGLES

### Angle 1: The Dormant Account and Its Gatekeepers
The $225,000 theft from Becerra's dormant campaign account involved three Sacramento power brokers — his own chief of staff of 20 years (McCluskie), Newsom's chief of staff (Williamson), and lobbyist Alexis Podesta — who quietly controlled the account while Becerra was in Washington running HHS. Podesta remains an unindicted co-conspirator active in Sacramento lobbying. The scheme raises a fundamental governance question: if Becerra did not know who was controlling a campaign account bearing his name, what does that say about his administrative oversight of a $1.7 trillion federal agency? The contrast between his HHS record and this story is a direct line from critics.

**Primary sources**: [PBS NewsHour, Nov 12, 2025](https://www.pbs.org/newshour/politics/former-newsom-aide-indicted-for-alleged-theft-of-campaign-funds-from-ex-health-secretary); [Sacramento Bee, Apr 8, 2026](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/capitol-alert/article315342965.html); [CalMatters FPPC investigation, Mar 23, 2026](https://calmatters.org/newsletter/newsom-former-chief-of-staff-investigated/)

### Angle 2: The CommonSpirit Conflict — A Governor's Spouse on the Board of a Federally Sanctioned Hospital Chain
Dr. Carolina Reyes sits on the Board of Trustees of CommonSpirit Health — the nation's third-largest hospital system — which faces active federal sanctions from CMS at two Sacramento-area hospitals (Mercy San Juan, Mercy General). A California governor would oversee Medi-Cal contracting, hospital licensing, and could direct the AG office. Becerra's prior AG office sued CommonSpirit's main California competitor (Sutter) during the period when his wife worked for Dignity Health (now CommonSpirit). He has not addressed how he would handle recusals. California Government Code § 87100 requires recusal from decisions where a public official has a financial interest. [California Globe, Apr 24, 2026](https://californiaglobe.com/fr/unforeseen-complications-can-becerras-family-connections-hurt-his-candidacy/) [Tier 2 — needs legal/ethics counsel review]

### Angle 3: The Chevron Check — Can a "Healthcare Governor" Take Big Oil Money?
Chevron's $39,200 contribution to Becerra's governor committee is its first to any California gubernatorial candidate since Jerry Brown in 2014 — twelve years ago, before the state's climate agenda became a top-tier political issue. Becerra simultaneously pledges to lower utility bills, fight price gouging, and promote clean energy. His healthcare-focused platform ("California's Health Care Governor") and labor coalition are already strained by the California Labor Federation's refusal to endorse him. The Chevron check and progressive backlash ([Politico, Apr 27, 2026](https://www.politico.com/news/2026/04/27/xavier-becerra-progressive-backlash-00891871)) are a ready-made story about whether Becerra's sudden financial desperation (4x burn rate) is forcing ideological compromise in the fundraising operation run by seasoned DCCC-affiliated consultants (Kyle Layman, Elizabeth Ta, David Pruitt) whose institutional instinct is to take available money.

Raises conflict-of-interest questions given Bianco's simultaneous candidacy ([Riverside County News Facebook post, Nov. 2025](https://www.facebook.com/rivconews/posts/as-sheriff-biancos-public-profile-widens-residents-examine-overlapping-roles-and/1444314751029715/)).

| 20 | **Richard Lawson** | $20,000 | IND | Gave Dec. 22, 2025; identity not confirmed in available data |
| 21 | **Rick Hartsock** | $39,270 (combined) | IND | Two contributions: $19,600 (Apr. 4, 2025) + $19,670 ([page 2](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/candidate/chad-bianco/contributors?page=3)) |
| 22 | **Jaclyn Hartsock** | $39,200 | IND | Two contributions: $19,600 (Apr. 4, 2025) + additional; likely spouse of Rick Hartsock — donor couple giving combined ~$78,470 |
| 23 | **Chad Bianco (self)** | $10,000 | ENTITY | Candidate contribution to own campaign |
| 24 | **David McFarland** | $18,318 | IND | Identity unconfirmed |
| 25 | **Jessica Tovali** | $17,000 | IND | Identity unconfirmed |

**Pattern analysis:**
- **Inland Empire real estate and construction** dominates large-dollar individual/entity donors (Highland Fairview, Haagen, Walker Evans, West Coast Drywall, Alliance Building Solutions, rj Noble). This sector has significant permitting and contract interests regulated under a governor's office.
- **Law enforcement PACs** (PORAC PAC, Santa Barbara DSA, San Diego DSA) provide maximum or near-maximum institutional contributions — a pattern inherited from Bianco's 2018 sheriff race.
- **Corona-connected energy/real estate siblings** (Downs Energy + M&D Development) represent the campaign's live FPPC compliance risk.
- **No tribal gaming donors** identified in the top 25 (Pechanga, Soboba, Morongo not visible in available extracts) — notable given Riverside County's major tribal interests. Could be present in itemized filings not fully extracted.

**Observations:**
- **No tribal gaming contributions** identified among top institutional donors despite Pechanga Band, Soboba Band of Luiseño Indians, and Morongo Band of Mission Indians all operating in Riverside County — a significant gap in what would otherwise be a natural donor constituency for a Riverside-based candidate. Tribes may be hedging with Democratic candidates.
- **Bail bond industry** (Bail Hotline) is a live conflict: bail bondsmen have a direct financial interest in Bianco's policy positions on pre-trial detention.
- **Moving California Forward / Sen. Portantino** transfer is the most anomalous item — a Democratic-adjacent ballot measure committee transferring $11,500 to a Republican gubernatorial candidate. Warrants FPPC records review for context.

## 5. INDEPENDENT EXPENDITURES

**Status note:** Cal-Access Form 496 data was not fully accessible during research (robots-blocked). The following is sourced from secondary reports and partial data. [Tier 2 — needs primary Cal-Access verification]

### Pro-Bianco IE
- **RSA (Riverside Sheriffs' Association PAC):** Endorsed Bianco April 15, 2026 ([Instagram](https://www.instagram.com/p/DXKNAgaFNpA/)). In the 2018 sheriff race, RSA channeled ~$575,000+ to Bianco's campaign directly ([Idyllwild Town Crier, Apr. 2018](https://idyllwildtowncrier.com/2018/04/04/sheriffs-association-funding-bianco-campaign/)). For the 2026 governor's race, independent expenditure totals from RSA have not been confirmed in available public data — RSA's political action infrastructure (distinct from the nonprofit 501(c)(5) entity) is described as aggressive on its own website ([rcdsa.org](https://www.rcdsa.org/about/political-action)).
- **PORAC PAC:** Has the infrastructure to run IE campaigns. Endorsed Bianco Aug. 2025 and gave direct contributions. Governor-cycle IE amounts not confirmed separately.
- No law enforcement PAC governor-cycle Form 496 filings were confirmed in this research.

### Anti-Bianco IE
- **California AG Rob Bonta / Democratic Party infrastructure:** Not organized as IE spending, but Bonta's public legal confrontation with Bianco (ballot seizure lawsuit, civil rights investigation) functions as a political counterweight.
- **No confirmed anti-Bianco IE committees** identified in available data. Notably, the Trump-to-Hilton endorsement (Apr. 6, 2026) created conditions for future anti-Bianco IE from MAGA-aligned PACs, though none confirmed at time of research.

**Trump endorsement impact on IE landscape:** Trump endorsed Hilton on April 6, 2026 ([CBS Los Angeles](https://www.cbsnews.com/losangeles/news/president-trump-endorses-steve-hilton-california-governor-race-he-is-a-truly-fine-man/)). Bianco had been publicly Trump-aligned throughout his campaign. Trump's choice to back Hilton could redirect future IE money from MAGA-adjacent donors and national Republican infrastructure toward Hilton, leaving Bianco's IE support primarily in the hands of California law enforcement PACs.

---

## 6. DONOR OVERLAPS + CONTRADICTIONS

### Bianco vs. Hilton (Intra-GOP)
- Both candidates draw from CA Republican donor networks, but the overlap appears limited at the individual donor level. Ballot Book analysis of H1 2025 showed Bianco with a deeply regional donor base (84.3% from LA media market counties — primarily Riverside, San Bernardino, and adjacent areas), while Hilton drew broader state and national donors ([Ballot Book, Aug. 2025](https://theballotbook.com/blog/bianco-s-donor-base-in-the-la-media-market-could-signal-a-gop-edge)) [Tier 2].
- **Downs Energy** is described as "a frequent contributor to Republican candidates" in California ([SF Chronicle](https://www.sfchronicle.com/politics/article/contributions-bianco-violate-state-campaign-rules-22160676.php)) — likely also a Hilton donor, creating potential for aggregation issues at the donor portfolio level.
- **PORAC's dual endorsement** of Bianco and Villaraigosa (not Hilton) is a major signal: law enforcement's top statewide org deliberately left Hilton without institutional LE support.

### Law Enforcement Hedging
- PORAC endorsed Bianco (R) and Villaraigosa (D) simultaneously — a hedge ensuring LE influence regardless of outcome ([PORAC president's message, Aug. 2025](https://porac.org/article/presidents-message-porac-california-governor-endorsement/)).
- No Democratic law enforcement donors to Bianco identified, though the "Moving California Forward / Portantino" committee transfer merits investigation for any coordination.

### Bail Bond Industry
- Bail Hotline Bail Bonds ($10,384) has a direct financial stake in policies Bianco advocates — opposing bail reform, maintaining cash bail, toughening drug and crime penalties. This donor relationship creates an appearance of policy-for-money that is legally permissible but politically exploitable.

### Conflicts with Sheriff's Official Duties
- **Wellpath/CFMG jail medical contract:** Riverside County Board of Supervisors authorized Amendment 3 to the county's inmate medical services contract with California Forensic Medical Group (CFMG/Wellpath) in September 2025, extending it two years ([Citizen Portal](https://citizenportal.ai/articles/6460185/board-approves-twoyear-extension-of-jail-medical-contract-amendment-includes-calaim-justice-initiative-staffing-updates)). Wellpath/CFMG has not been identified as a Bianco campaign donor in available data, but the sheriff's department oversees jail conditions under this contract — a structural conflict worth monitoring.

---

## 7. NETWORK + RELATIONSHIPS

### Endorsers
**Law enforcement:**
- PORAC (CA's largest LE org, ~86,000 members) — August 21, 2025 ([PORAC](https://porac.org/wp-content/uploads/PORAC-2025-Gov-Endorsements_Press-Release.pdf))
- California State Sheriffs' Association (CSSA, all 58 CA sheriffs) — April 2026 ([California Courier](https://californiacourier.news/2026/04/chad-bianco-california-governor-sheriffs-endorsement/))
- RSA (Riverside Sheriffs' Association) — April 15, 2026 ([Instagram](https://www.instagram.com/p/DXKNAgaFNpA/))
- California Narcotic Officers' Association (CNOA), per Bob Cooke (CNOA President) endorsement ([biancoforgovernor.com](https://biancoforgovernor.com/endorsements/))
- Tom Ferrara (Solano County Sheriff), Tyson Pogue (Madera County Sheriff), Jim Fryhoff (Ventura County Sheriff) ([biancoforgovernor.com](https://biancoforgovernor.com/endorsements/))
- Deputy Sheriffs' Assn. of San Diego County and Santa Barbara County Deputy Sheriff Assn. (financial contributions)

**Elected officials:**
- Heath Flora (Assembly Republican Leader) ([biancoforgovernor.com](https://biancoforgovernor.com/endorsements/))
- California Republican Assembly (CRA) — supermajority endorsement, Apr. 9, 2026 ([CRA](https://cragop.org/2026/04/09/california-republican-assembly-endorses-sheriff-chad-bianco-for-governor/))
- Jason Ingram (Lassen County District 5 Supervisor) ([biancoforgovernor.com](https://biancoforgovernor.com/endorsements/))
- **Don Barnes (Orange County Sheriff)** — Wikipedia-noted endorser; not separately confirmed in primary sources here [Tier 2 — needs verification]
- **Curt Hagman (San Bernardino County Supervisor)** — Wikipedia-noted relationship; not separately confirmed in primary sources here [Tier 2 — needs verification]

**Trump did NOT endorse Bianco.** Trump endorsed Hilton on April 6, 2026 ([CBS Los Angeles](https://www.cbsnews.com/losangeles/news/president-trump-endorses-steve-hilton-california-governor-race-he-is-a-truly-fine-man/)) despite Bianco being a vocal Trump supporter and ally throughout his tenure.

### Religious/Political Network
- **Tim Thompson (Pastor, Sandals Church, Riverside):** Bianco's political ally. Thompson backed Jay Kiel for the bench in 2022 — Kiel later signed the warrants for Bianco's ballot seizure. Thompson's network supports Bianco's evangelical Christian identity politics ([CalMatters investigation, Apr. 2026](https://calmatters.org/investigation/2026/04/chad-bianco-emails/)).
- **Claremont Institute:** Bianco attended their "Constitutional Sheriffs" training; Institute gave him its "Sheriff of the Year" award (a John Wayne bust) at a Huntington Beach fundraiser ([CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/investigation/2026/04/chad-bianco-emails/)).
- **Constitutional Sheriffs and Peace Officers Association (CSPOA):** Bianco identifies as a "constitutional sheriff" and had documented contacts with CSPOA-affiliated figures who urged him to pursue election fraud investigations ([CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/investigation/2026/04/chad-bianco-emails/)).

### Family
- **Denise Bianco (wife):** Appears actively on campaign trail alongside husband ([Plumas Sun](https://plumassun.org/2026/02/14/riverside-sheriff-and-2026-gubernatorial-candidate-addresses-plumas-voters/), [Instagram](https://www.instagram.com/reel/DW8xtrlDs6u/)). Joint income of $590,000 in 2025 per tax returns filed with state ([CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/03/tax-returns-governor-candidates/)). No public evidence of Denise Bianco on the Sheriff's Department payroll was found. **DATA GAP:** Bianco's base salary was $348,000 in 2024 after a 27% pay raise (highest paid sheriff in state in 2023 at $593,000 total compensation). The pay raise itself — voted by the Board of Supervisors — warrants scrutiny of which supervisors are aligned with Bianco politically.
- No other relatives identified on the department payroll in available sources.

### Former Undersheriff Network
- Bianco displaced incumbents and allies of former Sheriff Stan Sniff upon taking office in 2019; rapid personnel changes alleged by whistleblower Captain Victoria Flores ([USA Today, Sep. 2025](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2025/09/19/sheriff-chad-bianco-governor-jail-deaths-lawsuit-whistleblower/86163786007/)).
- **Dave Brown (RSA Executive Director):** Former contender in 2018 sheriff race; ran against both Bianco and Sniff in primary (Brown received 19.5%); now runs the RSA as Executive Director (per RSA Form 990, 2023) — a notable reconciliation given the contentious 2018 race.

### RSA as Kingmaker
The RSA is both the primary institutional financial backer and the union representing sheriff's deputies directly under Bianco's command. This creates a structural asymmetry: the RSA endorsed Bianco for governor while simultaneously negotiating with him over working conditions, salaries, and contracts in his role as their employer. This relationship mirrors but exceeds the typical union-boss dynamic and deserves scrutiny as a potential conflict in both directions.

---

## 8. POLICY-FOR-MONEY (ABBREVIATED)

**Wellpath/CFMG jail health contract:** Riverside County extended its contract with California Forensic Medical Group (CFMG/Wellpath) for two years in September 2025 under Bianco's watch ([Citizen Portal](https://citizenportal.ai/articles/6460185/board-approves-twoyear-extension-of-jail-medical-contract-amendment-includes-calaim-justice-initiative-staffing-contacts)). Wellpath has been sued nationwide for inadequate jail medical care. The extension occurred while the CA DOJ civil rights investigation into RCSO jail conditions was ongoing (since Feb. 2023). No confirmed Wellpath campaign donations to Bianco.

**Bail industry donor:** Bail Hotline Bail Bonds ($10,384) has a direct financial interest in Bianco's advocacy against bail reform.

**CCPOA alignment:** Bianco has publicly aligned with re-opening prisons shut by Newsom — a position that aligns with CCPOA (correctional officers union) financial interests, though CCPOA has not been identified as a direct Bianco governor donor.

**Use-of-force and internal accountability:** Captain Flores' whistleblower lawsuit alleges Bianco fostered a culture where deputies filming excessive force were not disciplined, and internal affairs found no misconduct despite video evidence ([USA Today](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2025/09/19/sheriff-chad-bianco-governor-jail-deaths-lawsuit-whistleblower/)). Systemic under-accountability reduces operational costs in the short term but generates civil liability (>$13 million in settlements already).

---

## 9. DARK MONEY

### RSA's Layered Structure
The Riverside Sheriffs' Association operates as a 501(c)(5) labor organization (EIN 956203844, [ProPublica](https://projects.propublica.org/nonprofits/organizations/956203844)) with annual revenue of approximately $4.8M (FY 2023). It also operates a separate **RSA Political Action Committee** with its own Cal-Access registration, which is the vehicle for direct candidate contributions and, separately, independent expenditures. This two-entity structure — nonprofit + PAC — allows the RSA to use member dues infrastructure to generate political influence while the PAC handles disclosed electoral spending.

Key FY 2023 figures for RSA 501(c)(5) ([ProPublica](https://projects.propublica.org/nonprofits/organizations/956203844)):
- Program services revenue: $3.15M (65.3%)
- Other revenue: $1.58M (32.8%)
- Executive compensation: $564,844 (11.3% of expenses)
- Total assets: $5.82M
- **Political spending not separately broken out in 990** — 501(c)(5) organizations are not required to disclose political expenditures on Form 990 in the same manner as 501(c)(4)s.

The RSA PAC's IE spending for the governor's race has not appeared in confirmed Cal-Access Form 496 filings in available research. This is the primary dark-money vector to chase. The RSA's public website claims it "plays an active role in the political arena" ([rcdsa.org](https://www.rcdsa.org/about/political-action)).

### Riverside Sheriff's Charities, Inc.
A private nonprofit using the sheriff's official address and an RSO email address, with Bianco as President/Director, and RSO employees as officers ([Riverside County News Facebook, Nov. 2025](https://www.facebook.com/rivconews/posts/as-sheriff-biancos-public-profile-widens-residents-examine-overlapping-roles-and/1444314751029715/)). Fundraises through paid events featuring Bianco in his official capacity. IRS Form 990 not surfaced in this research. This entity sits in a gray zone: it is not a campaign committee, but it aggregates donor relationships in Bianco's official persona while he is simultaneously a gubernatorial candidate.

### LLC Donor Cluster
Multiple LLC and corporate entity donations (Highland Fairview Operating Co., M&D Development, West Coast Drywall, TW Networx, Global Processing Systems, West Coast C&C Management, Alliance Building Solutions) lack employer/occupation identifiers in available Cal-Access extracts. The ownership structures of these entities warrant deeper investigation to identify ultimate beneficial owners and potential pass-through dark money.

---

## 10. ENFORCEMENT + LEGAL

### FPPC Matters
- **Downs Energy / M&D Development aggregation investigation:** The FPPC is the relevant enforcement body. As of March 2026, the SF Chronicle reported the contributions "could run afoul of state rules." No formal FPPC complaint or enforcement action was confirmed in public sources at time of research. If aggregated, the $156,800 combined total would be approximately double the $78,400 limit, potentially triggering fines, mandatory refund, and amended filings ([SF Chronicle, Mar. 31, 2026](https://www.sfchronicle.com/politics/article/contributions-bianco-violate-state-campaign-rules-22160676.php); [Hoodline](https://hoodline.com/2026/03/bianco-s-twin-donor-dilemma-rattles-california-governor-s-race/)).
- **Legal defense fund opacity:** The Press-Enterprise reported in November 2025 that the purpose of Bianco's legal defense fund expenses "is not clearly detailed in the public documents" — a potential disclosure issue under FPPC rules ([Patch, Nov. 2025](https://patch.com/california/palmdesert/rivco-sheriff-whos-running-ca-governor-asks-financial-help-pay-his-lawyers)).
- No prior FPPC fines or enforcement actions against Bianco committees confirmed in available research. [DATA GAP — FPPC enforcement database was not directly queried due to access issues.]

### Civil Suits — Jail Deaths
- More than a dozen wrongful-death lawsuits filed by families of jail fatalities; **settlements exceeding $13 million** ([USA Today, Sep. 2025](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2025/09/19/sheriff-chad-bianco-governor-jail-deaths-lawsuit-whistleblower/86163786007/)).
- **19 in-custody deaths in 2022** — a two-decade high, more than double the average ([USA Today](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2025/09/19/sheriff-chad-bianco-governor-jail-deaths-lawsuit-whistleblower/86163786007/)).
- **Captain Victoria Flores v. Bianco / County of Riverside:** Filed July 2024. Flores — 30-year department veteran, former captain at Robert Presley Detention — alleges Bianco dismissed her in retaliation for refusing to cover up staff failures connected to inmate deaths; that she was directed not to speak with the civil grand jury; that a superior instructed her not to document an inmate overdose; and that Bianco condoned excessive force without discipline ([USA Today](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2025/09/19/sheriff-chad-bianco-governor-jail-deaths-lawsuit-whistleblower/86163786007/)). Case later sealed.
- **Alicia Upton wrongful death suit:** Bianco, the County, and Flores named as defendants in case arising from 2022 suicide of 21-year-old woman in county jail.
- **Federal jury verdict (Feb. 2026):** In the Solis case (Cois M. Byrd Detention Center, mentally ill detainee), a federal jury found no constitutional violations; Bianco testified and campaign touted the verdict ([Corrections1, Feb. 2026](https://www.corrections1.com/legal/jury-clears-calif-deputies-jail-staff-in-inmates-2022-death)).
- A deputy was convicted after being caught off-duty with 100 lbs. of fentanyl during an DEA investigation while assigned to courthouse transport duties ([USA Today](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2025/09/19/sheriff-chad-bianco-governor-jail-deaths-lawsuit-whistleblower/86163786007/)).

### DOJ / AG Civil Rights Investigation
- **California DOJ civil rights investigation** opened February 23, 2023, by AG Rob Bonta — examining "pattern or practice of unconstitutional policing," jail conditions, excessive force ([CA DOJ press release](https://oag.ca.gov/news/press-releases/attorney-general-bonta-launches-civil-rights-investigation-riverside-county); [LAT, Feb. 2023](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2023-02-23/riverside-sheriff-state-civil-rights-investigation)). **Still ongoing as of April 2026.**
- Bianco publicly dismissed the investigation as "a political stunt" ([LAT](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2023-02-23/riverside-sheriff-state-civil-rights-investigation)).

### Ballot Seizure Legal Battle
- March 2026: Bianco's office seized 1,500 boxes (~650,000 ballots) from the Riverside County Registrar related to the November 2025 Prop. 50 special election — the first such seizure in U.S. history ([CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/chad-bianco-election-warrants/); [NYT](https://www.nytimes.com/2026/04/08/us/politics/california-supreme-court-orders-sheriff-to-halt-election-investigation.html)).
- **California Supreme Court** ordered Bianco to pause the investigation and preserve all seized materials, April 8, 2026 ([NYT](https://www.nytimes.com/2026/04/08/us/politics/california-supreme-court-orders-sheriff-to-halt-election-investigation.html)).
- AG Bonta filed a lawsuit; AG's request for emergency stay denied by Court of Appeal in March ([Riverside Record, Mar. 2026](https://riversiderecord.org/riverside-county-bianco-election-investigation-bonta-lawsuit/)).
- Riverside County Board of Supervisors denied funding for Bianco's legal defense in the matter, 4–1 ([NBC Palm Springs, Apr. 2026](https://www.nbcpalmsprings.com/2026/04/14/riverside-county-denies-funding-for-sheriff-biancos-election-investigation)).
- The warrant judge, Jay Kiel, is the same judge Bianco endorsed in 2022 — now signing warrants in a case benefiting his endorser ([CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/investigation/2026/04/chad-bianco-emails/)).

### Cloobeck v. Bianco
- **CVRI2505068**, Riverside County Superior Court: Filed by gubernatorial candidate Stephen Cloobeck (D) alleging Bianco violated state law by campaigning in his sheriff's uniform ([ballot-access.org, Nov. 2025](https://ballot-access.org/2025/11/17/chad-bianco-sued-for-campaigning-in-sheriffs-uniform/)). Filed August 2025, served October 2025. Cloobeck subsequently suspended his own campaign and endorsed Swalwell, but the case remains pending.

---

## 11. PRIOR-OFFICE DONOR HISTORY (ABBREVIATED)

### 2018 Sheriff Race: The RSA-Funded Upset
Bianco ran as a lieutenant against 4-term incumbent Stan Sniff. The RSA was the decisive financial engine:
- RSA PAC gave approximately **$252,000** by January 2018, another **$300,000** by February, and approximately **$20,000** more by March 13 — a total of **~$575,000+** to Bianco's direct campaign (Cal-Access committee ID #1397860) by April 2018, before the June primary ([Idyllwild Town Crier, Apr. 2018](https://idyllwildtowncrier.com/2018/04/04/sheriffs-association-funding-bianco-campaign/)). Additional IE spending by RSA PAC for the general election was not separately quantified here.
- RSA Board recommended members contribute up to $99 individually to Bianco — keeping contributions below the $100 disclosure threshold to protect contributors from potential retaliation by then-Sheriff Sniff ([RSA All Points Bulletin 2018](https://rcdsa.org/images/assets/APB/PDFs/RCDSA_APB__2018.pdf)).
- Bianco won the general 58.3%–41.7% ([Ballotpedia](https://ballotpedia.org/Chad_Bianco)).

### 2022 Sheriff Race
Bianco won the June 2022 primary outright (60.7%) against Michael Lujan; the general election was canceled ([Ballotpedia](https://ballotpedia.org/Chad_Bianco)). He ran effectively unopposed, limiting the need for major fundraising.

### Continuity to Governor's Race
Of Bianco's 1,992 unique donors in H1 2025 for the governor's race, **96.2% were new donors** — only 73 donors (3.8%) overlapped with his prior sheriff campaigns ([Ballot Book, Aug. 2025](https://theballotbook.com/blog/bianco-s-donor-base-in-the-la-media-market-could-signal-a-gop-edge)) [Tier 2]. This suggests Bianco has successfully expanded his donor base beyond his law enforcement-union base, primarily into the Inland Empire construction/real estate and broader Republican donor networks.

---

## 12. CONTEXT + ANGLES

### Angle 1: Oath Keepers Affiliation — Membership Confirmed, Denouncement Absent
Bianco was confirmed as a dues-paying Oath Keepers member in 2014, revealed by a data leak from the organization's servers published by Distributed Denial of Secrets in late September 2021 ([LA Times, Oct. 7, 2021](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2021-10-07/riverside-county-sheriff-chad-bianco-was-a-member-of-the-oath-keepers-extremist-group)). He was a lieutenant at the time. Bianco acknowledged the membership but notably **declined to denounce the group**, stating: "Like many other law enforcement officers and veterans who were members, I learned the group did not offer me anything and so I did not continue membership." In his April 2026 KQED interview with Marisa Lagos, Bianco defended the Oath Keepers' stated mission ("law enforcement officials and military officials that swore an oath to defend our constitution against all enemies, foreign and domestic") and said the group was tainted only by "three people" arrested at January 6th ([KQED, Apr. 23, 2026](https://www.kqed.org/news/12081096/riverside-county-sheriff-chad-bianco-on-his-faith-cutting-taxes-and-ballot-seizure)). **Donor intelligence implication:** Bianco's refusal to denounce aligns with his broader "constitutional sheriff" ideology and attracts donors from the militia-adjacent, election-skeptic right — an ideological constituency without formal financial footprint but with mobilization value.

### Angle 2: Jail Deaths — 19 in 2022, $13M+ in Settlements, Ongoing DOJ Investigation
Riverside County jails recorded 19 in-custody deaths in 2022 — a two-decade high and more than double the annual average ([USA Today](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2025/09/19/sheriff-chad-bianco-governor-jail-deaths-lawsuit-whistleblower/)). Whistleblower Captain Victoria Flores (30-year veteran, fired 2024) alleges cover-ups, directions to obstruct the civil grand jury, and a culture of retaliatory silence. Settlements have exceeded $13 million. The California DOJ civil rights investigation, opened February 2023, remains open as Bianco campaigns for governor. The jail medical contractor — Wellpath/CFMG — had its contract extended two years in September 2025 while this investigation was ongoing. **Donor intelligence implication:** Bianco's campaign narrative frames him as a law-and-order executive — donors from the real estate, construction, and business community are betting on that brand. The jail deaths create a direct vulnerability: his record of managing one of the state's largest jail systems includes documented deaths, settlements, and an ongoing civil rights probe. For donors, the risk is reputational, not financial, but the DOJ investigation could produce formal findings before the June primary.

### Angle 3: Trump Endorsed Hilton — RSA as Bianco's Last Major IE Backstop
Trump's April 6, 2026 endorsement of Hilton ([CBS LA](https://www.cbsnews.com/losangeles/news/president-trump-endorses-steve-hilton-california-governor-race-he-is-a-truly-fine-man/)) cleaved the expected MAGA IE infrastructure from Bianco. Bianco had actively aligned with Trump throughout his tenure (anti-mandate enforcement, immigration, election denialism) and had anticipated Trump's backing. With national conservative PAC money now flowing to Hilton, Bianco's IE backstop narrows to California law enforcement PACs — primarily RSA, PORAC, CSSA, and county-level deputy sheriffs associations. The RSA is both his most reliable institutional ally and his most structurally conflicted one (he is simultaneously their employer). **The RSA as kingmaker dynamic is circular:** RSA's IE spending in 2018 created Bianco as sheriff; Bianco as sheriff governs RSA's members and contracts; RSA endorses Bianco for governor; if Bianco becomes governor, RSA's institutional reach extends statewide. This financial and institutional loop is the central political economy of the Bianco operation.

### Angle 4: Ballot Seizure — First in U.S. History, Mid-Campaign, Judge He Endorsed Signed the Warrant
Bianco's seizure of 650,000 Proposition 50 ballots from the Riverside County Registrar in February–March 2026 is constitutionally and legally unprecedented. The investigation was based on allegations from fringe election-denial groups with no confirmed evidence of fraud; Bianco's own investigator had closed a prior related probe in 2022 for lack of evidence ([CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/investigation/2026/04/chad-bianco-emails/)). The warrant was signed by Jay Kiel — a judge Bianco personally endorsed in 2022. The California Supreme Court ordered Bianco to halt and preserve the materials. The Riverside County Board of Supervisors denied his request for county legal funding, 4–1. AG Bonta filed suit. **Donor intelligence implication:** The ballot seizure has a polarizing effect on Bianco's donor base. Within Inland Empire Republican donor networks, it reinforces his "constitutional sheriff" brand. For moderate Republican and business community donors who need a governor who can govern, it is a competency liability. The issue has also shifted polls: post-seizure polling shows Bianco dropping and Hilton gaining, with Bianco at 10–14% in April 2026 depending on pollster ([Octagon AI](https://octagonai.co/markets/elections/us-elections/who-will-lead-the-next-qualifying-poll-in-the-california-governor-s-race/)).

---

## DATA GAPS

1. **Cal-Access primary source inaccessible:** Direct queries to `cal-access.sos.ca.gov` returned "disallow_by_robots" errors. All financial figures are sourced from Transparency USA [Tier 2] or press reporting. Primary Cal-Access Form 460 filings for Bianco for Governor 2026 (FPPC #1479095) were not directly verified. URL attempted: `https://cal-access.sos.ca.gov/Campaign/Committees/Detail.aspx?id=1479095&session=2025`

2. **Treasurer name:** Not identified in any public source accessed. Should appear on Form 460 filings.

3. **RSA PAC governor-cycle IE spending:** Form 496 filings for RSA PAC for the 2026 governor's race were not confirmed. RSA endorsed Bianco on April 15, 2026; any IE spending after that date may not yet appear in available databases.

4. **FPPC enforcement database:** Not directly queried at `fppc.ca.gov/enforcement.html` due to access constraints. No prior FPPC fines confirmed, but the Downs Energy/M&D Development aggregation issue is an active potential matter.

5. **Tribal gaming contributions:** Pechanga Band of Luiseño Indians, Soboba Band, Morongo Band of Mission Indians — all Riverside County tribes with significant political giving history — not identified in available Bianco filings. Could be present in Form 460 filings not fully extracted.

6. **Top employers of individual donors:** Not available in Transparency USA extracts for most contributors. Occupations/employers for Charles Wood, Keith Shook, Richard Lawson, Dan Stephenson, and others are unknown.

7. **Bianco for Sheriff 2022 committee ID and donor detail:** The 2022 committee was not directly queried. Cal-Access ID not confirmed.

8. **Riverside Sheriff's Charities IRS Form 990:** Not retrieved. EIN not confirmed. Amount of money raised and any political blurring with sheriff's official functions not quantifiable.

9. **Legal defense fund committee details:** Press-Enterprise reported on this in November 2025 but noted the filing's stated purpose was unclear. The specific FPPC committee ID and full donor list are not in available data.

10. **Post-March 2026 filings:** Campaign finance reports covering January–March 2026 would reflect the critical period of Bianco's ballot seizure controversy, Trump's endorsement of Hilton, and FPPC Downs Energy inquiry publicity. These Q1 2026 filings were not available in aggregated form at time of research.

**Context:** Hilton ranked third overall in total raised among all 2026 CA governor candidates as of April 2026, behind self-funding billionaire Tom Steyer ($133M+ personal contribution) and San Jose Mayor Matt Mahan ($13.9M). [SF Chronicle tracker, Apr 24, 2026](https://www.sfchronicle.com/projects/2026/ca-governor-campaign-finance/); [CalMatters, Apr 2, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-gop-candidates/)

The CA individual contribution limit for the 2025–26 gubernatorial cycle is $36,400 per election [Tier 2 — verify current FPPC limit at [FPPC.ca.gov](https://www.fppc.ca.gov)]. Multiple donors appear to have given exactly $39,200, suggesting possible dual-election contributions ($36,400 + a secondary election tranche, or the limit may have been adjusted — **primary verification required against current FPPC schedule**).

## 5. INDEPENDENT EXPENDITURES

### For Hilton
No confirmed IE committees running advertising specifically for Steve Hilton have been identified in Cal-Access Forms 496/461 as of April 29, 2026. The [CA Gov Tracker IE page](https://cagovtracker.com/independent-expenditures) shows no Hilton-specific IE spending. Despite Trump's endorsement (April 6, 2026), no Make America Great Again Inc. or allied Trump-aligned federal super PAC expenditure in the CA governor's race has been confirmed in available records.

### Against Hilton
No confirmed IE committees running anti-Hilton advertising identified in available records.

### Context
The race's massive IE spending has been concentrated on the Democratic side — particularly the Silicon Valley-backed IE committee supporting Matt Mahan (Super Bowl ad), and oil companies dropping $5M against Tom Steyer on Earth Day. [LA Times debate recap, Apr 22, 2026](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-04-22/as-primary-election-nears-top-candidates-for-california-governor-debate-tonight) Neither Republican candidate has attracted significant IE support or opposition as of the primary filing periods reviewed.

**DATA GAP:** Full Cal-Access Form 496 search for committees filing IEs targeting Hilton could not be completed due to Cal-Access robots.txt restrictions on direct programmatic access. Manual review of [Cal-Access Power Search](https://powersearch.sos.ca.gov/) is recommended.

## 6. DONOR OVERLAPS + CONTRADICTIONS

### Hilton–Bianco Intra-GOP Overlap
No confirmed donors identified as giving to both Hilton and Bianco simultaneously in available TransparencyUSA data. The two campaigns have distinct donor networks: Bianco draws heavily from law enforcement (Peace Officers Research Association of CA, police chiefs, sheriff's deputies' unions) and Central Valley business interests; Hilton draws from LA and Bay Area real estate, media, and tech. [CalMatters, Apr 2, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-gop-candidates/)

### Cross-Party / Hedge Donors
Three confirmed donors are simultaneously supporting Hilton (R) and Democratic candidates:

| Donor | Hilton (R) | Democrat | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Sergey Brin** | $39,200 | $39,200 → Matt Mahan | Wealth-tax opponent; left CA for Nevada. [Bloomberg, Mar 10, 2026](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-03-10/billionaire-brin-now-bets-on-a-republican-to-govern-california) [Tier 2] |
| **Chris Larsen** | $39,200 | $39,200 → Katie Porter | Explicitly wants Hilton-Porter November matchup; affordability focus. [Politico, Dec 17, 2025](https://www.politico.com/newsletters/california-playbook/2025/12/17/meet-the-crypto-billionaire-hedging-his-bets-for-governor-00694484) [Tier 2] |
| **Uber Technologies** | $39,200 | $2M → Swalwell; $150K → Porter | Classic corporate hedge; rideshare regulation exposure. [Washington Examiner, Mar 24, 2026](https://www.washingtonexaminer.com/news/campaigns/state/4502369/uber-campaign-donations-california-governor/) [Tier 2] |

### Chernick Network — Trump PAC Overlap
Aubrey and Joyce Chernick (both $39,200 to Hilton) are confirmed major donors to Make America Great Again Inc. (MAGA super PAC) and other pro-Trump organizations, as well as to RFK Jr.'s 2023 campaign. Their presence in Hilton's donor roll reinforces his Trump-aligned positioning post-endorsement. [Mother Jones, Oct 2023](https://www.motherjones.com/politics/2023/10/robert-kennedy-jr-aided-by-gop-and-trump-pac-donors-chernick/) [Tier 2]

### Real Estate Sector Concentration
Geoffrey Palmer, Frank Suryan Jr. (Lyon Living), and Steven Craig (Craig Realty Group) are all Southern California commercial/multifamily real estate executives, each maxed out at $39,200. Palmer is the pre-eminent Trump donor among them. Hilton's housing deregulation platform — opposition to CEQA, impact fees, Coastal Commission — directly aligns with real estate sector interests. [Real Deal, Feb 4, 2026](https://therealdeal.com/la/2026/02/04/geoff-palmer-donates-to-gop-governor-hopeful-steve-hilton/)

### Peter Thiel / David Sacks / Joe Lonsdale
No confirmed contribution from Peter Thiel, David Sacks, or Joe Lonsdale to Hilton's principal campaign committee has been identified in available filings. Thiel gave $3M to the California Business Roundtable IE opposing the billionaire wealth tax, but no governor's race contribution confirmed. [Local News Matters, Apr 3, 2026](https://localnewsmatters.org/2026/04/03/billionaire-blitz-silicon-valley-elites-funnel-millions-into-key-california-political-contests/) [Tier 2] DATA GAP.

[Tier 2 — further verification needed]
