### Rachel Whetstone — Conflict Flag ⚠️
Hilton's wife, **Rachel Whetstone**, is the Chief Communications Officer of **Netflix** as of 2024. Her 2024 compensation: $6.7M (representing ~89% of the household's $7.5M total 2024 income). [CalMatters, Mar 28, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/03/tax-returns-governor-candidates/)

**Prior roles:** Head of Communications at Google → Senior VP Policy & Communications at Uber → CCO at Netflix. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Hilton); [LA Times, Apr 6, 2026](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-04-06/president-trump-endoses-steve-hilton-in-california-governors-race)

**Conflict flags:**
- **Netflix:** CA governor directly regulates broadband, content taxation policy, and the entertainment industry (including whether to extend the film/TV tax credit that has been crucial to Netflix productions in CA). Whetstone's employer has material interest in CA regulatory outcomes.
- **Uber:** Whetstone's former employer; Uber gave $39,200 to Hilton's campaign — the intersection of a spousal employment history, corporate donation, and policy (rideshare regulation, AB5) warrants scrutiny.
- **Google:** Whetstone helped oversee Google's relationship with UK government while Hilton was Cameron's Director of Strategy 2010-12. They were in government/industry roles simultaneously.

Whetstone and Hilton live in **Atherton, CA** (San Mateo County) with two children. They were godparents to David Cameron's son Ivan, who died at age six. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Hilton)

### Former Crowdpac Staff
- **Gisel Kordestani** — COO and co-founder of Crowdpac; replaced Hilton as CEO after his departure. No current connection to Hilton's governor campaign confirmed.
- **Jesse Thomas** — Served as acting CEO during transition; authored the "Stand Against Trumpism" post. No current connection to Hilton's campaign.

---

## 8. POLICY-FOR-MONEY

### Crowdpac History and Departure
Hilton co-founded **Crowdpac** in 2013 with two partners described as a Stanford professor and a Google executive. [CalMatters, Apr 2, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-gop-candidates/) The platform obtained a favorable FEC Advisory Opinion (AO 2014-07) confirming its commercial fee model did not constitute political contributions.

In May 2018, acting CEO Jesse Thomas published "A Stand Against Trumpism, A Stand for Democracy," announcing Crowdpac would temporarily suspend Republican fundraising citing backlash from its user community against Hilton's Fox News profile and pro-Trump commentary. [Mediaite, May 15, 2018](https://www.mediaite.com/online/fox-news-steve-hilton-parting-ways-with-crowdpac-company-says-its-rejecting-trumpism/) Hilton resigned as CEO the same day. His departure tweet: *"Officially left my start-up @Crowdpac today. Proud of what the amazing team has built; loved working with you + so grateful to our investors."*

The departure was framed publicly as amicable, but the underlying dynamic — a founder whose political brand became incompatible with his company's liberal user base — provides Bianco with ongoing attack material. Bianco calls Hilton "a fraud" partly on the basis that Crowdpac "rebranded to exclusively support Democrats." [CalMatters, Apr 2, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-gop-candidates/)

Crowdpac later shut down and relaunched as a Democrats-only platform. No outstanding donor relationships from the Crowdpac era to the governor campaign have been identified.

**Crowdpac investor funding:** Described as having backing from "Silicon Valley venture capitalists." [Philadelphia Citizen, Oct 2015](https://thephiladelphiacitizen.org/lets-vote-the-democratizer/) Specific investor names beyond Hilton, co-founder Gisel Kordestani, and co-founder role of a Stanford professor were not confirmed in available primary sources. Sean Parker's investment in Crowdpac: Parker's Wikipedia page references his role as Executive Chairman of Brigade (a competing civic-tech platform) — no confirmed investment in Crowdpac found. **DATA GAP — Sean Parker / Crowdpac investor identity requires primary verification.**

### Golden Together 501(c)(4) — Policy Positioning
Founded **2023** by Hilton with co-founders/advisors including Lanhee Chen (Hoover Institution Fellow, former GOP State Controller candidate), Gloria Romero (now his Lt. Governor running mate), and an advisory board spanning conservative, libertarian, and Democratic policy figures. [Golden Together Advisory Board](https://goldentogether.com/advisory-board/)

**Stated mission:** Bipartisan California policy research on upward mobility, housing, economy, and public safety. Positions mirror Hilton's campaign platform: CEQA reform, housing deregulation, public school accountability, energy abundance.

**Notable advisors:** Kevin Faulconer (former San Diego mayor, former GOP governor candidate), Jeff Reisig (Yolo County DA, lead author of Prop 36), Connie Conway (former US Rep), Jennifer Hernandez (land use attorney), Joel Kotkin (Chapman University urbanist). [Golden Together Advisory Board](https://goldentogether.com/advisory-board/)

**Dark money / 501(c)(4) limitations:** Golden Together is organized as a 501(c)(4), meaning it is not required to disclose donors publicly. No IRS Form 990 for Golden Together was located on [ProPublica Nonprofit Explorer](https://projects.propublica.org/nonprofits/) as of April 29, 2026 — the organization may be too new to have filed or filings may not yet be processed. DATA GAP. Funders are effectively undisclosed.

### Fox News "The Next Revolution" — Tenure and Donor Network
Hilton hosted Fox News' *The Next Revolution with Steve Hilton* from approximately 2017 to 2023. His Fox tenure cemented his relationship with Rupert Murdoch (now a $39,200 Hilton donor). Fox News gave Hilton the platform that makes him recognizable to California's 6M+ Trump 2024 voters. No donor-specific relationships traceable specifically to the Fox tenure were identified beyond Murdoch.

### Trump Endorsement Timing — Donor Surge Analysis
Trump's endorsement arrived April 6, 2026 — one day after a Rancho Mirage debate moderated by Richard Grenell, and before the CA GOP convention (April 11–13). Fundraising reports filed April 27, 2026 (F497 24-hour reports) show two tranches — $55,292 from 102 transactions and $49,378 from 35 transactions — indicating active post-endorsement fundraising. [CATargetBot0001 / Cal-Access F497, Apr 27, 2026](https://x.com/CATargetBot0001/status/2048819682921332957)

The Chernick couple's donation presence, both being confirmed MAGA Inc. donors, is consistent with Trump-aligned donors reinforcing Hilton post-endorsement. However, their donations predate the endorsement (Chernick donations appear in early filing periods). A surge analysis comparing donor overlap with Trump PAC donor lists pre- vs. post-April 6 would require access to full Form 497 filings not available through web-accessible tools.

---

## 9. DARK MONEY + SHELL ENTITIES

### Golden Together — Primary Dark Money Vector
Golden Together is Hilton's primary dark money vehicle. As a 501(c)(4) "social welfare" organization:
- **Donor disclosure:** Not required.
- **Political activity:** May engage in issue advocacy (but cannot have political activity as primary purpose).
- **990 filing status:** No Form 990 found on ProPublica Nonprofit Explorer (DATA GAP — organization may be too new or may not have filed first 990 yet).
- **Known board/founders:** Steve Hilton (founder), Lanhee Chen (advisory), Gloria Romero (advisory/running mate), Kevin Faulconer (advisory). [Golden Together](https://goldentogether.com/advisory-board/)
- **Spending in CA:** Golden Together has operated primarily as a policy/research institution with public events and press releases. No documented electioneering activity from the organization has been confirmed in available public sources.

The conversion of a 501(c)(4) founder/executive to a gubernatorial candidate creates inherent tension regarding the organization's "primary purpose" test if it continues operations that benefit the campaign. No FPPC complaint regarding Golden Together and the Hilton campaign has been identified.

### LLC Contributions
No LLC contributions with potentially undisclosed beneficial owners have been identified in Hilton's campaign filings beyond Pacific Coast Companies Inc. (whose connection to Lucchetti is documented in public reporting). Cal Pacific Supply ($25,000) is an entity whose beneficial ownership is not confirmed. DATA GAP.

### Shell Entity Risk Assessment
Per SHARED_CONTEXT rules: No LLC speculation beyond documented facts. Available evidence does not support characterizing any identified contributor as a shell entity. Pacific Coast Companies Inc. is a legitimate operating entity with a publicly documented ownership structure.

---

## 10. ENFORCEMENT + LEGAL

### FPPC
A search of [FPPC enforcement decisions](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/enforcement.html) for 2025 and 2026 does not identify any enforcement actions against Hilton for Governor 2026, Steve Hilton personally, or Golden Together. No FPPC complaint against the Hilton campaign has been identified in available public records.

Hilton filed a legal action in September 2025 seeking an injunction to stop Proposition 50 (redistricting), a rare pre-candidacy legal maneuver; a court found he had not properly served the lawsuit. [YouTube / CA news, Sep 25, 2025](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=A8gE9bW4bjQ) This is a civil matter, not an FPPC/FEC enforcement action.

### FEC — Crowdpac Matter (MURs 7309 and 7399)
In January 2018 and June 2018, the FEC received complaints alleging that Crowdpac was operating as an unregistered political committee. The complaints specifically cited Crowdpac's suspension of Republican campaigns and its association with Hilton as a conservative political strategist creating the impression of partisan bias.

**Outcome:** The FEC found **no reason to believe** Crowdpac violated the Federal Election Campaign Act. The FEC determined Crowdpac continued to operate as a commercial service provider, not a political committee. Case closed June 3, 2019. [FEC MURs 7309/7399 Factual and Legal Analysis](https://www.fec.gov/files/legal/murs/7309/19044417414.pdf)

**Key finding:** The FEC concluded that Crowdpac's decision to suspend Republican candidates was a business decision driven by commercial interests (user backlash), not by partisan motivation constituting political committee activity.

### Crowdpac Ouster — No Litigation Identified
Hilton's departure from Crowdpac in May 2018 was publicly characterized as amicable. No litigation between Hilton and Crowdpac, or related to his departure, has been identified in available court records. Hilton's own tweet confirmed a friendly separation.

### UK-Side Disclosures
As Cameron's Director of Strategy (2010–2012), Hilton would have been subject to UK civil service and parliamentary disclosure norms, not US donor disclosure requirements. No UK regulatory or legal matter involving Hilton has been identified in available sources. He renounced UK citizenship upon becoming a US citizen in 2021 (his own public statement). No ongoing UK legal implications for US campaign purposes.

---

## 11. PRIOR ORGANIZATIONAL HISTORY
*(Replaces "Prior Elected Office" — Hilton has held no US elected office)*

### Crowdpac (2013–2018)
- **Role:** Co-founder and CEO
- **Co-founders:** A Stanford professor and a Google executive (identities not fully confirmed in available primary sources — DATA GAP). COO/co-founder Gisel Kordestani (former Google employee, formerly on Mercy Corps board).
- **Investors:** "Silicon Valley venture capitalists" per contemporary reporting; specific VC firms not publicly confirmed. Sean Parker — connection to Crowdpac not confirmed in primary sources (Parker's own Wikipedia page identifies him as Executive Chairman of Brigade, a competing platform). DATA GAP.
- **Business model:** Crowdfunding platform matching donors to candidates based on political alignment; obtained FEC Advisory Opinion AO 2014-07 confirming commercial fee structure.
- **FEC scrutiny:** MURs 7309/7399 — resolved in Crowdpac's favor, June 2019. [FEC](https://www.fec.gov/files/legal/murs/7309/19044417414.pdf)
- **Departure:** May 2018, concurrent with Crowdpac suspending Republican fundraising. Framed as amicable by Hilton; company CEO cited Hilton's Fox News profile as creating partisan association incompatible with user base.
- **Subsequent trajectory:** Crowdpac rebranded as Democrats-only ("Crowd Blue"); later shut down entirely.

### Golden Together (2023–present)
- **Type:** 501(c)(4) social welfare nonprofit
- **Founded:** 2023 by Steve Hilton
- **Co-founders/Senior Advisors:** Lanhee Chen, Gloria Romero (now Hilton's Lt. Governor running mate), Kevin Faulconer, Jeff Reisig, Jennifer Hernandez, Joel Kotkin, Pete Peterson (Pepperdine Dean), Connie Conway, and others. [Golden Together Advisory Board](https://goldentogether.com/advisory-board/)
- **Mission:** Bipartisan California policy research on housing, economy, public safety, education, upward mobility.
- **Funders:** Undisclosed (501(c)(4) not required to disclose). No Form 990 located on ProPublica as of April 29, 2026.
- **IRS status:** Active 501(c)(4) — verification of current tax-exempt status at [IRS Tax Exempt Organization Search](https://www.irs.gov/charities-non-profits/tax-exempt-organization-search) recommended.
- **2026 election nexus:** Gloria Romero's move from Golden Together advisory board to Hilton's Lt. Governor running mate creates a direct organizational-to-campaign pipeline. This raises 501(c)(4) coordination questions, though no FPPC complaint has been filed.

### UK Conservative Party Era (2010–2012)
- **Role:** Director of Strategy to Prime Minister David Cameron. Worked alongside James O'Shaughnessy (Baron O'Shaughnessy, Director of Number 10 Policy Unit).
- **Relationship with Cameron:** Hilton and Cameron were close personal friends; Hilton and wife Rachel Whetstone were godparents to Cameron's son Ivan.
- **Domestic UK positions:** Advocated severe civil service cuts, welfare reform; known as "barefoot revolutionary" for unconventional ideas. Satirized in BBC's *The Thick of It* as Stewart Pearson. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Hilton)
- **US donor implications:** None. UK political contributions operate under entirely separate legal framework.
- **Context:** Bianco attacks Hilton's UK environmental and socially liberal positions during this period (supporting climate action, same-sex marriage, higher minimum wage) as evidence of ideological inconsistency. [CalMatters, Apr 2, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-gop-candidates/)

### Fox News "The Next Revolution" (2017–2023)
- **Role:** Host, weekly Fox News show
- **Duration:** ~6 years, aligned with peak Trump era and Biden presidency
- **Relevance:** Built Hilton's name recognition among CA's 6M+ Trump 2024 voters; generated the relationship with Rupert Murdoch ($39,200 donor); created the partisan association that precipitated his Crowdpac departure; produced the network of conservative commentators and donors now supporting his campaign.
- **2024 income from Fox:** $250,000 (final year, per tax return). [CalMatters, Mar 28, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/03/tax-returns-governor-candidates/)

### Stanford Teaching
Hilton taught at Stanford University during his California years, described on the Golden Together site. No specific courses, dates, or compensation identified in available public sources.

---

## 12. CONTEXT + STORY ANGLES

### Angle 1: The Rachel Whetstone Conflict Architecture
Steve Hilton's household income is 89% derived from his wife Rachel Whetstone's $6.7M Netflix salary — making the family financially dependent on an employer that has enormous regulatory exposure to the governor's office. Netflix's California operations involve content production (subject to film tax credits), broadband policy, potential streaming regulations, and labor law (SAG-AFTRA agreements that the governor could influence). Uber — Whetstone's prior employer — gave $39,200 to Hilton's campaign at the same time Hilton is promising to deregulate California's business environment. The question of whether, as governor, Hilton would recuse himself from Netflix-related or Uber-related regulatory decisions is unanswered. This is not a legal violation — but it is a governance story. *Primary source for income: [CalMatters tax returns, Mar 28, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/03/tax-returns-governor-candidates/).*

### Angle 2: The Dark Money Backstop — Who Funds Golden Together?
Hilton spent two years (2023–2025) building Golden Together as a "bipartisan" 501(c)(4) policy infrastructure that, in retrospect, looks like a pre-campaign platform: it developed his California policy positions, built a bipartisan advisor network (providing political cover), and recruited his Lt. Governor running mate (Gloria Romero). Golden Together's funders remain completely undisclosed — 501(c)(4)s are not required to publicly report donors. The critical question: were major California business interests (real estate, energy, tech) quietly funding Hilton's political groundwork through Golden Together before he entered the race? This is the "dark money incubator" story. *The Form 990, when filed, will reveal revenues and expenses but not individual donor identities unless the 990-T schedule applies. ProPublica access attempt: no filing found as of April 29, 2026.*

### Angle 3: The Cross-Party Billionaire Primary — Brin, Larsen, and the Affordability Bloc
Sergey Brin ($39,200 to Hilton, $39,200 to Mahan) and Chris Larsen ($39,200 to Hilton, $39,200 to Porter) represent a new California political phenomenon: ultra-wealthy tech executives giving to both parties' candidates in the same race, explicitly as a hedge. Brin's motivation (blocking the CA billionaire wealth tax) and Larsen's (securing an affordability-focused general election regardless of partisan outcome) suggest the 2026 governor's race is being partially co-opted by a Silicon Valley affordability/tax-revolt bloc that is operating across partisan lines. Hilton — because of his deregulatory platform and media profile — has become their preferred Republican instrument. The story: is a faction of the tech billionaire class using the CA governor's race to reshape state fiscal policy, and does Hilton understand (or care) that he is a vehicle in this project? *Sources: [Bloomberg, Mar 10, 2026](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-03-10/billionaire-brin-now-bets-on-a-republican-to-govern-california); [Politico, Dec 17, 2025](https://www.politico.com/newsletters/california-playbook/2025/12/17/meet-the-crypto-billionaire-hedging-his-bets-for-governor-00694484); [LA Times, Apr 27, 2026](https://www.latimes.com/business/story/2026-04-27/google-co-founder-sergey-brin-confronted-gavin-newsom-then-launched-political-war).*

## 5. INDEPENDENT EXPENDITURES

### Supporting Mahan

#### California Back To Basics Supporting Matt Mahan For Governor 2026 (FPPC 1487425)

- **Legal form:** IE committee (can accept unlimited contributions)
- **Key expenditures:**
  - Super Bowl ad buy: $1.5 million (NBC/Peacock; Los Angeles, San Diego, Sacramento markets; Bay Area sold out). [San Jose Inside, Feb. 7, 2026](https://www.sanjoseinside.com/politics/bold-play-mahan-committee-drops-1-5-million-super-bowl-ad/)
  - $4.8 million on statewide TV ads (broadcast + cable), announced Feb. 26, 2026. [LA Times, Feb. 26, 2026](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-02-26/group-spends-4-8-million-on-tv-ads-for-matt-mahans-gubernatorial-bid/)
  - Total raised (per FPPC): top 10 donors = $13.6M; total reported COH $6.5M+
  - Total IE spending across both Mahan committees: **>$19.5 million** through April 18, 2026. [San Jose Inside, Apr. 25, 2026](https://www.sanjoseinside.com/politics/as-election-draws-closer-mahan-continues-to-lead-in-fundraising/)
- **Funder origins (one level up):** The committee is operationally descended from **Back to Basics California**, a 501(c)(4) incorporated March 25, 2024 — nearly 2 years before Mahan's campaign launched. Adrian Rafizadeh (now campaign manager) was CEO; Jim Reed (Mahan chief of staff) took operational control Dec. 2025. A San Francisco law firm is registered at its address. [San Jose Inside, Feb. 7, 2026](https://www.sanjoseinside.com/politics/bold-play-mahan-committee-drops-1-5-million-super-bowl-ad/)

#### Deliver for California – Matt Mahan for Governor 2026 (FPPC 1488716)

- Smaller committee; COH $49,000+ as of late April.
- Top donors: Sergey Brin ($1M), Paul Buchheit ($1M), Brian Singerman ($250K), Gary Filizetti ($240K). [FPPC](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/)

### Against Mahan

- No IE committee against Mahan reported at/above FPPC threshold as of filings through April 2026. Organized labor has focused anti-spending on Tom Steyer's opponents. [FPPC](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/)

**Jim Reed** is the connective tissue between the 2022 Liccardo/Mahan IE ecosystem and the 2026 Back to Basics 501(c)(4): he managed Common Good SV in 2022 and then took leave from Mahan's chief-of-staff role to run Back to Basics California in December 2025 — a full month before Mahan announced his candidacy. This is a structurally pre-planned operation.

## 6. DONOR OVERLAPS + CONTRADICTIONS

### Overlaps With Other Candidates

| Donor | Mahan | Steyer | Villaraigosa | Hilton | Notes |
|-------|-------|--------|--------------|--------|-------|
| Reid Hoffman | $39,200 | — | — | — | LinkedIn; moderate Dem hedge |
| John Doerr | $1M (IE) | — | — | — | Kleiner Perkins; also opposes billionaire tax |
| Ron Conway | (Brigade investor; no 2026 contribution confirmed) | — | — | — | Known SV kingmaker |
| Vinod Khosla | $1.1M (IE) | — | — | — | Khosla Ventures; staunchly anti-labor |
| William Oberndorf | $843K (IE) | — | — | — | School-choice advocate; Republican donor history |

### Key Contradictions

1. **Labor vs. Donor Base:** Mahan campaigns on "pragmatic" housing and safety policy, but his entire donor network — tech VCs, the Govern for California network, Kleiner Perkins, Khosla — is in open conflict with organized labor in Sacramento. The same IEs funding Mahan are funding anti-Steyer efforts in other cycles. [CalMatters, Jan. 31, 2025](https://calmatters.org/politics/2025/01/california-political-donors/)

2. **Billionaire Tax Contradiction:** Mahan positions himself as a champion of working families while his top donors (Brin, Moritz, Doerr, Khosla, Caruso, Collison) are united primarily by opposition to the proposed California billionaire wealth tax. [2026 California billionaire tax Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_California_billionaire_tax)

3. **Thiel-Linked Donors + Democratic Branding:** Lonsdale (Cicero Institute, a right-leaning think tank), Grimm (Mithril Capital, Anduril), and Fubini (Anduril investor) are publicly Thiel-adjacent. Mahan's brand is centrist Democrat, but this cluster creates an exploitable vulnerability. [Local News Matters, Feb. 14, 2026](https://localnewsmatters.org/2026/02/14/matt-mahan-billionaire-tech-donors-california-governor/)

4. **Cristo Rey School Grant:** Mahan's wife Silvia Scandar Mahan is president/CEO of Cristo Rey San José Jesuit High School. The school received an $862,000 city grant in June 2023 (3rd such grant since 2017; total $1.8M to school). Mahan recused himself; critics questioned outreach process. [San Jose Spotlight, Jun. 27, 2023](https://sanjosespotlight.com/school-run-by-san-jose-mayors-wife-scores-city-grant/)

5. **49ers Funded His Opponent:** The San Francisco 49ers (Jed York) gave $300,000 to a Cindy Chavez IE in the 2022 mayoral race. Mahan has since had a cooperative relationship with the team on ancillary matters, but there is no evidence of pro-Mahan 49ers money in the 2026 race. [San Jose Spotlight, Apr. 19, 2022](https://sanjosespotlight.com/san-francisco-49ers-nfl-football-team-break-the-bank-for-san-jose-mayoral-candidate-santa-clara-county-supervisor-cindy-chavez-election-2022/)

## 8. POLICY-FOR-MONEY (ABBREVIATED)

**Homelessness / Encampments:** Mahan's "Responsibility to Shelter" initiative (adopted June 2025, 9-2 council vote) makes homeless people who refuse three shelter offers eligible for trespassing arrest. [Arizona Daily Star/AP, Jun. 2025](https://tucson.com/news/nation-world/government-politics/article_26d8387b-c375-5218-b371-07ae8bad461e.html) His donor base — tech executives and real-estate interests — benefits materially from encampment clearance around commercial corridors. A new dedicated police unit was proposed to enforce the policy. [San Jose Spotlight, May 8, 2025](https://sanjosespotlight.com/san-jose-mayor-wants-new-police-unit-to-arrest-homeless-people/)

**Police Staffing:** Mahan negotiated a 39-month MOA with SJPOA in Sept. 2025, framing San Jose as "safest big city in the nation." [San Jose city press release, Sep. 4, 2025](https://www.sanjoseca.gov/Home/Components/News/News/6894/4699) In 2022, the SJPOA endorsed Chavez (his opponent), not Mahan; his relationship with the union has since normalized but produced no documented PAC money for the 2026 race.

**Tech Zoning / Housing:** Mahan has opposed blanket upzoning (opposed "Opportunity Housing"/four-plex plan) while advocating Smart Growth near transit — a pro-development-but-targeted stance appealing to both market-rate developers (Caruso, real estate donors) and tech employers wanting workforce housing near campuses. [sjmayormatt.com/meet-matt](https://www.sjmayormatt.com/meet-matt)

---

## 9. DARK MONEY

### Back to Basics California (501(c)(4))

- **Type:** Dark-money 501(c)(4); not required to disclose donors.
- **Incorporated:** March 25, 2024, at a San Francisco law firm address — nearly two years before Mahan announced his candidacy. [San Jose Inside, Feb. 7, 2026](https://www.sanjoseinside.com/politics/bold-play-mahan-committee-drops-1-5-million-super-bowl-ad/)
- **Domain registered:** March 15, 2024 (backtobasicssj.com — the "SJ" suffix suggests it was initially a San Jose mayoral tool, not a statewide vehicle).
- **Social accounts:** Established July 2024.
- **CEOs:** Adrian Rafizadeh (Nov. 2024) → Jim Reed (Dec. 2025 to present).
- **Function:** Acts as upstream feeder and organizational parent to the IE committee California Back to Basics (FPPC 1487425). The 501(c)(4) itself does not have to disclose donors; only when it contributes to the IE committee do donors appear in FPPC filings.
- **Significance:** This structure allowed Mahan's team to build infrastructure, brand, and donor relationships for two years before his official entry, without any public disclosure.

### Govern for California (16-Chapter Nonprofit Network)

- **Type:** 16 affiliated chapters, each independently directed (per FPPC 2020 advice letter). Chapters can coordinate fundraising without sharing contribution limits.
- **Function:** Contributed $1.5M to California Back to Basics via the "Govern for California Action Committee"; $300,000 directly to campaign. Top GfC donors: Nicholas Pritzker (Tao Capital), Kevin Kiley. [FPPC list](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/)
- **FPPC history:** FPPC investigated GfC for potential contribution-limit circumvention and closed without action in January 2025, validating its multi-chapter structure. [CalMatters, Jan. 31, 2025](https://calmatters.org/politics/2025/01/california-political-donors/)
- **David Crane** manages GfC and appears to be managing the $35M refund-guarantee fundraising strategy for Mahan. [NY Mag, Apr. 9, 2026](https://nymag.com/intelligencer/article/california-candidate-offers-donors-money-back-guarantee.html)

### Solutions Silicon Valley (501(c)(4)) — 2022 Legacy Vehicle

- Founded by Sam Liccardo in February 2021; shares address and infrastructure with Common Good SV PAC; managed by Jim Reed.
- In 2022, was listed as "major funder" on attack mailers against Mahan's opponent Cindy Chavez, via data-sharing relationship with California Realtors PAC.
- Not confirmed active in 2026 statewide race; Reed's departure to Back to Basics renders this vehicle potentially dormant. [San Jose Spotlight, Nov. 4, 2022](https://sanjosespotlight.com/san-jose-mayors-groups-linked-to-attack-ads-common-good-solutions-silicon-valley-political-action-committee-pac-election-2022/)

### Rick Caruso and Affiliated Entities

- Caruso's $1.5M IE contribution is listed as "Rick Caruso and Affiliated Entities" — the "Affiliated Entities" language signals LLC structures. Real estate developers routinely use LLC networks to give; the FPPC disclosure aggregates these but underlying LLC identities may require additional Form 460 review. [FPPC list](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/)

---

## 10. ENFORCEMENT + LEGAL

### FPPC Complaint – IE Coordination (April 2026)

- **Status:** Active complaint filed with the California Fair Political Practices Commission, reported April 21, 2026. [Mission Local via Instagram, Apr. 21, 2026](https://www.instagram.com/p/DXcvfLDkQgw/)
- **Allegation:** Mahan illegally discussed "campaign strategy and messaging" with leaders of California Back to Basics and its donors, constituting illegal coordination between a candidate and an IE committee.
- **Evidence submitted:** Screenshots of Zoom calls and emails sent to FPPC. An April 6, 2026 Zoom fundraising call allegedly included Michael Moritz and Rick Caruso (both top Back to Basics donors), with Mahan's consultant's strategy slides screen-shared.
- **Legal assessment:** Multiple attorneys cited in reporting said it was a "bad look, but probably not actually a violation." [Reddit/r/bayarea, Apr. 23, 2026](https://www.reddit.com/r/bayarea/comments/1sthbmf/ethics_complaint_alleges_promatt_mahan_pac/)
- **FPPC response:** No action announced as of April 29, 2026. FPPC enforcement timelines are typically months to years.

### Social Media / Ethics (February–March 2026)

- Mahan's practice of using personal social media for both city business and campaign promotion drew ethics criticism. After announcing his gubernatorial run Jan. 29, 2026, he launched separate city-backed accounts in February, but critics noted his personal accounts (which built following with city resources) continued to feature campaign content.
- Ethics expert Davina Hurt (SCU Ethics Center): "The cleaner and more defensible standard would be to create an entirely separate campaign site." [SCU Ethics/San Jose Spotlight, Mar. 2, 2026](https://www.scu.edu/ethics/media-mentions/stories/san-jose-mayors-social-media-use-faces-criticism.html)
- No formal FPPC complaint filed on this issue as of research date.

### Cristo Rey Grant (June 2023)

- $862,000 five-year city grant to Cristo Rey San José Jesuit High School (third such grant since 2017; total $1.8M). Mahan recused himself. Critics: two public school districts were not notified of the opportunity. [San Jose Spotlight, Jun. 27, 2023](https://sanjosespotlight.com/school-run-by-san-jose-mayors-wife-scores-city-grant/)
- No FPPC or Ethics Commission complaint confirmed filed.

### No Confirmed FPPC Prior Enforcement History

- A Reddit commenter noted "Weren't there fundraising ethics matters in his 2022 campaign?" but no confirmed FPPC case was found in research. [Reddit/r/SanJose, Apr. 26, 2026](https://www.reddit.com/r/SanJose/comments/1swg31d/ethics_complaint_alleges_promatt_mahan_pac/) The 2024 FPPC Enforcement Decision citations PDF does not include Mahan's name. [FPPC 2024 Appendix II PDF](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/siteassets/documents/legal_div/political_reform_act/2024/2024_Appendix_II.pdf) [Tier 2 — needs primary verification via FPPC case search]

## 11. PRIOR-OFFICE DONOR HISTORY (ABBREVIATED)

### San Jose City Council, District 10 (2020–2022)

- Won March 3, 2020 primary outright with 58.5%.
- Early endorsers: Mayor Liccardo, Assessor Larry Stone, SVO PAC (Silicon Valley Organization/Chamber), council members Lan Diep and Pam Foley. [San Jose Inside, Aug. 2019](https://www.sanjoseinside.com/news/svo-endorses-matt-mahan-for-san-joses-d10-city-council-race/)
- Council-level contribution limits: $700 (2022); Mahan was fundraising leader among D10 candidates.

### San Jose Mayor 2022

- Individual contributions: **$2,227,299** (vs. Chavez $1,660,080). [MapLight/Silicon Valley Rising PDF](https://siliconvalleyrising.org/wp-content/uploads/2024/02/San-Jose-Election-2022-Campaign-Finance-Report-MapLight-1.pdf)
- Local San Jose donors: 63% of individual contributions ($1,394,095); California out-of-city donors: 32% ($715,394).
- IE support: Common Good Silicon Valley (PAC, Jim Reed) ~$190,000 in texts; Realtors PAC (data-sharing relationship); Silicon Valley Biz PAC.
- Opposition IE: 49ers (Jed York/DeBartolo Corp.) gave **$300,000** to Cindy Chavez IE. [San Jose Inside, Apr. 19, 2022](https://www.sanjoseinside.com/news/most-of-49ers-money-for-chavez-is-spent-future-aid-uncertain/)
- Mayoral limit: $1,400 per donor.

### Pre-Political Tech Career — Donor Network Origins

- **Causes (2008–2014):** Co-founded with Sean Parker and Joe Green as Facebook civic app. Became CEO/President 2013. Parker, Conway, and Benioff invested in the successor company Brigade. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matt_Mahan)
- **Brigade (2014–2019):** Civic social network. Investors: Sean Parker, Ron Conway, Marc Benioff. Acquired by Pinterest 2019; technology sold to Countable. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matt_Mahan); [Causes.com shutdown, NonProfit Times, 2014](https://thenonprofittimes.com/npt_articles/causes-org-platform-sold-shutdown/)
- The Brigade investor network (Parker, Conway, Benioff) represents the oldest layer of Mahan's donor relationships, though their 2026 contributions are not confirmed in reviewed primary filings.
- **Teach for America / Alum Rock:** 2006–2008, teaching at Alum Rock Middle School, San Jose. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matt_Mahan)

---

## 12. CONTEXT + ANGLES

### Angle 1: The Pre-Positioned Dark-Money Machine — Two Years Before the Campaign

The most structurally significant finding in this dossier is the **19-month gap** between the March 2024 incorporation of Back to Basics California (501(c)(4)) and Mahan's January 29, 2026 campaign launch. The domain "backtobasicssj.com" was registered on March 15, 2024 — when Mahan was roughly 18 months into his first mayoral term. Jim Reed, Mahan's chief of staff, took leave in December 2025 to run the organization. Adrian Rafizadeh, the 501(c)(4)'s CEO, became Mahan's campaign manager at launch. By the time the campaign filed with the Secretary of State, Back to Basics had already raised over $3.2 million and reserved $1.4 million in airtime. This is not a candidate who recruited donors — it is a candidate whose donor infrastructure recruited him. The April 2026 FPPC coordination complaint, alleging that strategy slides were shared on an April 6 Zoom with Moritz and Caruso present, adds a legal dimension to this structural pre-planning story. **Journalist angle: Who directed the 2024 incorporation? Who paid the San Francisco law firm? Was Mahan himself involved in the organizational decisions before formally exploring a candidacy?**

### Angle 2: The $35M Refund Guarantee — A Conditional Billionaire Bet

The "money-back guarantee" fundraising structure — raise $35M by April 17 or donors get refunds, with funds held in an "escrow" account managed by David Crane's Govern for California network until the threshold is met — is structurally novel in California politics and raises transparency questions. Funds held in a pre-deposit account before being transferred to a campaign committee may exist in a regulatory gray zone: they are not yet reportable as campaign contributions but are also not ordinary escrow. As of early April, Crane reported $13.5M in the account with another $5M anticipated. [NY Mag, Apr. 9, 2026](https://nymag.com/intelligencer/article/california-candidate-offers-donors-money-back-guarantee.html); [NYT, Apr. 7, 2026](https://www.nytimes.com/2026/04/07/us/elections/california-governor-mahan-donor-silicon-valley.html) **Journalist angle: Did the "escrow" funds comply with California's 24-hour and 10-day late contribution filing rules once transferred? Who custodied the funds and on what legal terms? Were anonymous donors temporarily shielded from disclosure?**

### Angle 3: The Cristo Rey / Liccardo Network — A Mayor's Wife, a Prior Mayor's Wife, and $1.8M in City Grants

Cristo Rey San José Jesuit High School — whose president is Silvia Scandar Mahan — was co-founded by former Mayor Sam Liccardo's wife, Jessica Garcia-Kohl. The school has received three city grants totaling $1.8M since 2017, with $862,500 approved in June 2023 under Mahan's mayoralty (Mahan recused). Two public school districts said they were never notified of the grant opportunity. The Liccardo-Mahan political relationship is comprehensive: Liccardo endorsed Mahan in 2020 and 2022; his chief of staff Jim Reed became Mahan's chief of staff and then the operator of Back to Basics; his nonprofit infrastructure (Solutions SV, Common Good SV) served as the 2022 IE network for Mahan. The Cristo Rey grant is the most tangible personal-benefit question. [San Jose Spotlight, Jun. 27, 2023](https://sanjosespotlight.com/school-run-by-san-jose-mayors-wife-scores-city-grant/) **Journalist angle: Was the grant RFP distributed to competing schools? What are the performance metrics of the city's three Cristo Rey grants? Is the school a vehicle for the Liccardo-Mahan network's soft power over San Jose civic life?**

## 6. DONOR OVERLAPS + CONTRADICTIONS

### Cross-Candidate Overlap (2026 Field)
*[Tier 2 — needs primary Cal-Access verification]*

No Cal-Access itemized filing was accessible to identify specific donors giving to multiple 2026 candidates. However, the following structural patterns are documented:

- **California Federation of Labor** endorsed four candidates simultaneously (Steyer, Swalwell, Villaraigosa, Porter), meaning labor PAC money likely flows to all four. ([CA Labor Federation Mar 16, 2026](https://calaborfed.org/press-releases/california-federation-of-labor-unions-endorse-for-governor-and-other-statewide-races-for-2026-primary-election/))
- **Individual donors overlapping with Becerra/Villaraigosa**: No specific dual donors identified in sources; needs Cal-Access cross-reference.
- **Mahan**: Funded by Silicon Valley tech/anti-labor billionaires — essentially no overlap with Porter's donor base.
- **Steyer**: Primarily self-funded; some individual progressive donors may overlap with Porter.

### Platform Contradictions Flagged

| Tension | Evidence |
|---------|----------|
| **Real estate industry donors vs. housing affordability platform** | National Assn of Realtors PAC ($10,000, 2022 House cycle); $1.03M from real estate individuals career-wide ([OpenSecrets](https://www.opensecrets.org/members-of-congress/katie-porter/industries?cycle=CAREER&type=I)) |
| **Law firm / lobbyist money vs. anti-lobbyist pledge** | $2.54M from Lawyers & Lobbyists sector career-wide; Daily Beast (Dec 2023) found "several" federally registered lobbyist donors who met criteria she pledged to reject — *campaign disputed characterization* |
| **Finance/investment sector vs. anti-Wall Street brand** | $3.24M from Finance/Insurance/Real Estate sector career-wide, mostly individuals, not corporate PACs; $1.36M from Securities & Investment sector |
| **Sugar company PAC** | Accepted $5,000 from American Crystal Sugar Co. PAC in 2019 — a corporate PAC, pre-dating her Senate pledge. [Daily Beast Dec 2023](https://www.thedailybeast.com/katie-porter-touts-clean-campaign-cash-her-record-isnt-so-spotless/) |
| **Trade association PACs** | Accepted from American Council of Life Insurers, Council of Insurance Agents and Brokers PACs — trade groups "function as a shield for individual corporate donations" per watchdog Documented. [Daily Beast Dec 2023](https://www.thedailybeast.com/katie-porter-touts-clean-campaign-cash-her-record-isnt-so-spotless/) |
| **UC Irvine housing subsidy** | Retained below-market-rate faculty housing on UCI campus while serving in Congress 2019–2024; FEC complaint filed, dismissed June 2024 — but she ran on anti-corporate housing platform while benefiting from publicly subsidized housing ([FEC MUR 8105](https://www.fec.gov/files/legal/murs/8105/8105_30.pdf)) |

**Donors with state business**: Gerald Singleton (OVRSITE PAC, $250K) litigates major wildfire cases including against PG&E — a company whose utility monopoly Porter has pledged to challenge as governor. Potential conflict area.

## 8. POLICY-FOR-MONEY

### CFPB and Consumer Protection
Porter served as California's independent monitor of banks under the $25B National Mortgage Settlement (pre-Congress). Her entire political brand is built on CFPB defense and consumer protection.

| Policy Action | Date | Donor Connection |
|--------------|------|-----------------|
| Defended CFPB on House floor against weakening amendment (Consumers First Act H.R. 1500) | May 23, 2019 ([YouTube](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KD4JDRXT-Ag)) | Consistent with anti-bank, anti-corporate donor base; top labor and progressive PAC contributors benefit from CFPB consumer protections |
| Used whiteboard to quiz CFPB Director Kraninger on payday loan APRs | 2019 Financial Services Committee hearing | Organized labor and consumer advocacy donors aligned; no specific donor-for-vote identified |
| Sponsored Stock Act 2.0 (ban congressional stock trading) with Sen. Gillibrand | 2022 | Donors include End Citizens United ($10,150), campaign finance reform constituency |
| Co-founded End Corruption Caucus | 2019 | Donor base in "Democratic/Liberal" sector ($1.69M career) |
| Introduced Stop Scam PACs Act | Aug 2022 | Ideological donors |

**No direct quid pro quo linkage found** between specific donors and specific votes. Porter's career trajectory shows ideological consistency with her donor base (labor, education, progressive organizations). The main tensions noted in Section 6 (real estate, lobbyist/law firm money, UC housing) are contradictions in degree, not in kind.

**Bills benefiting donor industries:**
- HELP America Run Act (HR 623, 2019): Would allow campaign healthcare spending — benefited progressive campaign infrastructure
- No bills identified that directly benefited financial, pharma, or oil/gas donors

## 9. DARK MONEY + SHELL ENTITIES

### 501(c)(4) Activity
No 501(c)(4) organization explicitly running issue advocacy aligned with Porter's positions has been identified in public sources for the 2026 governor race. The large progressive infrastructure (MoveOn, Indivisible, etc.) is generally aligned with her platform but no specific coordinated dark money operation has been reported.

### Shell Entities / LLC Donors
- **Cal-Access itemized filings unavailable** — LLC beneficial owners cannot be assessed (see DATA GAPS).
- No LLC donors to the governor committee have been publicly identified.
- Federal races: no LLC donors found; Porter historically rejects conduit structures.

### WHITEBOARD PAC (Senate 2024)
- Women Have Initiative To Elect, Boost, and Organize for A Real Democrat (WHITEBOARD): pro-Porter Senate super PAC. Raised $620,000. Top donors not fully itemized in sources. Named with clear association to Porter's brand. FEC filing status: active as of March 2024 primary.

### Straw Donor Allegations
No straw donor or conduit allegations found in any Tier 1 or Tier 2 source for any Porter committee.

### FPPC Matters
No FPPC enforcement actions against Porter or any Porter-associated committee found. FPPC enforcement database returned no Porter results in available search. ([FPPC enforcement page](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/enforcement/enforcement-actions.html) — direct search blocked by robots.txt)

---

## 10. ENFORCEMENT + LEGAL

### FEC — MUR 8105 (Primary Source: [FEC MUR 8105](https://www.fec.gov/files/legal/murs/8105/8105_30.pdf))

| Matter | Complainant | Allegation | Outcome |
|--------|------------|-----------|---------|
| **MUR 8105** | Committee to Defeat the President (anti-Biden PAC) / Ted Harvey | UCI made prohibited corporate contribution to Porter via below-market faculty housing and extended unpaid leave (2019–2024); Porter accepted prohibited in-kind contribution | **Dismissed June 4, 2024** ([FEC weekly update Jul 8–12, 2024](https://www.fec.gov/updates/week-of-july-8-12-2024/)) |

**Details**: Porter purchased a 4-bedroom home at UCI's University Hills campus for $522,645.27 in 2011. UCI granted unpaid leaves of absence starting Jan 2019 (congressional service), with renewals. Irvine Campus Housing Authority (ICHA) — a separate legal entity — allowed Porter to retain the home during leave. FEC found: (1) leave per established UC Academic Personnel Manual Sections 750/759; (2) UCI had no control over ICHA housing decisions; (3) no intent to influence election. All allegations dismissed.

**Reputational note**: Even though dismissed, the AP and LA Times investigated the housing arrangement extensively in Sept 2022, finding a UCI law school administrator who was also a Porter campaign donor helped secure her tenure extension. This overlap — a donor with institutional influence over her employment — is not an FEC violation but is a journalistic angle. [Tier 2 — AP/Business Journal reporting]

### Other Enforcement
- **FPPC**: No enforcement actions found against Porter or any Porter committee.
- **Federal/state investigations**: None identified.
- **Civil suits**: None relevant to campaign finance identified.

---

## 11. PRIOR-OFFICE DONOR HISTORY

### House (CA-45 / CA-47, 2018–2024)

**Career federal fundraising** ([OpenSecrets](https://www.opensecrets.org/members-of-congress/katie-porter/industries?cycle=CAREER&type=I)):
- Total categorized: $34.4M (75.37% of total)
- Total uncategorized: $11.2M (24.63%)
- Grand total raised across all federal committees: ~$45.6M career

**Key cycle fundraising (federal)**:
- 2018 (CA-45): Flipped seat from Republican Mimi Walters — exact totals not retrieved but ran on no-corporate-PAC platform from day one
- 2020 (CA-45): Re-elected vs. Greg Raths (53.5/46.5%)
- 2022 (CA-47): Re-elected vs. Scott Baugh (51.7/48.3%) — very close; Porter for Congress received ~$9M from ActBlue alone in 2022 cycle ([OpenSecrets vendor data](https://www.opensecrets.org/campaign-expenditures/vendor?cycle=2022&vendor=Katie+Porter+for+Congress))
- During 2022, House victory committee transferred $147K to Porter, Democracy Engine processed ~$100K, JStreet PAC gave $65K

**No corporate PAC money in any House cycle** (confirmed: [CalMatters Feb 12, 2024](https://calmatters.org/politics/elections/2024/02/california-senate-race-corporate-pacs/))

### 2024 Senate Run

- Announced Jan 10, 2023; raised $1M in first 24 hours (avg. $38) ([CalMatters Mar 11, 2025](https://calmatters.org/politics/2025/03/katie-porter-california-governor/))
- As of Sept 30, 2023: $12M on hand (Schiff had $32M) ([CalMatters Nov 2023](https://calmatters.org/politics/2023/11/california-election-senate-fundraising/))
- Total raised by mid-Feb 2024: ~$28M ([Forbes Mar 7, 2024](https://www.forbes.com/sites/alisondurkee/2024/03/07/rep-katie-porter-doubles-down-after-slamming-california-senate-race-as-rigged-by-billionaires/))
- Lost March 5, 2024 primary: 15.3% of vote, third behind Schiff (31.6%) and Garvey (31.5%)
- Post-primary COH: $1,413,663 (transferred to governor race fund)
- PAC contributions: only $67,526 (0.21% of total) — almost entirely non-corporate ([FEC S4CA00522](https://www.fec.gov/data/candidate/S4CA00522/))
- $3.562M transferred to other authorized committees post-Senate-loss (residual funds)
- Truth to Power leadership PAC raised $1,031,006 and spent $849,234 in 2023–24 cycle; contributed $129,500 to Democratic candidates ([OpenSecrets C00747766](https://www.opensecrets.org/political-action-committees-pacs/truth-to-power/C00747766/summary/2024))

**Continuity into Governor Race**: The ~$1M transfer from Senate residuals into the governor committee is the financial bridge. Her 100,000+ donor list from the Senate race is her main grassroots infrastructure asset.

---

## 12. CONTEXT + JOURNALIST-READY STORY ANGLES

### Angle 1: The Pledge Paradox — Trade Association Money and the "No Corporate PAC" Brand

Porter's brand is built on refusing corporate PAC money — confirmed as genuine throughout her House career. However, a *Daily Beast* investigation (Dec 2023) found she accepted money from trade association PACs (American Crystal Sugar Co. in 2019; American Council of Life Insurers; Council of Insurance Agents and Brokers), which watchdog Documented calls "shields for individual corporate donations." More substantively, her career-wide donor profile includes $3.24M from Finance/Insurance/Real Estate ($74,500 from sector PACs), $1.03M from real estate individuals, and $2.54M from lawyers and lobbyists — while simultaneously running against corporate influence in Sacramento. As governor, she would regulate the insurance industry, real estate development, and financial services. The question is whether donors from those sectors who gave individually (not via PAC) will expect policy consideration. No specific quid pro quo exists, but the aggregate is worth scrutiny. The California governor's race is the first time Porter runs in a state-regulated money environment where corporations can give directly — and she has pledged they won't. Verifying that from Cal-Access Form 460 itemized data is the key reporting step.

### Angle 2: The UC Irvine Housing-Donor Web

The FEC dismissed MUR 8105 (June 2024), but the underlying facts remain: Porter retained below-market faculty housing on the UCI campus 2019–2024 while championing affordable housing as her signature issue. The AP found that at least one UCI law school administrator — who was also a campaign donor — helped facilitate her tenure extension during Congress. The donor-administrator connection is not a campaign finance violation but is a conflict-of-interest narrative. As Porter now runs for governor on a housing affordability platform — and UCI is a public university under the state's UC system, which the governor helps fund and oversee — the optics of the arrangement are worth revisiting. The specific administrator's donation amounts and role would require a fresh FEC itemized search against UCI employer designations.

### Angle 3: The Crypto Billion-Dollar Counteroffensive and What It Means for Tech Policy

Fairshake PAC (crypto/VC: Andreessen $7M, Horowitz $7M, Coinbase/Armstrong, Winklevoss twins) spent $10.04M against Porter in the 2024 Senate primary — the single largest independent expenditure against any CA Senate candidate that cycle. Porter lost. The crypto industry's explicit goal was to prevent a Porter Senate victory; she is now running for governor. If Porter wins the primary and general election, she will be the governor of the state with the highest concentration of crypto and venture capital companies in the world — and they spent $10M to defeat her. No crypto-funded committee has yet formed against her in the governor race (see DATA GAPS). The story is: will Fairshake-aligned interests intervene in a state race, and what does $10M in federal spending foreshadow about the tech-vs.-progressive-governor dynamic if Porter wins? Her CFPB/consumer-protection posture, skepticism of crypto deregulation, and support from labor unions make her the candidate most likely to generate a repeat campaign-finance war with Silicon Valley at the state level.

---

12. **Former staff now lobbying** — No specific individuals identified in any public record or news source.

14. **SKDK consulting relationship** — No payments to SKDK found in any federal or state record. Relationship unconfirmed.

15. **H2 2025 and Q1 2026 burn rate** — Specific spending totals not disaggregated in any Tier 1 source. Approximate COH and raised figures available from Tier 2 sources only.

Steyer stepped down as NextGen leader when he entered the 2020 presidential race; current relationship unclear.

## 6. DONOR OVERLAPS + CONTRADICTIONS

### Cross-Candidate Overlap
Steyer's **near-total self-funding** structurally eliminates most traditional donor-overlap analysis. However:

- **Katie Porter** received **$16,100+ from Steyer personally** between 2018–2023 per FEC filings (House campaigns + Senate campaign). Porter now attacks Steyer in the 2026 race. [Tier 2 — [Fox News/FEC review](https://www.foxnews.com/politics/unearthed-fec-records-expose-katie-porters-hypocrisy-after-she-fumes-new-billionaire-joining-race)]
- **Former Steyer-backed candidates** from NextGen's 2014–2020 IE spending now include some 2026 figures. No specific cross-reference of NextGen's prior CA beneficiaries to current candidates confirmed at primary-source level.
- **Donors backing Matt Mahan's IE** (Michael Moritz, Reed Hastings, Sergey Brin, John Doerr, Vinod Khosla) are tech billionaires who have historically been aligned with moderate Democratic giving — these are **not Steyer donors** and represent the opposite end of the progressive-moderate Democratic spectrum.

### Farallon-Adjacent Money
- **Farallon Capital Management** (Steyer's former firm, still operating) has had no confirmed contributions to any 2026 CA gubernatorial campaign in available filings.
- Farallon's known investors and limited partners are not publicly identified per hedge fund norms (13F disclosures show portfolio positions, not LP identities).
- **Coal/fossil fuel contradiction:** Farallon invested hundreds of millions in Indonesian, Indian, and Chinese coal mining (Berau, Indiabulls, Meiya Power) and the Australian Maules Creek mine (30-year operating life) while Steyer was co-senior managing partner through 2012. Steyer completed personal divestment in 2014 but acknowledged in September 2019 debate he retained "some remnants" in hydrocarbons. [[The Hill](https://thehill.com/policy/energy-environment/478320-steyer-claims-he-divested-from-fossil-fuels-a-decade-ago-but-its/)] [[NYT 2014](https://www.nytimes.com/2014/07/05/us/politics/prominent-environmentalist-helped-fund-coal-projects.html)]
- **Private prison contradiction:** Farallon purchased ~$90M in CCA (now CoreCivic) stock (5.5% of outstanding shares) while Steyer was at the helm. CCA now operates federal ICE detention facilities. Steyer campaign calls the investment a "mistake" and says stock was sold by 2006. [[Politico CA](https://www.politico.com/states/california/story/2016/10/tom-steyer-pursuing-racial-and-economic-justice-issues-invested-heavily-in-for-profit-prisons-106634)]
- **Tobacco contradiction:** Farallon also invested in tobacco companies while Steyer simultaneously funded Prop 56 tobacco tax ($10.8M at time of the Sacramento Bee report). [Tier 2 — Politico reference]
- **None of these Farallon-adjacent investments appear to have generated direct political contributions** to Steyer's 2026 campaign from Farallon-linked parties, based on available evidence.

---

## 8. POLICY-FOR-MONEY ANALYSIS

### Climate Platform vs. Farallon Fossil-Fuel Holdings

**The Gap:** Steyer's flagship political identity is as the premier climate billionaire in American politics. He has spent an estimated $65M on Democratic candidates and climate ballot measures in 2016 alone, and $341M on his 2020 presidential campaign centered on climate emergency. Yet Farallon, under his leadership (1986–2012), funded:
- **Indonesian coal:** Berau coal ($60M+ loan 2004), production growing from 9M to 20M tons annually [NYT](https://www.nytimes.com/2014/07/05/us/politics/prominent-environmentalist-helped-fund-coal-projects.html)
- **Indian coal power:** Indiabulls subsidiary — 7,700MW Amravati + 1,350MW Nasik coal-fired plants; 20-year power purchase agreements
- **Chinese coal power:** Meiya Power — four plants, ~7,000MW total
- **Australian coal mining:** Maules Creek mine — $hundreds of millions investment, 30-year operational life, ~13M tons/year, ~30M tons CO2/year
- **Combined output:** Estimated 60M+ tons of CO2 per year from Indiabulls + Meiya alone [Resources for the Future estimate, per NYT]
- **Farallon's coal mines increased annual production by ~70 million tons** since receiving Farallon capital [NYT 2014]
- **Private prisons:** ~$90M in CCA/CoreCivic stock (5.5% of outstanding shares) [Politico](https://www.politico.com/states/california/story/2016/10/tom-steyer-pursuing-racial-and-economic-justice-issues-invested-heavily-in-for-profit-prisons-106634)
- **Tobacco:** Investments in tobacco firms while simultaneously funding tobacco tax campaigns [Tier 2 — Politico reference]
- **Keystone XL-related investments:** Farallon invested in Nexen ($220M, Sept. 2012), which developed Canadian oil sands operations [EBSCO/InfluenceWatch]

**Steyer's defense:** "I stepped back in 2012. I divested over a decade ago. It was a wake-up call." His campaign characterizes Farallon's portfolio as an inherent product of managing a diversified global fund across all sectors. [Tier 2 — Politico Playbook]

**2026 Campaign context:** Steyer's platform calls for:
- Breaking up CA investor-owned utility monopolies (direct threat to PG&E, SoCal Edison, SDG&E)
- Lowering utility bills by 25%
- Building 1 million homes in 4 years
- Universal healthcare (single-payer)
- Raising corporate property taxes
- Abolishing ICE

**Galvanize Conflict of Interest:** Steyer co-founded and remains associated with Galvanize Climate Solutions, a $1B+ climate-tech investment fund. His CA climate policies (clean energy build-out, EV mandates, utility restructuring) would benefit Galvanize portfolio companies. He took leave but did not fully divest. [Tier 2 — Harvard Political Review, [https://theharvardpoliticalreview.com/steyer-economy-environment/](https://theharvardpoliticalreview.com/steyer-economy-environment/)]

### Need to Impeach Donor Base / CA Overlap

Steyer invested **>$75M personally** in Need to Impeach (2017–2020), building a list of **8M+ signatories/donors** to the impeachment petition. [[CNBC](https://www.cnbc.com/2020/04/16/2020-election-tom-steyer-shuts-down-need-to-impeach-operation.html)] This email/donor list is one of the largest progressive contact databases in the country. Per 2019 reporting, Steyer spent ~$40M in 2019 alone rallying this network to pressure Congress. [Center for Public Integrity](https://publicintegrity.org/politics/tom-steyer-trump-impeachment/)

**Potential CA voter mobilization:** Whether the Need to Impeach/NextGen list is being deployed in the CA 2026 race for voter contact (as a 501(c)(4) activity rather than direct campaign contribution) is not confirmed from primary sources.

### Specific Donor-Policy Alignments
| Donor/Funder | Policy Interest | Steyer Position | Notes |
|-------------|----------------|----------------|-------|
| CA Teachers Association | Education funding, labor protections | Free community college; fund schools via corporate taxes (Prop 39 model) | CTA endorsing Steyer after Swalwell implosion |
| CA Nurses Association | Single-payer healthcare | "Only one who can deliver single-payer" | Strong alignment |
| Our Revolution | Progressive economic platform | Billionaire self-funder making anti-billionaire-influence pitch | Ideological alignment, unorthodox |
| PG&E ($10M against) | Preserve IOU utility monopoly | Break up utilities; reduce ROE | Direct conflict |
| CA Association of Realtors ($5M against) | Preserve Prop 13 commercial property protections | Lift commercial property tax limits (split-roll) | Direct conflict |

## 9. DARK MONEY + SHELL ENTITIES

### Steyer-Run 501(c)(4)s — Annual Revenue (ProPublica Nonprofit Explorer)

**NextGen Climate Action (EIN 46-1957345)** — primary 501(c)(4) vehicle. **Does not disclose individual donors** (standard for 501(c)(4)s). Steyer was effectively the sole or dominant funder in early years.

| Fiscal Year | Total Contributions |
|-------------|-------------------|
| 2013 | $6,270,000 |
| 2014 | $13,310,873 |
| 2015 | $23,513,084 |
| 2016 | $44,436,006 |
| 2017 | $19,488,943 |
| 2018 | **$53,984,607** |
| 2019 | $10,575,596 |
| 2020 | $10,480,887 |
| 2021 | $4,291,975 |
| 2022 | $20,404,892 |
| 2023 | $10,542,428 |
| 2024 | **$38,464,337** |

Source: [ProPublica Nonprofit Explorer](https://projects.propublica.org/nonprofits/organizations/461957345)

**Total contributions 2013–2024: ~$255M** — the dominant funder across all years is Steyer personally, with the 2021–2022 InfluenceWatch report confirming $5.08M Steyer personal contribution to NextGen Climate Action Committee (FEC super PAC arm) in 2021–22 cycle, plus $790K from America Votes and $300K from SEIU United We Can. [InfluenceWatch](https://www.influencewatch.org/political-party/nextgen-climate-action-committee/)

**Need to Impeach (501(c)(4), closed April 2020):** Steyer invested **>$75M personally** (spokesperson confirmed: "over $75 million of his personal funds"). [[CNBC](https://www.cnbc.com/2020/04/16/2020-election-tom-steyer-shuts-down-need-to-impeach-operation.html)] An FEC July–December 2019 report showed Steyer contributed **$4M+** to NTI even while running for president. Organization shut down after House impeachment vote; had $650K remaining.

**NextGen Policy:** Listed as active 501(c)(4); Kat Taylor serves as Board Chair. No 990 data retrieved at time of filing.

**Galvanize Climate Solutions:** Investment firm (LP structure), **not a nonprofit**. No 990 or IRS reporting obligation. Closed $1B fund in September 2023. [Axios](https://www.axios.com/pro/climate-deals/2023/09/14/galvanize-closes-1b-climate-tech-fund) Galvanize closed a decarbonization real estate fund in March 2026. [Heatmap](https://heatmap.news/climate-tech/galvanize-real-estate) Steyer on leave (not fully divested) while running for governor — creating potential policy conflict (see Section 8).

**FEC MUR 7587 — DACA Workers allegation:** A complaint alleged Steyer 2020 presidential campaign hired foreign nationals (DACA recipients). The FEC Office of General Counsel found "the available record does not" suggest a violation given lack of specific allegations and sworn statements from Steyer 2020. The FEC dismissed the Steyer portion while finding reason to believe against Sanders. [[FEC MUR 7587 Statement of Reasons](https://www.fec.gov/files/legal/murs/7587/7587_34.pdf)]

**FEC MUR 7712:** A separate complaint alleged Steyer campaign used "foreign national illegal aliens." Outcome: appears dismissed without enforcement action per available public records.

## 10. ENFORCEMENT + LEGAL HISTORY

### Federal (FEC)
| Matter | Description | Outcome |
|--------|-------------|---------|
| **MUR 7587** | Allegation Steyer 2020 hired DACA foreign nationals | Dismissed — OGC found insufficient evidence; FEC voted not to pursue [FEC PDF](https://www.fec.gov/files/legal/murs/7587/7587_34.pdf) |
| **MUR 7712** | Allegation of "foreign national illegal aliens" in campaign | Referenced in FEC records; no enforcement confirmed [FEC PDF](https://www.fec.gov/files/legal/murs/7712/7712_01.pdf) |
| **Iowa Endorsement-for-Pay Scandal (2019)** | Pat Murphy (Iowa state house speaker, Steyer's IA campaign aide) allegedly offered cash payments to Iowa politicians for endorsements | Murphy apologized; Steyer campaign denied authorization. No FEC enforcement action resulted. Campaign filed no disclosures of such payments confirming no money changed hands. [Salon](https://www.salon.com/2019/11/07/top-aide-for-billionaire-tom-steyers-presidential-campaign-busted-offering-cash-for-endorsements/); [CNN](https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/07/politics/tom-steyer-report-aide-money-endorsements) |
| **SC Voter Data Theft (2019)** | Dwane Sims (SC deputy state director) stole Kamala Harris campaign volunteer data from South Carolina Democratic Party VoteBuilder system | Sims fired; Steyer campaign apologized to Harris campaign; data deleted. No FEC or DOJ enforcement resulted. [CBS News](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/tom-steyer-kamala-harris-steyer-staffer-accused-of-stealing-voter-data/); [Fox News](https://www.foxnews.com/politics/steyer-aide-resigns-after-stealing-2020-voltunteer-data-from-harris-campaign-in-south-carolina) |

### California (Civil / Labor)
| Matter | Description | Outcome |
|--------|-------------|---------|
| **Wage/Labor Settlements (2021)** | Five former 2020 presidential campaign staffers filed complaints under California labor law (Private Attorneys General Act) for wage and labor violations. Two filed suit. | Steyer campaign paid **$24,000+** in settlement payments to five staffers + **~$19,000** in back wages to four staffers + **$40,000+** to Shavitz Law Group (plaintiff's labor law firm). Total exposure: ~$83,000+. [Politico](https://www.politico.com/news/2021/05/05/tom-steyer-settlement-campaign-staffers-485409) |

### FPPC
No current FPPC enforcement action against Steyer identified through FPPC enforcement page (site blocked) or web search. FPPC reports $21.025M in opposition IE spending against Steyer — confirming he is the most targeted candidate in the June 2026 primary by outside money. [[FPPC June 2026](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/)]

### Private Prison Ad / Cease and Desist (2026)
Steyer's campaign sent a cease-and-desist letter to an LA ABC affiliate regarding anti-Steyer ads that attributed Farallon's CCA investment to Steyer personally. The letter argues Farallon (not Steyer individually) made the investment and there are "no surviving records indicating what, if anything, he made." [Tier 2 — [Politico CA Playbook](https://www.politico.com/newsletters/california-playbook-pm/2026/04/08/steyer-private-prison-ad-00864330)] The anti-Steyer committee responded calling it "a thinly veiled attempt to rewrite history."

### D. Need to Impeach (501(c)(4), 2017–2020)
- Founded 2017 to pressure Congress to impeach Trump
- Steyer invested **$75M+ personally** over its 2.5-year life [[CNBC](https://www.cnbc.com/2020/04/16/2020-election-tom-steyer-shuts-down-need-to-impeach-operation.html)]
- Additional **$40M** pledged in January 2019 for ground mobilization [[ABC13](https://abc13.com/trump-impeachment-impeach-need-to-tom-steyer/5042710/)]
- Built list of **8M+ signatories** — the largest progressive mobilization list outside the DNC at the time
- Shut down April 2020 after House impeachment vote; $650K on hand at close
- **Funders:** Steyer was the primary and likely sole major donor; 501(c)(4) structure means no public donor disclosure

### E. California Ballot Measure Committees

#### Prop 39 (2012) — Out-of-State Business Tax / Clean Energy Jobs
- **Result:** PASSED
- Steyer: Author, primary funder, $21.9M personal contribution
- Total campaign raised: $23.1M

- **Result:** PASSED
- Steyer: Top supporter, **$11.55M** personal direct + additional via NextGen California Committee ($250K per FPPC) = **$11.8M+**
- Source: [FPPC Nov 2016](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/overview-of-november-2016-general-election/november-2016-general-election/); [Ballotpedia Prop 56](https://ballotpedia.org/California_Proposition_56,_Tobacco_Tax_Increase_(2016)) [Tier 2]
- **Note:** Farallon had previously invested in tobacco companies — creating the same contradiction pattern as fossil fuels.

#### Prop 67 (2016) — Plastic Bag Ban
- **Result:** PASSED
- Steyer: Supported (NextGen California Committee contributed $250K per FPPC 2016 list) [FPPC Nov 2016](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/overview-of-november-2016-general-election/november-2016-general-election/)

#### Prop 30 (2022) — EV/Wildfire Tax (Income >$2M)
- **Result:** FAILED (42.37% Yes, 57.63% No)
- Steyer: Supporter; personal contribution **$50,000** per FPPC 2022 list
- Primary funder was **Lyft ($45.2M)**; Steyer was not a significant financial driver of this campaign
- Gov. Newsom and CTA opposed — calling it a Lyft "cynical scheme"
- Source: [FPPC Nov 2022](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/november-2022-general-election/); [Ballotpedia Prop 30](https://ballotpedia.org/California_Proposition_30,_Tax_on_Income_Above_$2_Million_for_Zero-Emissions_Vehicles_and_Wildfire_Prevention_Initiative_(2022)) [Tier 2]

#### Prop 23 (2010) — Defeat Big Oil (Delay AB 32 Climate Law)
- Steyer invested $5M to **defeat** Prop 23 (which would have rolled back CA climate law) — considered the start of his public climate activism. [InfluenceWatch](https://www.influencewatch.org/person/tom-steyer/)

### F. Galvanize Climate Solutions
- Founded September 2021 with partner Kathryn Hall (wife Kat Taylor also listed as co-founder in some sources)
- Closed **$1 billion Fund I** (climate tech, early to growth stage) — September 2023 [Axios](https://www.axios.com/pro/climate-deals/2023/09/14/galvanize-closes-1b-climate-tech-fund)
- Closed decarbonization **real estate fund** — March 2026 [Heatmap](https://heatmap.news/climate-tech/galvanize-real-estate)
- Steyer is Co-Chair on leave; not a 501(c)(4) or PAC — investment LP structure
- **Not a dark money entity** but creates financial-conflict-of-interest optics: Steyer's CA energy/climate policies would benefit Galvanize portfolio companies

---

## 12. CONTEXT + JOURNALIST-READY ANGLES

### Angle 1: The Billionaire Who Campaigns Against Billionaires — And Is Losing on Persuasion Despite Winning on Spending

Tom Steyer is running the most expensive California gubernatorial campaign in state history, on pace to exceed $150M+ of personal spending, but remains **statistically tied** with rivals who are spending 10–30x less. Politico reports he was "tied with Eric Swalwell" after spending $120M — and then potentially "tied with Katie Porter" as well. [[Politico](https://www.politico.com/news/2026/04/16/swalwell-exit-steyer-money-governor-race-00875079)] CalMatters frames the central question: "Will another $120 million fundamentally change that?" The race raises a concrete empirical question about the diminishing marginal returns of self-funded campaigns — and whether a candidate who explicitly campaigns against billionaire influence can win by becoming the biggest-spending billionaire in California election history. His $341M in 2020 bought him a third-place finish in South Carolina.

### Angle 2: The Opposition Machine — How PG&E Is Trying to Buy the Governor's Race (Against Steyer)

The most notable financial story of the 2026 CA governor's race is not who is giving *to* Steyer but who is giving against him: **$21.025M in confirmed FPPC opposition money**, dominated by Pacific Gas & Electric ($9.975M) and anchored by a coalition of the CA Chamber of Commerce ($5M via JOBSPAC), CA Realtors ($5M), and CA Building Industry ($1M). [[FPPC](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/)] PG&E CEO Patti Poppe told investor analysts that "politicians have to say what they have to say, I guess, to get elected" in a remarkable on-record dismissal of Steyer's utility reform platform. [Energy and Policy Institute](https://energyandpolicy.org/becerra-150k-from-ca-utilities/) The story writes itself: a regulated monopoly spending $10M to defeat the candidate who wants to break it up. This is the inversion of traditional campaign finance analysis — the "dark money" question here is not who funds Steyer but who funds the opposition to him.

### Angle 3: Farallon's Long Shadow — The Fossil Fuel, Prison, and Tobacco Investments That Follow a Climate Billionaire

Every election cycle since 2014, Tom Steyer has faced variants of the same attack: his fortune was built in part on investments that contradict his environmental and progressive platform. In 2026, the three most prominent are coal (Farallon's hundreds of millions in Indonesian, Indian, Chinese, and Australian coal mining), private prisons (the ~$90M CCA stake, now a CoreCivic that operates ICE facilities), and tobacco (Farallon investments while Steyer funded CA's tobacco tax). [[NYT](https://www.nytimes.com/2014/07/05/us/politics/prominent-environmentalist-helped-fund-coal-projects.html)] [[Politico CA](https://www.politico.com/states/california/story/2016/10/tom-steyer-pursuing-racial-and-economic-justice-issues-invested-heavily-in-for-profit-prisons-106634)] In 2026, the private-prison angle has been weaponized by anti-Steyer PAC ads linking the CCA investment to Trump's ICE detention operations — a direct attempt to undercut his immigration platform with immigrant-rights voters. The new twist: Steyer's current climate investment firm **Galvanize** stands to benefit financially from the exact CA clean-energy policies he's promising to enact as governor, creating a prospective (rather than retrospective) conflict of interest that has received less scrutiny than his Farallon past.

**Status: SUSPENDED (still on June 2 ballot)**
_Prepared: 2026-04-29 | Primary: 2026-06-02_

## 1. Campaign Committee

**Committee name:** Swalwell for Governor 2026
**Cal-Access status:** Cal-Access direct retrieval was blocked (robots.txt disallow); committee detail page inaccessible via automated fetch. See DATA GAPS.

**IE Support Committee (FPPC-filed):**
- "Californians for a Fighter in Support of Eric Swalwell for Governor 2026" — Committee ID **1488732** ([FPPC June 2026 Primary Top Contributors](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/))
- Second IE committee: "Nurses and Educators Supporting Swalwell for Governor 2026 sponsored by SEIU California State Council" — Committee ID **1489873** ([FPPC](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/))

**Self-installed as treasurer:** Following suspension of his campaign, new Cal-Access filings show Swalwell installed himself as treasurer of the gubernatorial committee, giving him direct control over the remaining $4 million cash on hand — a move flagged by news reports as highly unusual. [Tier 2 — needs primary Cal-Access verification] ([Instagram/WABC post citing filings, Apr 24 2026](https://www.instagram.com/p/DXh5Ly8FMiX/))

**Key dates:**
- **Campaign announced:** November 20, 2025 ([CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/politics/2025/11/california-governor-eric-swallwell-announcement/))
- **Allegations published:** Friday, April 10, 2026 — *San Francisco Chronicle* and *CNN* ([CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-race-swalwell-allegations/))
- **Campaign suspended:** Sunday, April 12, 2026 ([AP](https://apnews.com/article/swalwell-democrats-california-governor-campaign-allegations-congress-8b60b0c226f93c691633231053d5ddf9); [Sacramento Bee](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/article315374153.html))
- **Resigned from Congress:** Monday, April 14, 2026 (effective immediately) ([Ballotpedia](https://news.ballotpedia.org/2026/04/22/eric-swalwells-resignation-leaves-californias-14th-congressional-district-vacant/); [270toWin](https://www.270towin.com/news/2026/04/14/democrat-eric-swalwell-republican-tony-gonzales-resign-congress_1802.html))
- **Name remains on ballot:** Suspension came after the statutory withdrawal deadline; Swalwell will appear on the June 2, 2026 primary ballot ([ABC7](https://abc7news.com/post/rep-eric-swalwell-suspends-california-governor-campaign-amid-sexual-assault-allegations/18876982/))

**Allegations summary:** A former district office staffer alleged rape in 2019 (when she was 21) and again in 2024, both times while too intoxicated to consent. Three other women told CNN of additional misconduct, including unsolicited explicit Snapchat photos. On April 15, Lonna Drewes held a press conference in Beverly Hills alleging Swalwell drugged her wine at a 2018 political event, took her to his hotel room, and choked and raped her. A second woman subsequently accused him of drugging and rape, bringing the total to five accusers. Swalwell denied all rape allegations while acknowledging unspecified "mistakes in judgment." ([Sacramento Bee timeline](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/capitol-alert/article315414220.html); [Sacramento Bee resignation](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/capitol-alert/article315398771.html))

---

## 2. Top-Line Fundraising at Suspension

All figures as of most recent available Cal-Access filings; direct primary source retrieval partially blocked (see DATA GAPS).

| Metric | Amount | Source |
|--------|--------|--------|
| **Direct contributions raised** (through ~Apr 9) | ~$7.4 million (>$8.7M by Apr 18 filing) | [LA Times](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-04-13/swalwell-supporters-scramble-after-he-drops-out-of-governors-race-who-benefits); [SF Chronicle tracker](https://www.sfchronicle.com/projects/2026/ca-governor-campaign-finance/) |
| **IE support raised** (primarily formed committees) | $12,755,500 | [FPPC](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/) |
| **Cash on hand** (Apr 18 report) | ~$4,000,000 | [SF Chronicle / iHeart](https://kost1035.iheart.com/featured/la-local-news/content/2026-04-28-swalwell-campaign-donors-seek-15-million-in-refunds-after-scandal/) |
| **Unpaid debts** (Apr 18 report) | ~$200,000 | [SF Chronicle](https://www.sfchronicle.com/politics/article/eric-swalwell-donor-refunds-22228349.php) |
| **Post-scandal donations received** (after Apr 10) | >$190,000 | [NY Post](https://nypost.com/2026/04/24/us-news/eric-swalwells-190k-post-scandal-cash-surge-raises-new-questions/) |
| **Refund requests** (as of Apr 28) | >$1.5M from 200+ donors | [SF Chronicle](https://www.sfchronicle.com/politics/article/eric-swalwell-donor-refunds-22228349.php) |

**What is happening to the $4M COH:** Swalwell installed himself as treasurer (Apr 24 filing), giving him sole control. Campaign staff report receiving hundreds of refund requests but have no authorized procedure or direction on processing them. The $40,000 attorney payment to Sara Azari (hired to defend him on TV) and $141,451 to Greenberg Traurig for "professional legal/accounting" services are among recent disbursements. No legal defense fund has been opened. Remaining funds may sit idle, be donated to party/charity, or used for wind-down costs — California law does not require refunds absent a court order. Cloobeck (who gave $1M+ through IE committee) threatened legal action for refund. [Tier 2] ([NOTUS](https://www.notus.org/money/eric-swalwell-tony-gonzales-campaign-money-surplus); [Newsweek](https://www.newsweek.com/eric-swalwell-used-campaign-funds-pay-attorney-who-publicly-defended-him-11875211))
