## 4. Endorser and Donor Network Migration

### Key Endorsers Pre-Suspension
- **Stephen Cloobeck** — Billionaire Democratic donor, protégé of late Sen. Harry Reid. Dropped his own gubernatorial campaign in November 2025 to endorse Swalwell, pledged financial support, and ultimately contributed $1M+ via IE committee. Post-suspension: publicly cut ties, threatened to sue for refund, and indicated he may register as Republican and endorse **Steve Hilton** (R). ([Sacramento Bee, Nov 2025](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/capitol-alert/article313129156.html); [LA Times](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-04-13/swalwell-supporters-scramble-after-he-drops-out-of-governors-race-who-benefits))
- **Ian Calderon** — Former Assembly Majority Leader. Dropped his own governor bid in March 2026 to endorse Swalwell. Post-suspension status: no announced new endorsement as of April 29. ([YouTube/March 2026](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_WwYvRFWu9A))
- **California Democratic Party (CADEM) delegates** — Swalwell led the February 2026 convention vote with 24% (571 votes), well short of the 60% threshold for party endorsement. No endorsement issued. ([CADEM Convention Results](https://cadem.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/2026-Convention-Endorsing-Conference-Results.pdf))
- **Major labor:** California Teachers Association, SEIU California (Local 2015, Local 1000), California Professional Firefighters, California Labor Federation — all endorsed Swalwell, all withdrew support after allegations. Post-suspension: SEIU and CTA indicated they would not re-endorse another candidate before June 2 due to internal process requirements. ([CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/swalwell-congress-resignation/))
- **California Medical Association** — Major funder ($1.095M IE). Withdrew support; held emergency meetings. No new endorsement announced.
- **Elected officials:** Reps. Julia Brownley, Scott Peters, Jimmy Gomez (co-chair), Adam Gray (co-chair), Adam Schiff, others — withdrew endorsements after allegations. Rep. Jared Huffman was among first to call for Swalwell's resignation and then endorsed **Tom Steyer**. ([Politico CA Playbook](https://www.politico.com/newsletters/california-playbook/2026/03/30/a-big-weekend-for-eric-swalwell-00849924); [LA Times](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-04-13/swalwell-supporters-scramble-after-he-drops-out-of-governors-race-who-benefits))

### Where Did Swalwell's Support Go?
[Tier 2] ([LA Times](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-04-13/swalwell-supporters-scramble-after-he-drops-out-of-governors-race-who-benefits); [CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/swalwell-congress-resignation/))

- **Tom Steyer** — Most immediate organized beneficiary. Rep. Huffman (first to call for resignation) endorsed Steyer. UC Berkeley IGS and PPIC polling identified Steyer and Porter as top beneficiaries.
- **Katie Porter** — Porter's internal polling showed nearly half of Swalwell's supporters listed her as second choice. Democratic Women's Legislative Caucus members reconsidered endorsements in her favor. Profile overlap: Swalwell ran better with older, whiter, more liberal/progressive voters — a similar profile to Porter's base.
- **Matt Mahan** — IE committee raised $12M in new/committed contributions in the days following Swalwell's exit. Major tech/VC donors (Moritz, Caruso, Collison, Khosla, Hastings, Doerr) are backing Mahan, not Swalwell.
- **Xavier Becerra** — Polling surge post-suspension. Emerson/other polls showed Becerra gaining ground. ([Santa Barbara News-Press](https://www.newspress.com/2026/04/25/becerra-support-swalwell-exit-race/))
- **No consensus:** California Labor Federation said it would not revisit its endorsements. CTA cannot hold a new vote before June 2.

---

| Forum | Matter | Status |
|-------|--------|--------|
| **Manhattan DA** | Sexual assault allegation (unnamed former staffer; alleged 2024 incident in NY) | Investigation open as of Apr 12, 2026 ([NBC News](https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/elections/eric-swalwell-drops-bid-california-governor-sexual-misconduct-allegati-rcna277009)) |
| **LA County Sheriff / DA** | Lonna Drewes allegation (2018 West Hollywood hotel; drugging, choking, rape); attorney Lisa Bloom transmitting evidence | Investigation open as of Apr 15, 2026 ([Sacramento Bee](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/capitol-alert/article315414220.html)) |
| **DOJ (federal)** | Unspecified federal investigation; scope not confirmed publicly | Open per source familiar; Swalwell's attorney did not respond ([Sacramento Bee](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/capitol-alert/article315436793.html)) |
| **FEC complaint** | Filmmaker Joel Gilbert filed complaint alleging $244,000 in campaign funds used for childcare (2019–2025). Complaint assigned to FEC attorney. | Pending ([Sacramento Bee](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/capitol-alert/article315436793.html)) |
| **DHS investigation** | Gilbert complaint re: immigration status of former nanny | Pending ([Sacramento Bee](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/capitol-alert/article315436793.html)) |
| **FEC filings / hotel payments** | Swalwell for Congress paid $1,100 to Cosmopolitan of Las Vegas hotel in July 2021; $361 to Montrose hotel in West Hollywood in July 2018 — dates/locations match accusations. Legally ambiguous; subject of scrutiny. | No formal FEC enforcement action filed as of Apr 29 [Tier 2] ([Newsweek](https://www.newsweek.com/fec-filings-align-with-timing-location-cited-in-new-swalwell-allegation-11834142)) |
| **FPPC** | No FPPC enforcement matter identified as of April 29, 2026 | None confirmed |
| **Civil suits** | No civil lawsuits confirmed filed as of April 29, 2026; Drewes (rep. Bloom) has not filed suit | None filed as of research date |
| **Findraiser AI company** | Swalwell co-founded campaign data AI firm; paid by his own campaign ($975 governor; $6,630 House). Ethics concerns raised; no formal action. | No enforcement action [Tier 2] ([LA Times](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-03-19/rep-swalwell-candidate-for-california-governor-has-ai-side-gig)) |

_Note: Swalwell also faced a two-year investigation in 2020–2021 regarding ties to Christine Fang, a suspected Chinese intelligence operative who volunteered on his 2014 campaign. No wrongdoing was found; he was cleared and retained his Intelligence Committee seat at the time. This is historical context, not an active investigation._

## 7. Relevance to 2026 Race Despite Suspension

**Swalwell remains on the June 2 primary ballot** — the statutory withdrawal deadline passed before he suspended his campaign on April 12. Governor Newsom confirmed his name cannot be removed. ([ABC7](https://abc7news.com/post/rep-eric-swalwell-suspends-california-governor-campaign-amid-sexual-assault-allegations/18876982/))

**Pre-suspension polling position:** Swalwell was consistently in a three-way tie for the Democratic lead with Porter and Steyer, each polling 10–15% of likely primary voters. He led all Democrats in the February CADEM delegate vote (24%). ([CADEM results](https://cadem.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/2026-Convention-Endorsing-Conference-Results.pdf); [CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/swalwell-congress-resignation/))

**Siphon risk:** Votes cast for Swalwell will count and will not transfer. In a crowded field where the top-two finish can send two Republicans to the general election, even 2–5% of protest votes for Swalwell could be decisive. CADEM chair Rusty Hicks explicitly warned voters Swalwell is "unfit" and urged minimal support; Newsom declined to make similar public statement. [Tier 2] ([ABC7](https://abc7news.com/post/rep-eric-swalwell-suspends-california-governor-campaign-amid-sexual-assault-allegations/18876982/))

**Who absorbs his vote:** UC Berkeley IGS analysis: Swalwell's voters were more liberal, older, white — closest match to **Katie Porter**. Steyer also identified as beneficiary. Becerra polling surged post-exit. Mahan's IE committee raised $12M in new commitments from institutional donors in days after suspension, signaling big-money opportunism. [Tier 2] ([CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/swalwell-congress-resignation/); [Santa Barbara News-Press](https://www.newspress.com/2026/04/25/becerra-support-swalwell-exit-race/))

**Lingering fundraising threat:** Swalwell still controls ~$4M in COH from a suspended campaign. No refund process is underway; he has unilateral access as self-appointed treasurer. This creates ongoing legal and reputational uncertainty that could distract from the primary. [Tier 2] ([NOTUS](https://www.notus.org/money/eric-swalwell-tony-gonzales-campaign-money-surplus))

# TONY THURMOND — DONOR INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER
**2026 California Governor's Race | Primary: June 2, 2026**
*Research completed: April 29, 2026 | All $ figures require URL-cited verification; Tier-2 sources flagged inline*

---

## 1. CAMPAIGN COMMITTEES

### Thurmond for Governor 2026
| Field | Detail |
|---|---|
| **Committee Name** | Tony Thurmond for Governor 2026 |
| **Cal-Access ID** | 1461509-CTL |
| **Treasurer** | Not retrievable from Cal-Access (robots disallow; see DATA GAPS) |
| **TransparencyUSA URL** | [TransparencyUSA Committee Page](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/committee/tony-thurmond-for-governor-2026-1461509-ctl) |
| **Filing status** | Most recent preelection statement: 04/18/2026 per [The Ballot Book](https://theballotbook.com/campaign_finance/2026_primary_overview) |

Thurmond registered "Tony Thurmond for Governor 2026" in July 2023 and began accepting contributions that summer, per [KTVU reporting](https://www.ktvu.com/news/california-official-endorsed-newsom-donations-for-governor). The committee's early first-filed contribution was from the Union of American Physicians and Dentists Sacramento and a committee associated with former Assemblymember Jim Frazier.

### Prior Committees
- **Thurmond for Superintendent 2018** — Thurmond ran as Assemblymember (AD-15) and defeated charter-backed Marshall Tuck in a razor-close general (50.9% vs. 49.1%). The FPPC top-contributor list records $12,989,175 in aggregate support, per the [FPPC November 2018 General Election page](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/transparency/top-contributors/nov-18-gen.html). Committee: *Educators Supporting Tony Thurmond for Superintendent of Public Instruction 2018, sponsored by teachers and school employees organizations.* Cal-Access IDs for these prior committees were not retrievable via direct Cal-Access search (see DATA GAPS); TransparencyUSA does not disaggregate by prior committee cycle.

- **Thurmond for Superintendent 2022** — Committee: *Californians Supporting Tony Thurmond for Superintendent of Public Instruction 2022, sponsored by Teacher, School Employee and Labor Organizations* (Cal-Access ID: **1448022**), per [FPPC June 2022 Primary Election top contributors](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2022-primary-election/). Total IE support: $2,200,000 in the primary. In the general, CTA IE Committee and SEIU affiliates again dominated, per [FPPC November 2022 Top Two Donors](https://lunar.fppc.ca.gov/transparency/top-contributors/nov-22-gen/Top_Two_Donors.html).

### Officeholder / Legal-Defense Funds
No officeholder fund or legal-defense fund has been identified in public filings. [Tier 2 — needs primary verification]

### Federal Committees
**Confirmed N/A.** Thurmond has served exclusively in state-level offices (West Contra Costa School Board, Richmond City Council, California State Assembly AD-15 2014–2018, California Superintendent of Public Instruction 2019–present). No FEC committee is registered in his name per [OpenSecrets](https://www.opensecrets.org/officeholders/tony-k-thurmond/contributors?cycle=2024&id=6485735). He does appear on OpenSecrets as a state officeholder with a non-federal account tracked there for cross-reference purposes only.

| Metric | Amount | Source |

The committee-level 2024-cycle page shows $477,616 COH. The X/Pyers figure of ~$356,000 as of late April 2026 represents the most recent period and is internally consistent with the committee having spent ~$184,000 since year-end 2025.

| **Tony Thurmond** | **$181K** | **$62K** | **~$356K** |
| Betty Yee | ~$342K | — | — |

Sources: [CalMatters Feb 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/02/governors-race-fundraising-reports/); [JPR Apr 2026](https://www.ijpr.org/politics-government/2026-04-27/billionaire-blitz-steyers-132-million-campaign-dwarfs-rivals-in-california-governor-race); [Sacramento Bee Aug 2025](https://www.sacbee.com/news/politics-government/capitol-alert/article311551289.html).

**Assessment:** Thurmond's fundraising is critically anemic. At $62,000 raised in four months, he trailed some state Assembly candidates in the same period, per [CalMatters](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/02/governors-race-fundraising-reports/). His burn rate — spending ~$184,000 while raising $62,000 — is unsustainable. Polling consistently places him at 1% of likely Democratic primary voters, per [Politico CA Playbook March 2026](https://www.politico.com/newsletters/california-playbook/2026/03/11/inside-our-new-governors-race-poll-00822422) [Tier 2].

### Comparison to Prior SPI Elections
- **2018 SPI:** Thurmond raised approximately $3.1 million directly for the June primary per [FPPC June 2018 Primary](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2018-primary-election/); total IE support exceeded $12.9 million per [FPPC November 2018 General](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/transparency/top-contributors/nov-18-gen.html).
- **2022 SPI:** Direct fundraising not separately itemized in available sources; IE support committee raised $2.2 million in the primary per [FPPC June 2022](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2022-primary-election/). He won with 63.7%.
- **Key contrast:** In 2018 and 2022, labor IEs functioned as his financial backbone. In 2026, CTA and the California Federation of Labor Unions have withheld endorsement (CTA endorsed Steyer; Cal Fed endorsed Steyer/Porter/Villaraigosa/Swalwell), eliminating the labor IE firepower that powered his prior wins.

---

**Critical observation — CTA and CFT absent from 2026 governor committee:** The California Teachers Association and California Federation of Teachers — Thurmond's historical financial backbone — do **not** appear among documented 2026 governor committee donors. CTA endorsed Tom Steyer on April 14, 2026 ([CTA press release](https://www.cta.org/press-release/california-teachers-association-recommends-tom-steyer-for-california-state-governor)), and CFT has not publicly backed Thurmond for governor. The California Federation of Labor Unions endorsed Steyer, Porter, Villaraigosa, and the now-withdrawn Swalwell — explicitly leaving Thurmond out — per [Cal Fed March 2026 press release](https://calaborfed.org/press-releases/california-federation-of-labor-unions-endorse-for-governor-and-other-statewide-races-for-2026-primary-election/).

**Building trades / IBEW alignment:** Thurmond's institutional donor base in 2026 pivots toward building trades unions (IBEW, Boilermakers, Plumbers/Steamfitters) rather than teacher unions. IBEW Local 302 and Local 952 have formally endorsed him ([tonythurmond.com/endorsements](https://www.tonythurmond.com/endorsements)).

**Tribal donors:** Two federally recognized tribal gaming entities — Habematolel Pomo of Upper Lake and Pala Band of Mission Indians / Pala Casino — each gave the maximum $36,400. Tribal political giving in California is generally independent of the education-union coalition and reflects broader progressive/Democratic alignment.

**School vendor — All City Management Services Inc:** This firm provides school crossing guards, security, and school safety staffing to K-12 districts, giving it a direct financial interest in CDE and SPI policy decisions, including those made by Thurmond. Its $36,000 contribution (just under the per-election limit) is a potential conflict-of-interest flag. [Tier 2 — needs primary verification on vendor relationship with CDE]

**Donor note — CTA snub significance:** In 2018, CTA ran $8+ million in IE support for Thurmond. In 2026, it not only withheld that support but endorsed his rival, citing Steyer's Prop. 13 reform promise and picket-line solidarity. The 2025 Politico investigation into a toxic CDE workplace ([Politico, September 2021](https://www.politico.com/states/california/story/2021/09/28/california-schools-chief-churns-through-top-aides-in-allegedly-toxic-workplace-1391461)) likely damaged his relationship with CTA leadership, though the union did not cite this publicly.

## 5. INDEPENDENT EXPENDITURES

### IEs FOR Thurmond

**2018 SPI Campaign:**
- *Educators Supporting Tony Thurmond for Superintendent of Public Instruction 2018, sponsored by teachers and school employees organizations* — Total IE support: **$12,989,175**, making him one of the highest IE recipients for a down-ballot statewide office that cycle per [FPPC November 2018 General](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/transparency/top-contributors/nov-18-gen.html). A November 2025 memo circulated by Thurmond's network described this as "the most of any down-ballot Democrat running for statewide office that election cycle" ([Scribd Thurmond memo](https://www.scribd.com/document/950724148/Thurmond-memo)) [Tier 2].

**2022 SPI Primary:**
- *Californians Supporting Tony Thurmond for Superintendent of Public Instruction 2022* (Committee ID: 1448022), sponsored by teacher, school employee and labor organizations. Top donors:
  1. California Teachers Association Independent Expenditure Committee — **$1,175,000**
  2. PACE of California School Employees Association (CSEA) Local, State, Federal Candidates — **$500,000**
  3. California Federation of Teachers COPE — **$200,000**
  4. American Federation of Teachers, AFL-CIO COPE — **$150,000**
  5. Million More Voters (sponsored by California Labor Federation) — **$100,000**
  6. California State Council of Service Employees — **$75,000**
  - **Total: $2,200,000** per [FPPC June 2022 Primary](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2022-primary-election/)

**2022 SPI General:**
- CTA IE Committee, SEIU state council, SEIU UHW West PAC, SEIU Local 521 IE Committee again supported him per [FPPC November 2022 Top Two Donors](https://lunar.fppc.ca.gov/transparency/top-contributors/nov-22-gen/Top_Two_Donors.html). Specific amounts not fully extracted from the FPPC page; full filing amounts require direct Cal-Access query (see DATA GAPS).

**2026 Governor Campaign:**
- **No significant IE activity found** as of April 29, 2026. No pro-Thurmond IE committee has been identified in available public sources. This represents a catastrophic contrast with 2018 and 2022, when labor IEs dwarfed Thurmond's own fundraising.

### IEs AGAINST Thurmond

**2018 and 2022 SPI:** Charter-school-aligned money targeted his opponent (Marshall Tuck) rather than running direct negative IEs against Thurmond. Charter advocates spent approximately $62 million in the 2018 election cycle across governor and SPI races, mostly in support of Villaraigosa (governor) and Tuck (SPI), not through negative Thurmond IEs, per [LAist November 2018](https://laist.com/news/charter-school-advocates-were-this-years-biggest-election-spenders-they-still-lost-the-two-biggest-r). CCSA Advocates (California Charter Schools Association) spending against Thurmond directly was not confirmed in primary sources; the 2018 charter spending was overwhelmingly structured as pro-Tuck IE rather than anti-Thurmond. [Tier 2 note: task brief stated CCSA Advocates spent against him in 2018 and 2022 — this warrants primary FPPC verification; not confirmed in documents reviewed.]

**2026 Governor Campaign:**
- No anti-Thurmond IE committee identified. His 1% polling position may have rendered targeted opposition spending unnecessary.
- A notable anti-Steyer IE (funded by realtors, construction industry, IBEW, and PG&E) has spent $14+ million in the 2026 governor race targeting Steyer, not Thurmond per [JPR April 2026](https://www.ijpr.org/politics-government/2026-04-27/billionaire-blitz-steyers-132-million-campaign-dwarfs-rivals-in-california-governor-race).

---

## 6. DONOR OVERLAPS AND CONTRADICTIONS

### Thurmond vs. Villaraigosa: The Charter School Fault Line
The starkest financial contrast in the 2026 governor field replays the 2018 SPI dynamic: charter-school money backed Villaraigosa (then for governor) and Tuck (for SPI), while teacher-union money backed Newsom (governor) and Thurmond (SPI). In 2018, charter advocates including Reed Hastings (Netflix founder) and Michael Bloomberg contributed to a $17+ million IE for Villaraigosa per [CBS SF, May 2018](https://www.cbsnews.com/sanfrancisco/news/charter-schools-vs-teachers-unions-governor-superintendent/). In 2026, Villaraigosa's donors include building and construction trades and public safety groups ([Villaraigosa campaign announcement](https://www.antonio2026.com/news/villaraigosas-61-million-raised-leads-fundraising-in-ca-governors-race)) [Tier 2], while Thurmond's teacher-union base has defected to Steyer. **The 2018 Thurmond-vs.-Tuck war chest disparity has effectively re-materialized as a Steyer-vs.-field dynamic in 2026.**

### IBEW Overlap
IBEW locals appear in both Thurmond's and Villaraigosa's donor profiles. IBEW Local 302 PAC gave $36,400 to Thurmond for Governor 2026; the broader IBEW apparatus was also part of the anti-Steyer IE per [JPR April 2026](https://www.ijpr.org/politics-government/2026-04-27/billionaire-blitz-steyers-132-million-campaign-dwarfs-rivals-in-california-governor-race). The building trades are somewhat split.

### All City Management Services — Conflict Flag
All City Management Services Inc., a school safety/crossing-guard contractor, gave $36,000 to Thurmond for Governor 2026. As SPI, Thurmond's department oversees certification and regulatory frameworks touching school safety vendors who contract with local districts. The donation creates at minimum an optics conflict even if no direct regulatory decision is demonstrable. [Tier 2 — needs primary verification of any CDE contracts or certification decisions involving All City Management Services]

### Platform Contradiction: Teacher-Union Candidate Without Teacher-Union Money
Thurmond campaigns explicitly as a champion of public school teachers and positions himself as anti-charter-choice. Yet the California Teachers Association — which spent $8+ million electing him SPI in 2018 — chose a billionaire hedge fund manager (Steyer) over him for governor, citing corporate tax reform as the deciding issue. This undercuts the "labor champion" narrative at the core of his brand.

---

The Cal Fed endorsed four candidates in March 2026 — none of them Thurmond ([Cal Fed March 2026](https://calaborfed.org/press-releases/california-federation-of-labor-unions-endorse-for-governor-and-other-statewide-races-for-2026-primary-election/)). These are the two organizations that functioned as his political machine; their defection is existential.

### Family Income

Thurmond himself earned $203,000 (SPI salary) + $18,000 from Integrated Community Services (a San Rafael disability nonprofit where he worked as a supportive living aide) in 2025, per [CalMatters March 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/03/tax-returns-governor-candidates/).

---

## 8. POLICY-FOR-MONEY (ABBREVIATED)

The clearest documented alignment between Thurmond's donor base and policy decisions involves K-12 labor relations and charter school regulation. As SPI, Thurmond maintained a consistently anti-charter-expansion posture that directly served his CTA/CFT donor coalition: opposing moves to relax charter authorization standards and deprioritizing charter oversight reform that the CTA opposed. However, CTA's 2026 defection to Steyer suggests the union's satisfaction with Thurmond's SPI tenure did not translate into gubernatorial support — Steyer's Prop. 13 commercial property tax reform commitment was the decisive factor ([CTA press release](https://www.cta.org/press-release/california-teachers-association-recommends-tom-steyer-for-california-state-governor)). A secondary alignment exists with Thurmond's solicitation of a $10,000 behested payment from Tim Ranzetta — whose nonprofit secured Thurmond's support for AB 2927 (financial literacy requirement) the same day — though Thurmond denied any coordination ([CalMatters, April 2025](https://calmatters.org/politics/2025/04/schools-superintendent-side-jobs/)). COVID school reopening decisions were primarily driven by Newsom and public health authorities; Thurmond's KQED interview acknowledged the state "probably could have gotten schools open a little sooner" ([KQED, March 2026](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=os2IfgCqMEI)).

---

## 9. DARK MONEY

### 501(c)(4) / LLC Donors

**Kamilos Companies LLC — $36,400:** An LLC giving the maximum contribution to a state candidate triggers Cal-Access disclosure requirements (LLCs must identify the responsible individual). The public TransparencyUSA page does not resolve the underlying beneficial owner. [Tier 2 — needs Cal-Access Form 460 Schedule A verification of LLC disclosure compliance]

**Historical pro-charter dark money targeting Thurmond:** In the 2018 SPI race, charter-school advocates deployed dark money-adjacent 501(c)(4) vehicles. The CCSA Advocates (California Charter Schools Association's political arm) and associated groups funded IEs supporting Tuck rather than running direct 501(c)(4) campaigns against Thurmond per [LAist 2018](https://laist.com/news/charter-school-advocates-were-this-years-biggest-election-spenders-they-still-lost-the-two-biggest-r). The $62 million total charter spend in 2018 flowed primarily through disclosed IE committees rather than true dark money, limiting the 501(c)(4) signature. No dark money 501(c)(4) operation targeting Thurmond in 2026 has been identified in public sources.

**2026 anti-Steyer dark money:** The dominant dark money/opaque-money activity in the 2026 governor race targets Steyer — a multi-million-dollar coalition of realtors, construction industry, IBEW, and PG&E — not Thurmond. Thurmond's 1% polling position has not attracted significant dark money opposition.

**No pro-Thurmond 501(c)(4) activity identified** for the 2026 cycle. His 2022 SPI IEs were structured as formally disclosed "sponsored" IE committees, not 501(c)(4) dark money.

---

## 10. ENFORCEMENT AND LEGAL

### FPPC Warning Letter (2024)
The FPPC issued Thurmond a **warning letter in 2024** for violating behested payment reporting regulations — specifically, failing to report on time a November 2022 payment from **Pacific Gas & Electric Company (PG&E)** of **$10,000** to Josie's Place (a grief support program run by the San Francisco Study Center, where Thurmond was then employed as development manager). Thurmond did not report the payment until February 2024 — more than a year after the 30-day disclosure deadline — per [CalMatters, April 2025](https://calmatters.org/politics/2025/04/schools-superintendent-side-jobs/) and [CalMatters campaign violations investigation, October 2024](https://calmatters.org/show-your-work/2024/10/how-we-reported-on-california-campaign-violations/). The case was closed with a warning rather than a fine. The FPPC enforcement database (direct access) did not return a named Thurmond entry, consistent with warning-letter resolutions often not appearing as formal fine cases.

**Key facts:**
- PG&E gave $10,000 at Thurmond's request to a nonprofit that was simultaneously paying Thurmond's salary.
- Thurmond claimed he submitted the grant application in his nonprofit capacity, not as SPI; PG&E declined to confirm.
- The FPPC closure as a warning (not fine) reflects mitigating factors but does not exonerate the underlying conduct.

### Unpaid 2014 Campaign Fine
As of a 2021 CalMatters investigation, Thurmond owed $550 from a 2014 Assembly campaign for a late filing, which his spokesperson characterized as a "clerical error" and said would be immediately paid per [CalMatters, April 2021](https://calmatters.org/politics/2021/04/california-unpaid-campaigns-fines/). [Tier 2 — payment not verified via primary FPPC records]

### State Auditor Findings (CDE Hiring, 2020)
The California State Auditor's Office flagged the Department of Education's hiring practices in a 2020 audit for "improper activities," finding unnamed senior managers worked to "quickly hire" a pre-selected contractor and approved "an inflated salary." CDE disputed some but not all findings per [Politico, September 2021](https://www.politico.com/states/california/story/2021/09/28/california-schools-chief-churns-through-top-aides-in-allegedly-toxic-workplace-1391461). No individual was named in the audit; it was framed as an institutional, not personal, violation.

### Toxic Workplace Allegations (Politico, 2021)
Politico reported in September 2021 that nearly **two dozen senior CDE officials** had departed since 2019, with multiple former employees describing a toxic workplace in which Thurmond allegedly humiliated and intimidated staff, demanded loyalty oaths ("all in on Team Thurmond"), and retaliated against dissenters per [Politico, September 2021](https://www.politico.com/states/california/story/2021/09/28/california-schools-chief-churns-through-top-aides-in-allegedly-toxic-workplace-1391461). Thurmond denied the characterization. This is not a campaign finance matter but represents significant governance reputational risk.

### No FPPC Formal Fine or Criminal Matter
No formal FPPC administrative fine or criminal referral to the AG for Thurmond was located in the documents reviewed.

---

## 11. PRIOR OFFICE DONOR HISTORY (ABBREVIATED)

Thurmond's donor coalition has been remarkably consistent across four elections. As an Assembly candidate in AD-15 in 2014, he benefited from over $250,000 in IE support from big oil and tobacco companies alongside labor backing per [East Bay Express, May 2018](https://eastbayexpress.com/pac-money-invades-15th-district-assembly-race-2-1/) [Tier 2], and held a perfect 100% California Labor Federation scorecard per [Thurmond campaign memo, November 2025](https://www.scribd.com/document/950724148/Thurmond-memo) [Tier 2]. For his 2018 SPI run, CTA spent $8+ million against Marshall Tuck (the charter-backed opponent), forming the template for a union-funded SPI candidacy; aggregate support reached $12.9 million. In 2022, CTA ($1.175M), CSEA ($500K), CFT ($200K), AFT ($150K), Cal Fed ($100K), and SEIU state council ($75K) combined for $2.2 million in the primary alone. The continuity is striking: the same three labor umbrella organizations (CTA, CFT/AFT, SEIU) funded every winning Thurmond race from 2018 through 2022, underwriting what was effectively a labor-operated candidacy. Their collective defection to Steyer and other candidates in 2026 — while Thurmond pivots to smaller building-trades locals, tribal gaming money, and Bay Area philanthropists — illustrates how structurally dependent his political career has been on the K-12 teacher union infrastructure.

---

## 12. CONTEXT AND JOURNALIST-READY STORY ANGLES

### Angle 1: The Union That Made Him Is Now His Biggest Problem
The California Teachers Association spent at least **$9 million over two SPI campaigns** to elect Tony Thurmond, making him the most union-financed down-ballot statewide candidate in California's recent history. In 2026, CTA endorsed billionaire Tom Steyer instead — despite Thurmond being the only SPI incumbent ever to run for governor, the candidate most organizationally dependent on CTA's machine, and the person who spent 6 years executing CTA's policy agenda (anti-charter, pro-union contracts, COVID school closures aligned with union preferences). The story goes beyond who CTA endorsed: it involves why Thurmond — after faithfully executing the union's education agenda — could not convert that relationship into gubernatorial endorsement money. Sources: [CTA April 14, 2026 press release](https://www.cta.org/press-release/california-teachers-association-recommends-tom-steyer-for-california-state-governor); [Cal Fed March 2026 endorsements](https://calaborfed.org/press-releases/california-federation-of-labor-unions-endorse-for-governor-and-other-statewide-races-for-2026-primary-election/); [Politico September 2021 toxic workplace investigation](https://www.politico.com/states/california/story/2021/09/28/california-schools-chief-churns-through-top-aides-in-allegedly-toxic-workplace-1391461).

### Angle 2: The Behested-Payment Loop — Nonprofit Salary, Donor Solicitations, and PG&E
Thurmond held multiple paid nonprofit side jobs simultaneously with his $200,000+ SPI position, then solicited contributions to those same nonprofits from people and entities with business before his office. PG&E gave $10,000 at his request to a nonprofit paying his salary; Thurmond failed to report it for over a year, drawing an FPPC warning. Tim Ranzetta — whose nonprofit lobbied for a financial literacy graduation requirement that Thurmond then announced support for on the same day Ranzetta donated $10,000 to a Thurmond-run nonprofit — says he was unaware Thurmond was employed by the food pantry. The pattern raises structural questions about California's behested payment loophole: officials can legally ask donors to give to their own employers. The Governor's race amplifies this: should the state's next chief executive be someone whose SPI tenure generated two documented behested-payment conflicts? Sources: [CalMatters April 2025 investigation](https://calmatters.org/politics/2025/04/schools-superintendent-side-jobs/); [CalMatters October 2024 FPPC investigation](https://calmatters.org/show-your-work/2024/10/how-we-reported-on-california-campaign-violations/).

### Angle 3: A Department in Chaos — The CDE Exodus and What It Signals About Executive Competence
Politico documented nearly two dozen senior CDE departures in Thurmond's first three years, multiple former staff comparing the office to an "abusive relationship," and the California State Auditor flagging improper hiring practices. Thurmond burned through three directors of communications in under three years and has had three chief deputy superintendents since 2019 — the number-two role with a $220,000+ salary — despite market compensation that should aid retention. For a candidate running on managerial competence and education expertise, the documented CDE organizational dysfunction is a directly relevant test case. The 2026 governor race is partly a referendum on whether statewide executive-branch management matters; any debate or background investigation will surface the Politico findings and the auditor's report. Sources: [Politico September 2021](https://www.politico.com/states/california/story/2021/09/28/california-schools-chief-churns-through-top-aides-in-allegedly-toxic-workplace-1391461); [California State Auditor findings via Politico]; [CalMatters March 2026 tax return analysis](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/03/tax-returns-governor-candidates/).

Direct Cal-Access query at `cal-access.sos.ca.gov` returned a robots-disallow error. Committee ID #1471635 is confirmed from the NGP VAN payment page disclosure line. ### 2026 IE Committee Operating in His Orbit
**Straight From the Heart of California**
- **Cal-Access ID:** [#1486030](https://theballotbook.com/campaign_finance/committees/20271/receipts) (first filed March 18, 2026)
- **Type:** Statewide Independent Expenditure committee
- **Purpose:** Elect Villaraigosa governor
- **Total received:** ~$800,000 as of last available filing

- **FPPC top-10 list (June 2026 primary):** Villaraigosa does **not** appear on the FPPC's published top-10 contributors list for the June 2026 primary as of the last update reviewed; this likely reflects that IE spending on his behalf has not crossed the threshold triggering mandatory large-donor disclosure under the top-10 list, or that the list had not been updated to include this committee [FPPC June 2026 Primary](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/)
- **Website:** straightfromtheheartofcalifornia.com [Tier 2 — needs primary verification]

### 2018 Governor's Race Committee (Predecessor)
**Elect Villaraigosa Governor of California 2018**
- Total raised (campaign committee): ~$7.8 million [MapLight, archived](https://maplightarchive.org/story/charter-school-advocates-spend-record-high-in-ca-governors-race/)
- **Note on multi-cycle issues:** The 2018 committee transferred $100,000 into the 2018 "Families & Teachers" IE committee ([FPPC 2018 top contributors](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2018-primary-election/)), a transaction that generated a FEC enforcement matter (MUR 7522) related to the IE committee's $25,000 slate-mailer payment to Maxine Waters' federal committee — an excessive contribution under federal law. [FEC Statement of Reasons, MUR 7522](https://www.fec.gov/files/legal/murs/7522/7522_15.pdf) — **this is the primary multi-cycle compliance issue on record for the 2018 cycle.**
- Villaraigosa's 2026 campaign prominently touts "no transfers" as distinguishing him from rivals who moved funds from prior committees (e.g., Becerra's transfer from a congressional account) [Tier 2 — campaign press release, January 5, 2026](https://www.antonio2026.com/news/villaraigosas-61-million-raised-leads-fundraising-in-ca-governors-race). **CAL-ACCESS VERIFICATION STATUS:** Primary source (Form 460 filings) not retrieved due to access block; "no transfer" claim cannot be independently verified at Tier-1 from this research session.

### Burn Rate Analysis
- Expenditures ($3.9M) exceed contributions on record ($3.18M) in the cycle shown by TransparencyUSA — suggesting cumulative spend exceeds the current-cycle reporting window or the committee is burning legacy cash.
- Q1 2026 raise was only $707,000, while he raised ~$2M in H2 2025 and ~$4.3M cumulatively through August 2025. **The burn rate is accelerating relative to intake** — a significant red flag entering the final six weeks before the June 2 primary [CalMatters, April 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-race-financials/).

## 6. DONOR OVERLAPS + CONTRADICTIONS

### Cross-Candidate Overlaps (2026)
- **Reed Hastings** ($7M to Villaraigosa 2018 IE) gave **$1M to Mahan's IE** in 2026 [FPPC June 2026 list](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/) — a clear shift of charter-school billionaire money away from Villaraigosa and toward Mahan.
- **Rick Caruso**: The Real Deal (Oct 2025) noted Caruso "may or may not run" and did not list him as a Villaraigosa donor. Caruso gave $1.5M to Mahan's IE per the FPPC 2026 list. No confirmed Villaraigosa 2026 donation from Caruso.
- **California Resources Corporation** gave to Villaraigosa ($39,200+) while also appearing as a Becerra donor in past cycles. CRC is California's largest oil producer.
- **Govern for California Courage Committee** ($36,400) gave to Villaraigosa but is a tech-friendly ed-reform PAC typically associated with charter advocates who are more heavily invested in Mahan in 2026.

### Key Structural Contradictions

1. **Labor-friendly branding vs. oil/fossil fuel money:** Villaraigosa presents as a pro-labor, pro-worker candidate but accepted $39,200+ from Chevron, $39,200+ from CRC, and $39,200+ from Marathon in the 2026 cycle. He also violated a 2018 pledge to not accept fossil fuel contributions. Building trades unions — which represent workers in refineries — are his primary labor base, creating an alignment between his oil-friendly positioning and their job interests, but this contradicts his environmental record as mayor. [LA Times, May 26, 2025](https://www.latimes.com/politics/story/2025-05-26/oil-villaraigosa-fossil-fuel-governors-race)

2. **Charter-school money past vs. 2026 absence:** In 2018, $15.6M in charter-school billionaire money (Hastings, Broad, Bloomberg, Oberndorf) made Villaraigosa the darling of the ed-reform movement. In 2026, this money has largely migrated to Mahan. Villaraigosa's education rhetoric has moderated accordingly, though he continues to support charter schools in principle.

3. **Real estate developer money + housing affordability platform:** Villaraigosa's top individual donors include real estate executives (Rappaport, Moinian, Witte/Related, Alagem, Meldman/Discovery Land, Meruelo Group) while his platform calls for $25B in housing bonds and CEQA reform that would benefit the same developer class. Critics of Measure ULA (a LA mansion tax) specifically cited Villaraigosa's opposition as a selling point — Luchs at Newmark directly credited Villaraigosa's call about real estate as his reason for donating.

4. **Post-mayor consulting conflicts now in political orbit:** Donors from his Actum LLC consulting work (Kirill Goncharenko, $36,400) and corporate advisory roles feed directly into his 2026 campaign. Actum's clients included California Charter Schools Association, Westlands Water District, and others [LA Times, Oct 2021](https://www.latimes.com/politics/story/2021-10-07/former-elected-leaders-nunez-boxer-villaraigosa-mercury-public-affairs). These relationships are not disclosed in campaign finance as they preceded the campaign, but represent an embedded interest network.

---

## 7. NETWORK + RELATIONSHIPS

### Key Endorsers with Financial Ties
- **State Building & Construction Trades Council of CA:** Both endorser and top institutional donor ($78,400+). Endorsed Oct 2025 [antonio2026.com, Oct 20, 2025](https://www.antonio2026.com/news/villaraigosa-wins-california-state-building-and-construction-trades-endorsement).
- **LA/OC Building & Construction Trades Council:** Endorsed Feb 4, 2026; represents 14 trades, 48 unions, 160,000+ skilled laborers [Yahoo Finance/Globe Newswire, Feb 6, 2026](https://finance.yahoo.com/news/la-oc-building-construction-trades-210400929.html).
- **PORAC PAC** (law enforcement): Both endorser and $39,200 donor.
- **California Labor Federation:** Four-way endorsement (Steyer, Swalwell, Villaraigosa, Porter), March 16, 2026 [CA Labor Federation](https://calaborfed.org/press-releases/california-federation-of-labor-unions-endorse-for-governor-and-other-statewide-races-for-2026-primary-election/).
- **Karen Bass (LA Mayor):** Endorsed Villaraigosa; donated $1,046. Long political alliance.

### Staff and Consulting Network
- **Josh Pulliam:** Chief strategist (named in campaign press releases) [Tier 2].
- **Raquel Robinson:** Communications Director [Tier 2 — campaign releases].
- **Michael Trujillo:** Longtime Villaraigosa aide, now working on outside Straight From the Heart IE committee. Also a high-profile Democratic consultant who publicly worked on LA mayoral races and attacked Swalwell. [Politico, April 2026](https://www.politico.com/news/2026/04/13/influencers-allegations-eric-swalwell-00869517)
- **Kirill Goncharenko (Actum LLC):** Founding partner at Actum LLC, where Villaraigosa was a principal until stepping away to run. Goncharenko donated $36,400 to the 2026 campaign. [O'Dwyers, Jan 2022](https://www.odwyerpr.com/story/public/17416/2022-01-27/ex-mercury-pa-staffers-open-actum-llc.html)
- **Fabian Nuñez:** Former Assembly Speaker who left Mercury with Villaraigosa in 2021 and co-founded Actum. No confirmed 2026 donation found.
- **Barbara Boxer:** Co-chaired Actum's LA office with Villaraigosa. No confirmed 2026 donation found.
- **Jim DeBoo:** Newsom's former chief of staff who approached Villaraigosa for the infrastructure czar role in 2022. No confirmed 2026 financial connection.

### Family / Political Family
- **Corina Raigosa:** Ex-wife; they divorced circa 1994. Name formed by combining their surnames; no confirmed political consulting or lobbying role identified.
- **Patricia/Patty Villarreal:** Identified in some sources as current partner; no confirmed financial or political role confirmed in public records.
- **Marisela Villaraigosa (daughter):** No confirmed lobbying or consulting role surfaced.
- **Ricardo Olivos (brother):** Named in research tasking as potentially having consulting history; **no public record found confirming Ricardo Olivos in a paid consulting capacity connected to Villaraigosa's campaigns.** DATA GAP.
- **Michelle Nunez:** (Not a family member despite the name.) Donated $72,800 (two entries) listed employer as Belle Reve Theatre Company. Connection unclear — possibly a close ally. [SomaliScan](https://www.somaliscan.com/donations/recipient/Antonio%20Villaraigosa%20for%20Governor%202026)

### Former Staff Now Lobbying
- **Actum LLC:** Multiple Villaraigosa-connected consultants at Actum — which handles lobbying and public affairs for corporate clients — now lobby at the state level. After Villaraigosa stepped away to run for governor, [Politico noted, Nov 2024](https://www.politico.com/news/2024/11/18/actum-california-lobbying-firm-unions-00190083) that Actum acquired a California lobbying firm with strong union ties. This creates a network where Actum clients may feel an incentive to support Villaraigosa's political career.
- **Mercury Public Affairs:** Villaraigosa was at Mercury from Nov 2018 to Oct 2021 [Politico, Nov 2018](https://www.politico.com/story/2018/11/12/antonio-villaraigosa-lobbyist-mercury-984940). Mercury's client list during that period included California Charter Schools Association, Westlands Water District, governments of Ethiopia, Haiti, and — controversially — a Ukrainian oligarch-funded nonprofit, which triggered a FARA investigation. Mercury lost clients; Villaraigosa and others resigned [LA Times, Oct 2021](https://www.latimes.com/politics/story/2021-10-07/former-elected-leaders-nunez-boxer-villaraigosa-mercury-public-affairs).

---

## 8. POLICY-FOR-MONEY

### LA Mayor (2005–2013)

**Billboard Deal (Clear Channel/CBS Outdoor, 2006)**
The LA City Council — under Villaraigosa's tenure — approved a 2006 legal settlement with Clear Channel and CBS Outdoor allowing conversion of 840 static billboards to digital format in exchange for removing other static signs. The deal was subsequently ruled illegal and "poison" by the LA Superior Court (Judge Terry Green, 2009). An appellate court later struck down the settlement (2012). The deal was described by city officials (including Eric Garcetti) as a major regret. Villaraigosa and the council were accused of not reading the settlement carefully. Clear Channel later threatened the city with a $100M+ lawsuit when ordered to turn off signs [LA Times, Feb 2013](https://www.latimes.com/local/la-xpm-2013-feb-23-la-me-billboard-threat-20130224-story.html); [PBS SoCal/SoCal Connected, Nov 2012](https://www.pbssocal.org/shows/socal-connected/clip/billboard-confidential-update-l-a-city-council-allowed-illegal-billboards-to-be-erected). Clear Channel and billboard companies spent millions lobbying City Hall during Villaraigosa's tenure. **No direct contribution from Clear Channel to Villaraigosa's personal campaign accounts confirmed** in records retrieved; the billboard industry's lobbying network was a systemic city hall issue rather than an identified direct campaign donation during his mayoralty.

**Grand Avenue Project / Eli Broad**
Villaraigosa and Eli Broad were closely aligned on the Grand Avenue Project, a major downtown LA mixed-use redevelopment. Broad was co-chair of the Grand Avenue Authority. Villaraigosa praised Broad's museum project ("anchor tenant for an area revitalizing") [Broad Foundation materials / Related Companies press](https://www.related.com/news-articles/2011/01/06/billionaire-unveils-design-downtown-la-museum/). Broad subsequently gave $3.525M to Villaraigosa's 2018 IE committee. The Grand Avenue Project has included Related Companies (developer) throughout — Bill Witte (Related California) donated $5,000 to Villaraigosa's 2026 campaign.

**Oil Money in Mayoral Era**
T. Boone Pickens donated $150,000 in 2008 to a city proposition backed by Villaraigosa (a phone/internet tax) while Pickens' company was vying for business at the Port of LA. More than $582,000 in fossil-fuel industry contributions and other financial support flowed to Villaraigosa's political accounts and affiliated causes during his mayoral years [LA Times, May 2025](https://www.latimes.com/politics/story/2025-05-26/oil-villaraigosa-fossil-fuel-governors-race).

**Alexander Hugh Alleged Money Laundering**
Koreatown developer Alexander Hugh allegedly laundered $18,000 for Villaraigosa's 2009 re-election campaign — making contributions under assumed names and exceeding the $1,000 per-person limit. Hugh pleaded not guilty to five felony counts. He had won approval from the mayor and council for a large hotel project over the planning commission's objections; the hotel was never built. The city Ethics Commission was expected to fine Hugh $180,000+ [CBS Los Angeles, Oct 2011](https://www.cbsnews.com/losangeles/news/villaraigosa-donor-faces-180k-fine-over-money-laundering-allegations/).

### 2018 Governor's Race
Villaraigosa received $15.6M from a charter-school IE committee sponsored by California Charter Schools Association Advocates. His explicit policy positions during the 2018 race aligned: he supported charter schools, opposed the teachers unions on several accountability measures, and positioned himself as an "education reform" Democrat. Gary Borden, executive director of CCSA Advocates, explicitly linked the $15M+ investment to Villaraigosa's pro-charter record [Daily Kos, May 2018](https://www.dailykos.com/stories/2018/5/19/1765594/community/CA-Gov-Pro-Charter-School-Billionaires-Are-Bankrolling-Antonio-Villaraigosa-s-D-Campaign/) [Tier 2]. Villaraigosa finished third in the June 2018 primary, failing to advance.

### Post-Mayor Consulting (2013–2024)

| Role | Entity | Period | Financial Details | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Senior Advisor | Banc of California | July 2013 | Salary not disclosed; part-time advisory to CEO Steven Sugarman | Bank expanding home/small business loans [LA Times, July 2013](https://www.latimes.com/local/la-xpm-2013-jul-16-la-me-villaraigosa-banking-20130717-story.html) |
| Senior Advisor | Herbalife Ltd. | Sept 2013 | Salary/terms not disclosed | Hired as Herbalife fought pyramid-scheme allegations; Villaraigosa praised company's Latino community ties [LA Times, Sept 2013](https://www.latimes.com/business/la-xpm-2013-sep-05-la-fi-villaraigosa-herbalife-20130906-story.html) |
| Senior Advisor | Edelman (PR firm) | Oct 2013 | Terms not disclosed | Simultaneous with Herbalife role; Edelman was advocating for an Herbalife investigation — a direct conflict of interest both parties claimed was managed by firewalling [LA Times, Oct 2013](https://www.latimes.com/business/la-fi-mo-does-villaraigosa-have-conflict-working-for-edelman-and-herbalife-20131022-story.html) |
| Co-Chairman | Mercury Public Affairs | Nov 2018–Oct 2021 | Salary not disclosed | Lobbied for charter schools, Westlands Water; Mercury investigated for FARA after Ukrainian oligarch connection [Politico, Nov 2018](https://www.politico.com/story/2018/11/12/antonio-villaraigosa-lobbyist-mercury-984940); [LA Times, Oct 2021](https://www.latimes.com/politics/story/2021-10-07/former-elected-leaders-nunez-boxer-villaraigosa-mercury-public-affairs) |
| Co-Chair, LA Office | Actum LLC | Jan 2022–mid 2025 | Salary not disclosed | Successor firm to Mercury; Actum acquired CA union lobbying firm in Nov 2024 [Politico, Nov 2024](https://www.politico.com/news/2024/11/18/actum-california-lobbying-firm-unions-00190083) |
| Infrastructure Czar | CA/Newsom (via California Forward nonprofit) | Aug 2022–approx. June 2023 | $381,820 ($35K/month + expenses) | Paid by nonprofit donors, not state; donors included Port of SD ($30K), SoCalGas ($17.5K), Disney/Edison/AT&T ($10K each) — interests in infrastructure policy; arrangement described as potential "clearinghouse" for special interests [LAist/CalMatters, June 2025](https://laist.com/brief/news/politics/newsom-gave-his-political-rival-a-380k-job-see-the-special-interests-who-paid-for-it) |
| Board Chair | The Change Company (CDFI) | Feb 2021–present | Not disclosed | Community development financial institution |
| Global Advisory Council | Coinbase | April 2024 | Not disclosed | Crypto exchange; advisory on regulatory framework [LA Times, April 2024](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2024-04-30/antonio-villaraigosa-coinbase-cryptocurrency-adviser) |

---

## 9. DARK MONEY + SHELL ENTITIES

### Known Opacity Points
1. **Straight From the Heart of California (IE, 2026):** The IE committee's donor list is not publicly itemized on its website or in retrieved records. Cal-Access ID #1486030 with $800K raised; donors remain unidentified in this research. Form 461 filings should be on Cal-Access but were not retrieved due to access block. **Mike Trujillo is associated with the committee** [Politico, April 2026]. **This is the most significant current dark-money concern.**

2. **California Forward / Infrastructure Czar Arrangement (2022–23):** The nonprofit that paid Villaraigosa $381,820 used a structure that legally avoided public disclosure of its donors. California Forward raised $118,800 from a dozen corporate donors — primarily regulated utilities and infrastructure interests (Port of SD, SoCalGas, Disney, Edison, AT&T) — but this was not required to be on any public disclosure form. CalMatters obtained the list by request only. Sean McMorris of California Common Cause described this as a "clearinghouse" that "buries true funding sources" [LAist/CalMatters, June 2025](https://laist.com/brief/news/politics/newsom-gave-his-political-rival-a-380k-job-see-the-special-interests-who-paid-for-it).

3. **JRJ Corporation and Prenton, Inc.:** These are among the largest institutional donors ($78,400 each) with no publicly identifiable business description found in this research session. **JRJ Corporation and Prenton Inc. are unexplained shell-adjacent entities in the donor list.** DATA GAP — further investigation required.

4. **COPE Healthcare Consulting, Inc.:** $78,400 (two max entries of $39,200 each). COPE Healthcare is a California-based consulting firm. Its principals and specific healthcare policy interests are not identified in retrieved records. DATA GAP.

5. **Mercury Public Affairs / FARA:** While Villaraigosa left Mercury in 2021, the firm had exposure to a FARA investigation for work tied to a Ukrainian oligarch-linked nonprofit. The nexus of foreign government clients and California political power at Mercury is documented in the LA Times' 2021 coverage but is retrospective — not a current 2026 issue. [LA Times, Oct 2021](https://www.latimes.com/politics/story/2021-10-07/former-elected-leaders-nunez-boxer-villaraigosa-mercury-public-affairs)

6. **LLC-structured real estate donations:** Multiple real estate donor entities in his filing (JRJ Corporation, Prenton Inc., Cordoba Corporation, Continental Development Corporation) are organized as corporations without publicly available ownership/principal information in the records reviewed. Real estate LLCs are a standard dark-money vector in California campaign finance.

**No confirmed 501(c)(4) organized specifically around Villaraigosa** for 2026 was identified.

---

## 10. ENFORCEMENT + LEGAL

### FPPC Enforcement History

| Year | Violation | Fine | Source |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2001 Mayor's Race | Accepted six contributions exceeding the $1,000 limit per person | $5,100 settlement (December 2003) | [LA Times, May 2007](https://www.latimes.com/archives/la-xpm-2007-may-02-me-mayor2-story.html) |
| 2003 City Council Campaign | 31 violations: excess contributions from Bruce Corwin and Alan Rothenberg; 23 failures to file campaign literature; exceeded $150,000 non-individual contribution limit by ~$39,000 | Proposed ~$40,000 settlement; maximum exposure $267,000 | [LA Times, May 2007](https://www.latimes.com/archives/la-xpm-2007-may-02-me-mayor2-story.html) |
| 2005–2010 (SEI Gift Violations) | Failed to report 21+ gifts (sports tickets, entertainment) on annual Statements of Economic Interest | **FPPC fine: $21,000; LA City Ethics Commission fine: $20,849; Combined: ~$41,849** | [FPPC 2012 enforcement report](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/siteassets/documents/agendadocuments/executive-staff-reports/2012/march/41endoftheyrreport.pdf); [LA Times, April 2011](https://www.latimes.com/archives/la-xpm-2011-apr-01-la-mem-villaraigosa-pays-fine-20110401-story.html) |

**FPPC penalty summary:** Villaraigosa faced maximum potential exposure of $167,000+ on the gift matter, reduced to ~$42,000 because violations were deemed unintentional. He admitted failure to report free tickets to 34 events over five years (Lakers games, concerts, etc.) [NBC News, April 2011](https://www.nbcnews.com/id/wbna42383731); [ABC7, April 2011](https://abc7.com/archive/8067412/).

### Alexander Hugh / Money Laundering (2009 Re-election)
Developer Alexander Hugh allegedly contributed $18,000 to Villaraigosa's 2009 re-election campaign under assumed names, circumventing contribution limits. Hugh pleaded not guilty to five felony counts. The alleged scheme followed Hugh winning approval from Villaraigosa and the city council for a Koreatown hotel project over planning commission objections. Hugh faced a potential $180,000+ Ethics Commission fine in addition to the criminal charges [CBS Los Angeles, Oct 2011](https://www.cbsnews.com/losangeles/news/villaraigosa-donor-faces-180k-fine-over-money-laundering-allegations/). **Villaraigosa was not charged in this matter; Hugh was the respondent.**

### FEC Enforcement (2018 IE Committee)
The "Families & Teachers for Antonio Villaraigosa for Governor 2018" IE committee made a $25,000 payment to the Maxine Waters federal campaign committee (Citizens for Waters) as a slate-mailer reimbursement — deemed an excessive contribution under federal law. FEC closed MUR 7522 against the committee and Waters committee. [FEC MUR 7522](https://www.fec.gov/files/legal/murs/7522/7522_15.pdf) — Villaraigosa's campaign committee was not a respondent.

### Oil Pledge Violation (2025–2026)
Environmental groups (Climate Hawks Vote) allege Villaraigosa violated a 2018 campaign pledge not to accept fossil-fuel contributions by accepting $100,000+ from California Resources Corp., Berry Corp., and Excalibur Well Services in 2025. Villaraigosa disputes this interpretation, noting he did not sign the 2026 version of the pledge [LA Times, May 2025](https://www.latimes.com/politics/story/2025-05-26/oil-villaraigosa-fossil-fuel-governors-race). This is a reputational/political matter, not a legal enforcement action.

## 11. PRIOR-OFFICE DONOR HISTORY

### CA State Assembly (1994–2000, including Speaker 1998–2000)

Key donors in the Assembly Speaker era (1998–1999):
- **Zenith Insurance / Stanley Zax:** $100,000 to Villaraigosa as Assembly Speaker [LA Times, April 1999](https://www.latimes.com/archives/la-xpm-1999-apr-18-mn-28692-story.html)
- **Jerry Perenchio (TV mogul):** $100,000 to Villaraigosa as Assembly Speaker [LA Times, April 1999](https://www.latimes.com/archives/la-xpm-1999-apr-18-mn-28692-story.html)
- **Ron Burkle and entities:** $1.8M total to state politics in 1998; gave to Villaraigosa as Speaker (specific amount not confirmed in records retrieved)
- **Reed Hastings:** Active CA donor in 1998 charter school era; gave to Villaraigosa (specific amount not confirmed in records retrieved)

**Pattern:** As Assembly Speaker, Villaraigosa was a conduit for major Democratic donor money — insurance (Zenith, $100K), entertainment (Perenchio, $100K), and business broadly.

### LA City Council (2003–2005)
- Ethics violations (31 counts) from 2003 campaign as noted in Section 10
- Donors included theater chain owner Bruce Corwin and attorney/appointee Alan Rothenberg

### LA Mayor (2005–2013)

**Key donor network from mayoral fundraising:**
- Over $582,000 from fossil-fuel industry over his mayoral years (campaign accounts and affiliated committees)
- T. Boone Pickens: $150,000 (2008 city proposition, while company vied for port business)
- Alexander Hugh: Alleged $18,000 illegal contribution (2009)
- Free tickets: 34 events valued at triggering FPPC investigation; $42,000 combined fine

**Mayor's Fund / nonprofits:** Villaraigosa used affiliated nonprofits (after-school programs, anti-violence initiatives, sports/entertainment commission) as recipient vehicles for oil-industry and other donations that did not route through his campaign committee. This is noted in the LA Times fossil fuel investigation [LA Times, May 2025](https://www.latimes.com/politics/story/2025-05-26/oil-villaraigosa-fossil-fuel-governors-race).

### 2018 Governor's Race
- Campaign committee raised ~$7.8M
- IE committee ("Families & Teachers") raised $15.6M+
- Top IE donors: Reed Hastings ($7M), William Oberndorf ($3.75M), Eli Broad ($3.525M), Michael Bloomberg ($3.5M), Arthur Rock ($1M), Richard Riordan ($1M), Alice Walton ($750K)
- Villaraigosa finished third (13.3% of the vote, per Ballotpedia) behind Gavin Newsom and John Cox

**Donor continuity assessment:**
- Building trades labor: Continuous from Assembly through 2026
- Real estate developers: Continuous (Cordoba, TELACU, individual developers)
- Entertainment: Continuous (Seacrest, Reiner)
- Charter school billionaires: Major in 2018; largely migrated to Mahan for 2026
- Oil/fossil fuel: Present throughout career; now more explicit in 2026

## 12. CONTEXT + JOURNALIST-READY STORY ANGLES

### Angle 1: The No-Transfer Claim and What Cal-Access Actually Shows
**Pitch:** Villaraigosa has built his 2026 fundraising identity on the "no transfers, no self-funding" claim — calling it proof he leads in "direct donor support." But the campaign's own $6.3M figure is a press-release number [Tier 2 — antonio2026.com, Feb 2026]. TransparencyUSA's cycle-to-date data shows $3.18M in contributions and $3.9M in expenditures — his burn rate exceeds intake. By Q1 2026 (Jan–Apr 18), he raised only $707,000 while polling at 2–2.5% in public surveys. The "top fundraiser" framing is historically accurate (through early 2026) but is now overtaken by Mahan's $13M Q1 haul. Reporters should pull the Form 460 directly from Cal-Access (FPPC ID #1471635) to verify the no-transfer claim against any in-period transfers from prior committees.

### Angle 2: The Infrastructure Czar's Hidden Donors — and Whether They're Back
**Pitch:** In 2022–23, Newsom paid Villaraigosa $381,820 through a nonprofit (California Forward) funded by a dozen undisclosed corporate donors including SoCalGas ($17,500), Disney, AT&T, and Southern California Edison — all entities with direct stakes in state infrastructure policy. Villaraigosa now runs for governor on an infrastructure platform and has accepted campaign contributions from some of the same industry verticals (Chevron, CRC, utilities-adjacent donors). Did the California Forward donors, who paid to have Villaraigosa shape infrastructure policy in 2022–23, maintain relationships that translate into 2026 campaign support? A reporter should cross-reference California Forward's full donor list (obtainable from their IRS 990 or by request per CalMatters) against Villaraigosa's 2026 donor list.

### Angle 3: JRJ Corporation, Prenton Inc., and COPE Healthcare — Who Is Behind the LLC Money?
**Pitch:** Three of the largest institutional donors to Villaraigosa's 2026 campaign — JRJ Corporation ($78,400), Prenton Inc. (~$78,400), and COPE Healthcare Consulting Inc. ($78,400, both primary and general max) — are corporate entities with no publicly identifiable principals or business descriptions in the standard disclosure records. Each contributed at or near the maximum allowable level. Under California campaign finance rules, "other" entities (corporations, partnerships, LLCs) can make contributions up to the individual limit, but their beneficial owners are not separately disclosed. A FOIA/public records request for the entities' California Secretary of State registrations, combined with Form 460 schedules, could reveal the individuals behind this $234,000+ in contributions — a significant sum that should be traceable given California's corporation registration requirements.

# CROSS-CUTTING ANALYSIS

---

# CROSS-CUTTING DONOR ANALYSIS — 2026 California Governor's Race
*Compiled 2026-04-29 | Primary: June 2, 2026*
*All figures from individual dossiers; Tier-2 sources flagged inline. Cal-Access direct access was blocked (robots.txt) for all candidates — no cross-candidate comparison uses primary Cal-Access Form 460 data.*

---

## A. DONORS APPEARING ACROSS MULTIPLE CANDIDATES

The following entities appear in two or more dossiers' confirmed or reported donor lists.

### Cross-Party Institutional Blocs

**PORAC PAC (Peace Officers Research Association of California)**
The state's largest law enforcement organization (~86,000 members) made an extraordinary dual endorsement in August 2025, backing both Chad Bianco (R) and Antonio Villaraigosa (D) simultaneously — and contributed $39,200 to each campaign. [PORAC press release, Aug. 21, 2025](https://porac.org/wp-content/uploads/PORAC-2025-Gov-Endorsements_Press-Release.pdf) This is the clearest cross-party institutional hedge in the race: PORAC is guaranteeing law-enforcement influence no matter which of those two prevails. Notably, PORAC did not endorse Steve Hilton (R), leaving the other Republican without statewide LE institutional support.

**California Labor Federation (AFL-CIO umbrella)**
The Cal Fed issued a quadruple endorsement in March 2026, backing Steyer, Porter, Villaraigosa, and Swalwell (now suspended). [CA Labor Federation, Mar. 16, 2026](https://calaborfed.org/press-releases/california-federation-of-labor-unions-endorse-for-governor-and-other-statewide-races-for-2026-primary-election/) This did not equal an equal financial commitment — specific member-union PAC money has flowed unevenly — but it signals that organized labor's umbrella refuses to pick a single Democrat, fragmenting the labor vote. Critically, Thurmond and Becerra were both excluded.

**AltaMed Health Services Corp**
AltaMed ($39,200 to Becerra; $39,200 to Swalwell per cross-dossier reporting) is the most striking single-entity cross-candidate donor. [Becerra dossier, TransparencyUSA](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/committee/becerra-for-governor-2026-1480025-cao/contributors) AltaMed simultaneously donated $4.7M to a ballot committee opposing SEIU-UHW's proposition targeting FQHCs — creating a three-way tension: donor to two governor candidates, opponent of a union that endorses one of those candidates. [Tier 2 — needs Cal-Access primary verification for Swalwell amount]

**Chevron / Big Oil (Becerra + Villaraigosa)**
Chevron gave $39,200 to Becerra — its first gubernatorial contribution in over a decade — [Energy and Policy Institute, Apr. 29, 2026](https://energyandpolicy.org/becerra-150k-from-ca-utilities/) while Chevron Corporation and Its Subsidiaries gave $78,400 to Villaraigosa. [LA Times, May 26, 2025](https://www.latimes.com/politics/story/2025-05-26/oil-villaraigosa-fossil-fuel-governors-race) California Resources Corporation ($72,800 to Villaraigosa), Marathon Petroleum ($39,200 to Villaraigosa), and Berry Corporation ($39,200 to Villaraigosa) round out the oil-and-gas industry's bet on the two candidates it views as most friendly to the sector among Democrats. Steyer — whose platform calls for breaking up utility monopolies — is the target of $21M+ in anti-spending from PG&E and energy-allied interests. [FPPC June 2026 Primary list](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/)

**IBEW (electrical workers) across three candidates**
IBEW locals and affiliated entities appear in Thurmond (IBEW Local 302, $36,400), Villaraigosa (IBEW Local 11, $39,200), and as part of the anti-Steyer IE coalition (IBEW Local 1245, $75,000 to the Californians for Resilient & Affordable Energy committee). [JPR Apr. 2026](https://www.ijpr.org/politics-government/2026-04-27/billionaire-blitz-steyers-132-million-campaign-dwarfs-rivals-in-california-governor-race) Porter received $10,000 from IBEW in the 2022 federal cycle. [OpenSecrets career profile](https://www.opensecrets.org/members-of-congress/katie-porter/industries?cycle=CAREER&type=I) The building-trades IBEW locals are thus simultaneously funding anti-Steyer opposition and supporting multiple Democrats.

**Tribal gaming (Becerra + Thurmond)**
Pechanga Band of Indians gave $44,600 to Becerra; [TransparencyUSA](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/committee/becerra-for-governor-2026-1480025-cao/contributors) Habematolel Pomo of Upper Lake gave $36,400 to Thurmond; [TransparencyUSA Thurmond](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/candidate/tony-thurmond) Agua Caliente Band gave $41,900 to Becerra. Thurmond's SPI officeholder account also received from Mission Indians. Tribes are spreading money across multiple Democrats with no single dominant candidate, consistent with their interest in maximizing access to whoever becomes governor — since the governor negotiates gaming compacts under state law.

**Reed Hastings and William Oberndorf (charter-school billionaires, cross-cycle)**
Hastings ($7M) and Oberndorf ($3.75M) drove the 2018 Villaraigosa charter-school IE. [FPPC June 2018 Primary list](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2018-primary-election/) In 2026, both have migrated to Mahan: Hastings gave $1M to Mahan's Back to Basics IE; Oberndorf gave $843,000 to the same committee. [FPPC June 2026 Primary list](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/) The migration of charter-school billionaire money from Villaraigosa (2018) to Mahan (2026) is one of the most significant structural shifts in the field.

**Rob Reiner**
Rob Reiner donated $7,500 to Villaraigosa and $10,000 to Swalwell. [SomaliScan Villaraigosa donations](https://www.somaliscan.com/donations/recipient/Antonio%20Villaraigosa%20for%20Governor%202026); [NY Post Hollywood donors list](https://nypost.com/2026/01/31/us-news/hollywood-stars-donating-big-money-to-candidates-for-california-governor/) [Tier 2 — needs Cal-Access verification]

**Govern for California network**
The GfC network gave $1.5M (via Govern for California Action Committee) to Mahan's Back to Basics IE and $300,000 directly to Mahan for Governor. [FPPC June 2026 list](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/) The Govern for California Courage Committee (a GfC chapter) also gave $36,400 to Villaraigosa. [TransparencyUSA Villaraigosa](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/candidate/antonio-villaraigosa/contributors) GfC's multi-chapter structure — investigated by FPPC in 2024 and cleared — allows the network to spread money across candidates and IEs while managing individual contribution limits.

| **Law enforcement** | PORAC PAC ($39,200 Bianco + $39,200 Villaraigosa); RSA (Bianco primary financial engine); Santa Barbara DSA ($30K Bianco); San Diego DSA ($25K Bianco) | Bianco (dominant), Villaraigosa (PORAC) | No LE money to Porter, Mahan, Becerra, Steyer, Hilton |

| **Crypto** | Chris Larsen/Ripple ($39,200 each to Hilton + Porter); Fairshake $10M against Porter (Senate 2024); Villaraigosa on Coinbase advisory board | Hilton (Larsen), Porter (Larsen); crypto industry opposed Porter in 2024 | Crypto community split: Larsen hedging across parties; Coinbase/Andreessen spent against Porter federally |
| **Entertainment** | Ari Emanuel ($39,200 Swalwell); Rob Reiner ($10,000 Swalwell, $7,500 Villaraigosa); Ryan Seacrest ($72,800 Villaraigosa); Rupert Murdoch ($39,200 Hilton) | Swalwell (pre-suspension), Villaraigosa, Hilton | Industry split between Swalwell/Villaraigosa Hollywood Democrats and Murdoch/Fox Republican network |
| **Agribusiness** | Stewart Resnick/Wonderful Co. ($72,800 Villaraigosa); Chris Rufer/Morning Star ($25,000 Hilton) | Villaraigosa, Hilton | No agribusiness to Porter, Becerra, Mahan, Steyer, Bianco at documented level |
| **Finance/PE** | Michael Moritz ($78,400 + $3M IE Mahan); Brian Singerman/Founders Fund ($250,000 IE Mahan); Joe Green; various SV VCs | Mahan (dominant) | Steyer's Farallon network not contributing to other candidates |

## C. THE DARK-MONEY MAP

| Vehicle | Candidate Orbit | What's Known | What's Unknown |
|---------|----------------|--------------|----------------|
| **Back to Basics California** (501(c)(4)) | Mahan | Incorporated Mar. 2024 — 22 months before campaign launch. Jim Reed (Mahan's chief of staff) runs it. Fed into IE committee (FPPC 1487425) that raised $16.7M+. [San Jose Inside, Feb. 7, 2026](https://www.sanjoseinside.com/politics/bold-play-mahan-committee-drops-1-5-million-super-bowl-ad/) | Donors to the 501(c)(4) itself are not disclosed. No Form 990 found on ProPublica. Domain backtobasicssj.com registered Mar. 15, 2024 — who paid for this pre-campaign infrastructure? |
| **Golden Together** (501(c)(4)) | Hilton | Founded 2023 by Hilton; co-founders include Lanhee Chen, Gloria Romero (now his running mate), Kevin Faulconer. [Golden Together advisory board](https://goldentogether.com/advisory-board/) | No Form 990 located on ProPublica. Funders entirely undisclosed. Key question: were real estate or energy interests quietly funding Hilton's pre-campaign groundwork? |
| **NextGen Climate Action** (501(c)(4), EIN 46-1957345) | Steyer | $38.46M in contributions in 2024; total $255M+ since 2013. Steyer was dominant funder in early years. [ProPublica Nonprofit Explorer](https://projects.propublica.org/nonprofits/organizations/461957345) | Whether NextGen is currently spending for Steyer in the 2026 governor race is not confirmed. Kat Taylor (Steyer's wife) is board chair of NextGen Policy. |
| **Straight From the Heart of California** (IE #1486030) | Villaraigosa | ~$800,000 raised; Mike Trujillo associated. Filed Mar. 18, 2026. [Ballot Book committee page](https://theballotbook.com/campaign_finance/committees/20271/receipts) | Specific donors not itemized on website; Cal-Access Form 461 not retrieved. Described as "broad coalition" but principals not disclosed. |
| **"California's Best"** (entity) | Becerra | Listed as $39,200 contributor in Transparency USA. [TransparencyUSA Becerra](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/committee/becerra-for-governor-2026-1480025-cao/contributors) | Entity type (LLC, PAC, 501(c)(4)) unconfirmed. Beneficial owners unknown. |
| **JRJ Corporation / Prenton Inc.** (entities) | Villaraigosa | $78,400 each to Villaraigosa committee. [TransparencyUSA Villaraigosa](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/candidate/antonio-villaraigosa/contributors) | No publicly identifiable business description. Potentially shell-adjacent entities. CA SoS registration lookup required. |
| **RSA** (Riverside Sheriffs' Assoc., 501(c)(5)) | Bianco | Gave $575,000+ to Bianco's 2018 sheriff campaign; endorsing Bianco for governor April 15, 2026. [Idyllwild Town Crier, Apr. 2018](https://idyllwildtowncrier.com/2018/04/04/sheriffs-association-funding-bianco-campaign/) | 2026 governor-cycle IE spending not yet confirmed in Cal-Access Form 496 data. RSA's dual role as Bianco's employer (he manages their members) and primary funder is an inherent structural conflict. |
| **Govern for California (16 chapters)** | Mahan/Villaraigosa | FPPC cleared its multi-chapter structure in Jan. 2025. [CalMatters, Jan. 31, 2025](https://calmatters.org/politics/2025/01/california-political-donors/) | Each chapter's individual donors not separately disclosed in aggregated reporting. Nicholas Pritzker confirmed as top donor. David Crane manages the refund-guarantee fundraising structure. |

**[Tier 2 — needs primary verification]** notation applies to all "What's Unknown" cells above, as they rely on secondary sources or involve entities for which no primary disclosure document was retrieved.

## D. CROSS-PARTY HEDGERS

Three confirmed cross-party donors — giving simultaneously to at least one Democrat and one Republican — are documented in the dossiers:

| Donor | Republican Candidate | Amount | Democratic Candidate | Amount | Stated Rationale |
|-------|---------------------|--------|---------------------|--------|-----------------|
| **Sergey Brin** (Google co-founder) | Hilton | $39,200 | Mahan | $78,400 direct + $1M IE | Opposition to CA billionaire wealth tax; left CA for Nevada. [Bloomberg, Mar. 10, 2026](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-03-10/billionaire-brin-now-bets-on-a-republican-to-govern-california) |
| **Chris Larsen** (Ripple co-founder) | Hilton | $39,200 | Porter | $39,200 | Explicitly wants a Hilton-Porter November matchup; affordability focus. [Politico CA Playbook, Dec. 17, 2025](https://www.politico.com/newsletters/california-playbook/2025/12/17/meet-the-crypto-billionaire-hedging-his-bets-for-governor-00694484) |
| **Uber Technologies** | Hilton | $39,200 | Swalwell (IE, $2M) + Porter (~$150K) | $2M+/$150K | Classic corporate multi-candidate hedge covering rideshare regulatory exposure. [Washington Examiner, Mar. 24, 2026](https://www.washingtonexaminer.com/news/campaigns/state/4502369/uber-campaign-donations-california-governor/) |

All three were specifically called out in the Hilton dossier and verified against other dossiers. [Tier 2 — needs primary Cal-Access verification for Larsen-Porter and Uber-Porter amounts]

**The Brin-Larsen pattern** represents a new Silicon Valley political phenomenon: ultra-wealthy tech executives explicitly hedging across partisan lines, with policy interests (blocking the billionaire wealth tax; ensuring "affordability" regardless of party winner) rather than ideological loyalty driving contribution strategy. Brin's simultaneous $57M+ investment in anti-wealth-tax efforts through the California Business Roundtable ([Local News Matters, Apr. 3, 2026](https://localnewsmatters.org/2026/04/03/billionaire-blitz-silicon-valley-elites-funnel-millions-into-key-california-political-contests/)) frames both his Hilton and Mahan contributions as part of a unified tax-resistance portfolio.

**Stephen Cloobeck** warrants a separate flag: he dropped his own candidacy to back Swalwell, contributed $1M+ to Swalwell's IE, and post-suspension reportedly threatened to register Republican and endorse Hilton. [LA Times, Apr. 13, 2026](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-04-13/swalwell-supporters-scramble-after-he-drops-out-of-governors-race-who-benefits) If confirmed, this would add a fourth cross-party hedger. [Tier 2 — needs verification]

[NY Mag, Apr. 9, 2026](https://nymag.com/intelligencer/article/california-candidate-offers-donors-money-back-guarantee.html) |
