---

## F. WHERE DROPOUT MONEY WENT

Four candidates withdrew or suspended before the June 2 primary. The evidence on donor migration:

**Toni Atkins** (withdrew Sept. 2025, endorsed Steyer):
Atkins was the presumptive frontrunner with significant labor and progressive infrastructure behind her. Her endorsement of Steyer — and the subsequent CTA endorsement of Steyer — suggests that much of the organized labor energy that would have gone to Atkins migrated to Steyer. Specific donor-level migration is not documented from primary sources (Cal-Access blocked), but the pattern is consistent: Steyer picked up CTA and Our Revolution after Atkins exited. Betty Yee's withdrawal on Apr. 20, 2026 and immediate endorsement of Steyer reinforced this channel. [Yahoo/ABC10, Apr. 21, 2026](https://www.yahoo.com/news/articles/betty-yee-backs-tom-steyer-221932341.html)

**Stephen Cloobeck** (withdrew Nov. 2025, endorsed Swalwell, contributed $1M+ IE):
Cloobeck's money went entirely to Swalwell's IE infrastructure. Post-suspension, he sought refund of his $1M+ contribution and reportedly threatened to endorse Hilton. [LA Times, Apr. 13, 2026](https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2026-04-13/swalwell-supporters-scramble-after-he-drops-out-of-governors-race-who-benefits) Cloobeck money has no confirmed post-Swalwell landing as of 2026-04-29. [Tier 2]

**Eric Swalwell** (suspended Apr. 12, 2026 — still on ballot):
The Swalwell suspension is the most consequential donor-migration event of the primary. Key documented movements:
- **Tom Steyer** — Most immediate organized beneficiary: Rep. Huffman endorsed Steyer, CTA (which endorsed Swalwell) and other former Swalwell supporters moved to Steyer per multiple polling analyses. [CalMatters, Apr. 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/swalwell-congress-resignation/)
- **Katie Porter** — Porter's internal polling showed nearly half of Swalwell's supporters listed her as second choice; UC Berkeley IGS identified Porter and Steyer as top beneficiaries. [Tier 2 — CalMatters] Porter's profile overlap with Swalwell's base (older, more liberal, progressive) is the demographic bridge.
- **Xavier Becerra** — Polling showed a $400,000 donation surge post-suspension (1,659% engagement spike per [Scope Weekly, Apr. 15, 2026](https://www.scopeweekly.com/2026/04/becerra-surge-sparks-ktla-debate-fight-as-400k-fundraising-spike-shakes-california-governor-race/)).
- **Matt Mahan** — IE committee raised $12M+ in new commitments in days following Swalwell's exit, primarily from tech/VC institutional donors who were positioning for a Steyer-less or Swalwell-less field.
- **$4M Swalwell COH orphaned**: Swalwell installed himself as treasurer of his campaign committee (Apr. 24, 2026), giving him sole control over ~$4M remaining cash. Over 200 donors sought $1.5M+ in refunds. California law does not require refunds absent a court order. The $4M remains frozen in a suspended candidate's control. [SF Chronicle, Apr. 2026](https://www.sfchronicle.com/politics/article/eric-swalwell-donor-refunds-22228349.php)
- **SEIU $4M+ IE** (two committees) — Cannot be legally redirected to another candidate without a new IE committee structure. Both IE committees (1488732 and 1489873) list Swalwell as the target; any redeployment would require FPPC review. [FPPC June 2026 list](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/)

**Eleni Kounalakis** (running for State Treasurer — not a prior governor withdrawal in 2026, but relevant): No confirmed donor migration to 2026 governor candidates from Kounalakis's prior gubernatorial coalition.

---

## G. CANDIDATES RANKED BY FUNDRAISING

*All figures Tier 2 unless noted; primary Cal-Access sources universally blocked. Figures reflect most recent available reporting period (approximately April 18, 2026).*

| Candidate | Total Raised (approx.) | Cash on Hand | Top Single Source | Self-Funding % | Source |
|-----------|----------------------|-------------|------------------|---------------|--------|
| **Tom Steyer** | ~$144M | ~$12M (est.) | Thomas Steyer (self) | ~93%+ | [SF Chronicle tracker](https://www.sfchronicle.com/projects/2026/ca-governor-campaign-finance/); [CalMatters Apr. 24, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-race-financials/) |
| **Matt Mahan** | $13.5M (campaign) + ~$25M (IEs) ≈ $38.5M total ecosystem | $8.5M (campaign) + $6.5M (Back to Basics IE) | Michael Moritz ($3M IE) | ~0% self-funding; 100% outside donors | [San Jose Inside, Apr. 25, 2026](https://www.sanjoseinside.com/politics/as-election-draws-closer-mahan-continues-to-lead-in-fundraising/); [FPPC list](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/) |
| **Eric Swalwell** *(suspended)* | ~$8.7M (campaign) + $12.76M (IEs) ≈ $21.4M total | ~$4M (frozen) | Uber Innovation PAC ($2M IE) | 0% | [SF Chronicle tracker](https://www.sfchronicle.com/projects/2026/ca-governor-campaign-finance/); [FPPC list](https://www.fppc.ca.gov/search-filings/top-10-contributors-list/june-2026-primary-election/) |
| **Steve Hilton** | ~$9.5M total (cagovtracker) | ~$796K (one period per TransparencyUSA) | Aubrey Chernick / Joyce Chernick ($39,200 each) | ~2% (personal: $190,099) | [cagovtracker.com](https://cagovtracker.com/candidates/steve-hilton); [TransparencyUSA](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/committee/steve-hilton-for-governor-2026-1480425-cao/contributors) |
| **Katie Porter** | ~$9M total cycle | $3.75M+ | 100,000+ small-dollar donors (avg. $33) | 0% | [CalMatters Apr. 24, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-race-financials/); [Porter campaign release](https://katieporter.com/2026/04/katie-porter-campaign-reports-high-cash-on-hand-just-days-before-ballots-drop/) |
| **Villaraigosa** | ~$7.15M (cumulative Ballot Book) | ~$3.46M | State Building & Construction Trades Council ($78,400) | 0% | [Ballot Book](https://theballotbook.com/campaign_finance/committees/6700/receipts); [TransparencyUSA](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/committee/antonio-villaraigosa-for-governor-2026-1471635-ctl/donors) |
| **Becerra** | ~$5.23M (TransparencyUSA cumulative) | $507K (as of Apr. 18) | California State Council of Laborers PAC ($54,700) | 0% | [TransparencyUSA](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/race/governor-of-california); [CalMatters Apr. 24, 2026](https://calmatters.org/politics/2026/04/california-governor-race-financials/) |
| **Bianco** | ~$4.2M (through ~Dec. 2025) | ~$1.98M | Downs Energy / M&D Development (combined $156,800 — under FPPC review) | ~0.24% (self: $10K of $4.2M) | [TransparencyUSA](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/committee/bianco-for-governor-2026-1479095-cao); [SF Chronicle, Mar. 2026](https://www.sfchronicle.com/politics/article/contributions-bianco-violate-state-campaign-rules-22160676.php) |
| **Thurmond** | ~$1.37M (lifecycle) | ~$356K (Apr. 23, 2026) | Habematolel Pomo / IBEW Local 302 ($36,400 each) | 0% | [TransparencyUSA](https://www.transparencyusa.org/ca/candidate/tony-thurmond); [R. Pyers via Twitter, Apr. 23, 2026](https://x.com/rpyers/status/2047485785386127493) |

**Key observations:**
- Steyer's $144M dwarfs all others combined; his self-funding percentage approaches 93-100%.
- Mahan has the most financially powerful outside-money infrastructure ($25M+ in IEs).
- The two candidates with the most non-self-funded institutional depth — Mahan (tech/VC billionaires) and Swalwell (healthcare/SEIU) — represent structurally opposite donor coalitions.
- Porter is the only major candidate running entirely on small-dollar donors, consistent with her "no corporate PAC" brand.
- Thurmond and Becerra face existential cash constraints: Thurmond raised $62,000 in Q1 2026; Becerra has a 4x burn rate vs. income.

All dollar figures in this analysis are derived from the individual candidate dossiers compiled 2026-04-29 and are cited to their source URLs inline. # DATA GAPS — 2026 CA Governor Donor Intelligence
*Consolidated from all 9 candidate dossiers + cross-cutting analysis | As of 2026-04-29*

---

## SYSTEMIC CROSS-CUTTING GAPS

These gaps affect ALL candidates:

1. **Cal-Access direct portal universally blocked.** Every subagent attempting `https://cal-access.sos.ca.gov/Campaign/Candidates/list.aspx` and `https://cal-access.sos.ca.gov/Campaign/Committees/Detail.aspx?id=...` received a robots.txt disallow error. No Form 460 (Schedule A itemized contributions), Form 461 (independent expenditure filer), Form 496 (24-hour IE disclosure), or Form 497 (late contribution) data was retrieved directly from Cal-Access for any candidate. All financial data in all dossiers comes from Tier 2 aggregators (TransparencyUSA, The Ballot Book, cagovtracker.com, OpenSecrets, CalMatters) or FPPC-published top-10 contributor lists.

2. **Cal-Access NextGen / PowerSearch blocked.** `https://powersearch.sos.ca.gov/basic.php` returned HTTP 400. `https://powersearch.sos.ca.gov/advanced.php` returned only a form UI with no results. No candidate or committee searches succeeded.

3. **FPPC enforcement database not directly queried.** `https://www.fppc.ca.gov/enforcement/enforcement-actions.html` returned HTTP 4xx or was blocked in all research sessions. Enforcement status for all candidates is based on press reporting and secondary sources only, not primary FPPC database search.

4. **Treasurer names absent for most committees.** Cal-Access Form 410 (Statement of Organization) was not retrievable for any 2026 governor committee. Treasurer names confirmed from primary source for ONLY Mahan for Governor 2026 (Ted Trujillo) and Porter's federal committees (Alexander Warren).

5. **Individual donor itemized lists unavailable.** Without Cal-Access Form 460 Schedule A access, no cross-candidate individual donor cross-reference was possible from primary sources. The donor_overlaps.csv relies on Tier 2 sources for most individual donor-candidate pairs.

6. **FPPC 2025-26 contribution limit discrepancy unresolved.** SHARED_CONTEXT cites $36,400/election; filings show contributors at $39,200 and $78,400 (suggesting primary+general). Current FPPC-adjusted limit for 2025-26 gubernatorial cycle not independently confirmed from `fppc.ca.gov`.

7. **No Form 496 (24-hour late IE) data retrieved.** IE spending close to the primary (April-May 2026) is likely underreported in all dossiers.

---

## CROSS-CUTTING GAPS IDENTIFIED IN THIS ANALYSIS

1. **No donor cross-reference from primary Cal-Access data.** The donor_overlaps.csv relies entirely on Tier 2 sources. Any cross-candidate giving patterns not captured in press coverage or FPPC top-10 lists are invisible. A systematic Cal-Access bulk data download (available at `https://github.com/california-civic-data-coalition/django-calaccess-raw-data`) would enable primary-source cross-referencing.

2. **AltaMed dual role (Becerra + Swalwell donor, anti-SEIU ballot committee funder) — amounts to Swalwell not independently verified** from a Tier 1 source; cross-dossier confirmation needed.

3. **Atkins/Yee/Cloobeck/Kounalakis dropout donor migration.** Specific individual donor moves from these withdrawn candidates to active candidates are not captured in itemized filings (Cal-Access blocked). Only endorsement-level signals and polling data confirm migration patterns.

4. **SEIU post-Swalwell money.** SEIU California ($4M in IEs for Swalwell) has not confirmed any redeployment of IE committee funds post-suspension. Whether the orphaned IE committees (1488732, 1489873) can legally redirect funds to other candidates requires legal analysis — a gap this research did not resolve.

5. **Becerra's "post-Swalwell surge" of ~$400K** — described in press but not verified against Cal-Access F497 filings.

6. **FPPC June 2026 Primary top-10 list completeness.** The list is updated intermittently; the version reviewed may not reflect April 28-June 2 activity.

7. **Dark money (501(c)(4)) cross-comparisons.** Golden Together (Hilton), Back to Basics California (Mahan), and NextGen Climate Action (Steyer) are all 501(c)(4)s not required to disclose donors. None had retrievable Form 990s for the 2025-26 period. No cross-organization donor overlap analysis is possible.

8. **Villaraigosa Coinbase advisory relationship and 2026 crypto donations.** Villaraigosa joined Coinbase's advisory council in April 2024. Chris Larsen (Ripple co-founder) gave to both Porter and Hilton but no confirmed Villaraigosa 2026 crypto donation identified. The Coinbase advisory role warrants follow-up given crypto's heavy involvement in CA electoral politics via Fairshake.

9. **Mercury/Actum client list vs. Villaraigosa 2026 donors.** Mercury and Actum clients (charter schools, Westlands Water, utilities) who may now be 2026 donors cannot be verified without full itemized Cal-Access data.

10. **CCPOA (prison guard union) alignment with Bianco vs. anti-Steyer IE participation.** CCPOA gave $25,000 to the anti-Steyer IE but no confirmed direct Bianco contribution. Whether CCPOA is coordinating with the Bianco campaign through non-disclosed channels requires primary source review.


---

# COMPANION DATA FILES

The following structured CSVs accompany this report:

- `committees.csv` — every campaign / IE / 501(c)(4) committee mentioned across the dossiers (state, federal, dark-money), with IDs, treasurers, status, and source URLs.
- `donor_overlaps.csv` — every individual / PAC / corporation / LLC / union / tribe appearing in 2+ candidate dossiers, with amounts to each candidate and source URLs.
- `independent_expenditures.csv` — every IE committee active in the 2026 cycle (and historically significant 2018/2024 IEs), with totals and top funders one level up.
- `data_gaps.md` — consolidated list of every unfindable / unverifiable item, organized by candidate, with the URL attempted.
